\section{Introduction}

\subsection{Local measurements, constraints, and brackets}

The object of study is a local constrained mechanical system. Fix a defect
world-line $\R\times p$ inside the $1+4$-real-dimensional space-time
$\R^2\times\C^2$. The transverse data is a single real line of
\emph{topological time} (the $\R^2$ factor), and a formal holomorphic
symplectic disk
$$(z_1,z_2),\qquad \omega=dz_1\wedge dz_2,$$
the formal neighbourhood of $p\in\C^2$. The defect is a \emph{point in $\C^2$,
dragged along $\R$}; nothing else has been postulated.

The two normal coordinates $z_1,z_2$ describe the position of the defect
inside the symplectic disk. A stack of $N$ identical probes at the defect
represents each coordinate by an $N\times N$ matrix:
$$z_1\rightsquigarrow\phi_1,\qquad z_2\rightsquigarrow\phi_2,
  \qquad\phi_i\in\lie{gl}_N.$$
The symplectic form pulls back to the matrix-valued two-form
$\Omega_N=\mathrm{Tr}(d\phi_1\wedge d\phi_2)$, and the symplectic potential
along the world-line is
$$\theta_N=\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2).$$
Acting on a probe stack by an internal change of basis is a gauge operation.
The gauge generator is the $\lie{gl}_N$-valued moment map
$$\mu_\epsilon=-\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\epsilon[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr),\qquad
  \epsilon\in\lie{gl}_N,$$
and demanding gauge-invariance of the world-line dynamics imposes the
\emph{first-class constraint}
$$[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0.$$
The Lagrange multiplier for this constraint is a connection
$A\in\Omega^1(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N$. The boundary action is therefore
\emph{not chosen}; it is the unique first-order action carrying the
symplectic potential and enforcing the first-class constraint:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:open-action-derived}
S_\partial
  =\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2+A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr).
\end{equation}
This is the Dirac standard. The ``open string field theory on $\R\times p$''
is the canonical mechanics of an $N$-probe stack on the formal symplectic
normal disk, with the matrix moment-map equation as its first-class
constraint. Lemma~\ref{lem:dirac-probe-reduction} records the precise
constrained-mechanics statement and identifies $A$ as the multiplier.

The BV reduction of this constrained system is an algebraic step. The
constraint is recorded as a Koszul differential by a single odd matrix
antifield $\psi=A^*\in\lie{gl}_N[1]$ with
\begin{equation}\label{eq:open-Q}
Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2],\qquad Q\phi_1=Q\phi_2=0.
\end{equation}
The reduced local polynomial algebra at a brane point is
$$\mathcal R_N
  =\C[\phi_1{}^i{}_j,\phi_2{}^i{}_j]
   \otimes\Lambda(\psi^i{}_j),$$
and $H^0(\mathcal R_N^{GL_N},Q)$ is, by definition, the algebra of
$GL_N$-invariant local observables on the Dirac-reduced phase space of
commuting matrix pairs. This algebra is the open trace algebra of the defect;
it is what one is forced to write down once the probe stack and the constraint
have been named. The full BV master action is the canonical lift of
\eqref{eq:open-action-derived} to ghost-number-zero fields; this lift is
recorded in Lemma~\ref{lem:open-action-reduction} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:open-bv-truncation}.

\subsection{The Hamiltonian Lie algebra of the symplectic disk}

The corresponding closed system is dictated by the same canonical mechanics.
A closed infinitesimal symmetry of the formal symplectic disk is a
Hamiltonian vector field $X_f=\{f,-\}$. Constants act trivially: $X_c=0$ for
$c\in\C$. The closed Hamiltonian Lie algebra is therefore the formal power
series modulo constants,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hbar-Lie-algebra}
\bar A=\C[z_1,z_2]/\C\cdot1,\qquad
\widehat{\mathfrak h}=\C[[z_1,z_2]]/\C\cdot1,
\end{equation}
with bracket
$$\{f,g\}=\partial_{z_1}f\,\partial_{z_2}g
  -\partial_{z_2}f\,\partial_{z_1}g\pmod{\C}.$$
Polynomial calculations use $\bar A$; closed
Chevalley--Eilenberg/Koszul calculations use the completed
$\widehat{\mathfrak h}$. Continuous duality on $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$
produces $\mathfrak h^\vee=\widehat{\mathfrak h}^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}$, with
the Taylor-monomial basis $\delta_{k,l}$ for $k+l>0$. We use
$\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}$ for an abstract copy of $\bar A$ whose nonconstant
basis vectors are represented on the brane by the first descendant cycles
$\Psi_{k,l}$ (Construction~\ref{constr:boundary-evaluation}).

\begin{rmk}[Scalar Hamiltonian and center-of-mass term]\label{rmk:scalar-hamiltonian-center-of-mass}
  The quotient by constants is load-bearing. In the reduced Hamiltonian
  algebra of the formal disk,
  $$\{z_1,z_2\}=1\equiv0\quad\text{in }\bar A.$$
  On the unreduced brane phase space, however,
  $$\{\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1),\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_2)\}=N.$$
  This is the center-of-mass symplectic pair of the stack. Every bracket
  statement below involving linear Hamiltonians is therefore a statement after
  projection to the Hamiltonian quotient by scalar trace classes. The same
  term reappears quantum mechanically as the Capelli shift in
  Remark~\ref{rmk:normal-ordering-obstruction}.
\end{rmk}

The closed canonical theory must promote $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$ to a local
field theory whose phase space is the cotangent of the Hamiltonian-deformation
moduli; the cotangent of canonical transformations is the unique covariant
choice. This is what BCOV \cite{bcov} prescribes for the closed B-model on a
Calabi--Yau, with the polyvector cotangent realised by the divergence
operator. On a holomorphic-symplectic surface the local cotangent theory is
the Hamiltonian BF theory for the Tate Lie algebra
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cotangent-Lie-algebra}
\mathfrak g=\widehat{\mathfrak h}\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee[1],
\end{equation}
where the shift $[1]$ records the BV degree of the cotangent field and the
Lie bracket on $\mathfrak g$ is the semi-direct sum of the Hamiltonian
bracket on $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$ with the coadjoint action on
$\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$.

The closed local observables are the continuous Chevalley--Eilenberg
cochains
$$\mathcal{O}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{grav}}
  =C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)
  =\widehat{\mathbf S}\bigl(\mathfrak g^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[-1]\bigr),$$
and their Koszul dual is the completed graded enveloping algebra
$$\bigl(\mathcal{O}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{grav}}\bigr)^!
  \simeq\widehat{U(\mathfrak g)}.$$
The PBW Rees algebra $U_\hbar(\mathfrak g)$ has completed special fibre
\begin{equation}\label{eq:PBW-special-fibre}
U_\hbar(\mathfrak g)/(\hbar)
  \cong\widehat{\mathbf S}\bigl(\widehat{\mathfrak h}
    \oplus\mathfrak h^\vee[1]\bigr).
\end{equation}
The structural content of \eqref{eq:cotangent-Lie-algebra}--%
\eqref{eq:PBW-special-fibre} is that the closed sector \emph{is the shifted
cotangent theory of canonical transformations of the disk};
Proposition~\ref{prop:hamiltonian-polyvector-reduction} below derives
$\widehat{\mathfrak h}$ from divergence-closed polyvectors on the formal disk.

\subsection{Closed-open measurement and the derived Poisson centre}

A closed Hamiltonian $f(z_1,z_2)$ is \emph{measured} by the brane by
substitution of the matrix-valued normal coordinates:
$$J(f)=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}.$$
At finite $N$ one chooses a word ordering. In $H^0(\mathcal R_N^{GL_N},Q)$
adjacent swaps are exact,
$Q\,\mathrm{Tr}(\psi vu)=\mathrm{Tr}([\phi_1,\phi_2]vu)$, so the ordering
ambiguity disappears modulo the constraint. In the stable connected limit
$N\to\infty$, $J(f)$ is a well-defined Hamiltonian observable on the brane.
The matrix Poisson bracket gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:open-bracket}
\bigl\{J(f),J(g)\bigr\}_\partial=J\bigl(\{f,g\}_{\mathfrak h}\bigr),
\end{equation}
after removal of the scalar Hamiltonian. Equation~\eqref{eq:open-bracket} is
the ordinary canonical bracket of the probe system: it is not a string-theoretic
input; it is the statement that the probe brane is a representation of the
Hamiltonian Lie algebra of the disk. On monomials,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bracket-coefficient}
\bigl\{\overline{\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1^k\phi_2^l)},
       \overline{\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1^m\phi_2^n)}\bigr\}
  =\overline{(kn-lm)\,\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1^{k+m-1}\phi_2^{l+n-1})}.
\end{equation}

The map $f\mapsto J(f)$ is the \emph{moment-map shadow} of the full
closed-open operation. The full operation cannot be a single function on the
open algebra: a closed local field that lives in a region of space-time near
the brane should produce \emph{a central operation on all open factorisation
observables}, not merely an element. The correct target is therefore the
derived Poisson centre
$$Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{open}}).$$
The structural form of this identification is the content of
Theorem~\ref{thm:reduced-derived-poisson-center} below: the closed
Chevalley--Eilenberg cochains on $\mathfrak g$ identify with the reduced
derived $P_0$-Poisson centre of the stable open Hamiltonian algebra, and the
boundary observable $J(f)=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$ is the
image, under that identification, of the coordinate dual to the shifted
cotangent generator (\emph{not} of the coordinate dual to $f$ itself); the
closed Hamiltonian ghost becomes the Hamiltonian vector-field operation on
the brane.

\subsection{Scalar reduction and the U(1) center anomaly}\label{subsec:scalar-anomaly}

Throughout this manuscript constants in $\C[z_1,z_2]$ and the finite-rank
scalar trace $\mathrm{Tr}(1)=N$ are removed before the bracket is recorded.
This convention has algebraic content. The class of the removed cocycle is
the U(1) center anomaly: the unique nontrivial class
$[c]\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\mathfrak h, \C)$ obstructing the lift of the
scalar-reduced Hamiltonian Poisson bracket to the unreduced bracket on
$\C[z_1,z_2]$ on the closed side, and the unique obstruction to lifting the
trace algebra Lie bracket to $\lie{gl}_N$ rather than to its quotient
$\mathfrak{sl}_N\oplus\C\cdot I$ on the open side. Theorem~\ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly}
makes this precise; Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-classical-anomaly} identifies the
same class with the Moyal/Capelli $\hbar N$ shift on the brane. The flag
``before/after killing the scalar'' is propagated explicitly through every
later theorem statement that touches $\mathfrak h$ or
$\mathcal A_{\partial}$.

\paragraph{Notation.} Write $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}=\C[z_1,z_2]_+$ for
the polynomial Hamiltonian Lie algebra without the constant subalgebra
removed; the bracket on $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ is
$\{f,g\}=\partial_{z_1}f\,\partial_{z_2}g-\partial_{z_2}f\,\partial_{z_1}g$ and
takes values in $\C[z_1,z_2]_+\oplus\C\cdot 1$. Define
$$\omega:\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}\otimes\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}
  \longrightarrow\C,\qquad
  \omega(f,g)=[\,\{f,g\}\,]_0,$$
the constant Taylor coefficient of $\{f,g\}$. On monomials,
$$\omega(z_1^kz_2^l,z_1^mz_2^n)=
  \begin{cases}
    kn-lm, & (k+m,l+n)=(1,1),\\
    0, & \text{otherwise},
  \end{cases}$$
hence $\omega$ is concentrated in the unique bidegree where the bracket
multidegree $(k+m-1,l+n-1)$ is $(0,0)$; this is exactly the bidegree the
manuscript discards as ``scalar trace''.

\begin{lem}\label{lem:omega-cocycle}
  $\omega$ is a Lie 2-cocycle on $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$, and its
  cohomology class
  $$[c]:=[\omega]\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}},\C)$$
  is nontrivial. After projection to $\bar A=\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}/\C$,
  the same formula represents a nontrivial class
  $[\bar c]\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  The Jacobi identity for $\{-,-\}$ on $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ asserts
  $$\{f,\{g,h\}\}+\{g,\{h,f\}\}+\{h,\{f,g\}\}=0,$$
  and projecting each summand to its constant Taylor coefficient gives the
  cocycle identity
  $$\omega(f,\{g,h\})+\omega(g,\{h,f\})+\omega(h,\{f,g\})=0.$$
  Antisymmetry $\omega(g,f)=-\omega(f,g)$ is inherited from antisymmetry of
  the bracket. Hence $\omega\in Z^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}},\C)$.
  Suppose $\omega=\delta\eta$ for some linear $\eta:\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}\to\C$.
  Then $\omega(f,g)=-\eta(\{f,g\})$. Test on $f=z_1$, $g=z_2$:
  $\omega(z_1,z_2)=1$ while $\{z_1,z_2\}=1$, so
  $\eta(1)=-1$. But $z_1\cdot 1$ and $1\cdot z_1$ both bracket to zero with
  any $g\in\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ except via the same calculation, so
  the system $\eta(\{f,g\})=-\omega(f,g)$ overdetermines $\eta$: testing on
  $f=z_1^2,g=z_2$ gives $\eta(2z_1)=0$, hence $\eta$ vanishes on
  $z_1\C[z_1,z_2]_+$, contradicting $\eta(1)=-1$. Therefore
  $[\omega]\neq 0\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}},\C)$.
  The same argument descends to $\bar A=\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}/\C$, since
  $\omega$ vanishes on the line $\C\cdot 1$ already, so it descends to a
  cocycle on the quotient and remains nontrivial.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}[U(1) center anomaly: closed side]\label{thm:u1-center-anomaly}
  The class $[\bar c]\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$ of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:omega-cocycle} is the unique obstruction class to lifting
  the Lie algebra structure on $\bar A$ to a Lie algebra structure on the
  unreduced polynomial Hamiltonians $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ along the
  abelian extension
  $$0\longrightarrow \C\cdot 1\longrightarrow \mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}
    \longrightarrow \bar A\longrightarrow 0.$$
  Equivalently, $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ is isomorphic to the central
  extension $\bar A_{[\bar c]}=\bar A\oplus\C K$ with bracket
  $$[\,(f,aK),(g,bK)\,]=(\{f,g\}_{\bar A},\,\bar c(f,g)\,K),$$
  and $[\bar c]$ generates a one-dimensional sub-line of
  $H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$ that is the obstruction.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  Central extensions of $\bar A$ by $\C$ are classified by
  $H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$ via the standard Chevalley-Eilenberg
  argument. The exact sequence above is a central extension because the
  constant Hamiltonian $1\in\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ has zero Hamiltonian
  vector field, so $\C\cdot 1$ is central in
  $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$. The class of this extension is the obstruction
  to a Lie-algebra splitting; computing the class on monomial generators,
  $$[z_1^kz_2^l,z_1^mz_2^n]_{\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}}
    =\{z_1^kz_2^l,z_1^mz_2^n\}=
    (kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1},$$
  and projecting to $\C\cdot 1$ keeps only the $(0,0)$-Taylor coefficient
  $\omega$ of Lemma~\ref{lem:omega-cocycle}. Thus the extension class is
  $[\bar c]$, and Lemma~\ref{lem:omega-cocycle} shows it is nontrivial. The
  same lemma shows the line $\C\cdot[\bar c]$ is one-dimensional inside
  $H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$, and that splitting along this line
  recovers $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}[U(1) center anomaly: open side]\label{thm:u1-center-anomaly-open}
  At finite $N$ the trace algebra Lie bracket
  $\{F,G\}=\mathrm{Tr}(\partial_{\phi_1}F\,\partial_{\phi_2}G
  -\partial_{\phi_2}F\,\partial_{\phi_1}G)$ on
  $\C[\lie{gl}_N\oplus\lie{gl}_N]^{GL_N}$ satisfies
  $$\{\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1,\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_2\}=N$$
  in the unreduced ring, and zero in the scalar-reduced quotient
  $H^0_{\mathrm{red}}=H^0/\C\cdot\mathrm{Tr}(1)$. The cohomology class of this
  central scalar in $H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}$ of the unreduced trace algebra is
  the image of $[\bar c]$ under the boundary evaluation map
  $$\partial_{\mathrm{bb},N}^{\mathrm{full}}:\C[z_1,z_2]\longrightarrow
    \C[\lie{gl}_N^2]^{GL_N},\qquad
    f\longmapsto \mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2),$$
  i.e.\ the same anomaly class is realised on the brane as the U(1) center
  of $\lie{gl}_N$ with central element $I$.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  The matrix Poisson bracket gives, on monomials of bidegree $(1,0)$ and
  $(0,1)$,
  $$\{\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1,\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_2\}
    =\mathrm{Tr}\bigl((\partial_{\phi_1}\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1)
      (\partial_{\phi_2}\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_2)
      -(\partial_{\phi_2}\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1)
      (\partial_{\phi_1}\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_2)\bigr)
    =\mathrm{Tr}(I\cdot I)-0=N.$$
  Hence the unreduced bracket realises the constant $N$ as a scalar element.
  In $H^0_{\mathrm{red}}=H^0/\C\cdot\mathrm{Tr}(1)$ this scalar is killed,
  matching the projection on the closed side. The boundary evaluation map
  $\partial_{\mathrm{bb},N}^{\mathrm{full}}$ sends $1\in\C[z_1,z_2]$ to
  $\mathrm{Tr}(I)=N$ and satisfies, for monomials with $(k+m,l+n)=(1,1)$,
  $$\partial_{\mathrm{bb},N}^{\mathrm{full}}(\{z_1^kz_2^l,z_1^mz_2^n\})
    =(kn-lm)\cdot\mathrm{Tr}(I)
    =(kn-lm)\cdot N\cdot I,$$
  which equates the closed cocycle $\omega$ with the open trace bracket on
  the central direction. Hence the extension class on the brane is the
  image of $[\bar c]$. Since $\C\cdot I\subset\lie{gl}_N$ is the U(1) centre
  with character $\mathrm{Tr}$, the brane realisation of $[\bar c]$ is
  exactly the U(1) centre of $\lie{gl}_N$.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}\label{rmk:quotient-discipline-flag}
  Every theorem in this manuscript that uses $\mathfrak h$, $\bar A$, or
  $\mathcal A_{\partial}=H^0_{\mathrm{red}}$ lives \emph{after} killing the
  scalar. The unreduced statement requires keeping the central line
  $\C\cdot 1\subset\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ on the closed side and
  $\C\cdot\mathrm{Tr}(1)$ on the open side, with the U(1) center anomaly
  class $[\bar c]$ recording the obstruction to a Lie-algebra splitting.
  Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}, Theorem~\ref{thm:bulk-boundary},
  Corollary~\ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling}, and
  Proposition~\ref{prop:first-order-bracket} are all stated on the reduced
  side; their unreduced refinements are governed by $[\bar c]$ via the
  central extensions of Theorems~\ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly}
  and~\ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly-open}.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection*{Quantum-classical equivalence of the U(1) center cocycle}

\begin{thm}[Quantum-classical equivalence of the U(1) center class]\label{thm:quantum-classical-anomaly}
  Let $\Phi=(\phi_1,\phi_2)$ be the classical brane field on the formal
  local disk and $\Phi_\hbar=(\phi_1^{\hbar},\phi_2^{\hbar})$ its Weyl
  quantization at finite $N$, with the Moyal product
  $f*g=m\circ\exp\bigl(\tfrac{\hbar}{2}P\bigr)(f\otimes g)$ for
  $P=\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}-\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1}$.
  Then on the brane the quantization satisfies the Capelli/canonical
  commutator identity
  $$Y_{\hbar}X_{\hbar}-X_{\hbar}Y_{\hbar}+\hbar N I=0,\qquad
    X_{\hbar}=\phi_1^{\hbar},\ Y_{\hbar}=\phi_2^{\hbar},$$
  which evaluates to $\{\phi_2,\phi_1\}=-\delta=N$ on the trace generators
  $X=\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1$, $Y=\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_2$.
  In the classical limit $\hbar\to 0$, the bracket
  $\{\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1,\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_2\}=N$ recovers the central scalar
  of Theorem~\ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly-open}.
  The classical Poisson cocycle $\omega$ of Lemma~\ref{lem:omega-cocycle}
  and the quantum Capelli shift $\hbar N$ represent the \emph{same
  cohomology class} $[\bar c]\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$ under
  classical-to-quantum reduction, i.e.\ via the Rees deformation
  $U_{\hbar}(\bar A_{[\bar c]})$ specialising to
  $\widehat{\mathbf S}(\bar A_{[\bar c]})$ at $\hbar=0$.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  The Weyl convention gives $[X_{\hbar},Y_{\hbar}]_*=\hbar\{X,Y\}+O(\hbar^3)$.
  On the trace generators, Proposition~\ref{prop:first-order-bracket} at
  $(k,l,m,n)=(1,0,0,1)$ gives $\{X,Y\}=N$ before scalar reduction. Hence
  $$X_{\hbar}Y_{\hbar}-Y_{\hbar}X_{\hbar}=\hbar N+O(\hbar^3),$$
  and at finite $N$ the higher-order terms vanish on these linear generators
  because $P^r$ requires at least $r$ derivatives in each tensor factor.
  Rearranging gives the displayed Capelli/canonical identity. This is the
  classical-to-quantum reduction in the sense of Razmyslov~\cite{razmyslov}
  and Procesi~\cite{procesi}: the trace identities of $\lie{gl}_N$ at level
  $N$ are exactly the Capelli identities~\cites{capelli,howe-capelli}, and
  the abelian Capelli at $r=1$ is the canonical-commutator shift.

  For the cohomology-class identification, observe that the Rees algebra
  $U_{\hbar}(\bar A_{[\bar c]})$ has central fibre
  $\widehat{\mathbf S}(\bar A_{[\bar c]})$ at $\hbar=0$ and generic fibre
  containing $\bar A_{[\bar c]}$ as Lie algebra at $\hbar=1$. The
  PBW filtration's associated graded carries the Lie 2-cocycle as the
  primary obstruction to PBW-splitting the deformation. Both sides of the
  classical-to-quantum reduction therefore record the same class in
  $H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C)$: classically $\omega$ is the obstruction
  to splitting the central extension $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}\to\bar A$,
  quantum-mechanically the same $\omega$ is the leading-order coefficient
  of the Moyal star commutator on the central direction.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  The class $[\bar c]$ is therefore a physical observable of the brane:
  the U(1) center of $\lie{gl}_N$ acts on the brane Hilbert space with
  character $\mathrm{Tr}$, and the canonical/Capelli shift $\hbar N$ is the
  charge of this central direction. The scalar reduction in the body of the
  manuscript is the operation of restricting to the kernel of this
  character; it is not a vacuous bookkeeping step.
\end{rmk}

\subsection{The two algebras}

The local model contains two algebras, both \emph{derived} from the
canonical mechanics above rather than postulated:
\begin{itemize}
  \item The algebra $\mc{A}_N$ of $GL_N$-invariant local trace observables
    on the Dirac-reduced probe stack of \eqref{eq:open-action-derived};
    equivalently, the algebra of local operators of the open BV theory on
    the brane line $\R\times p$.
  \item The algebra $\mc{B}$ of local operators of the closed Hamiltonian
    BF sector \eqref{eq:cotangent-Lie-algebra}; the operator-product
    expansion in the $\R$-direction equips $\mc{B}$ with an associative
    product, derived from the locally constant factorisation structure of
    the topological direction.
\end{itemize}

\begin{conj}[Stable bulk--boundary Koszul duality]\label{conj:An-Koszul}
  In the stable large-$N$ limit and within the Hamiltonian sector,
  $$\lim_{N\to\infty}\mc A_N\ \simeq\ \mc B^!,$$
  the Koszul dual of $\mc B$. Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local} is the classical
  Hamiltonian shadow of this conjecture; the quantum refinement is the
  formal Weyl/Moyal target of \S\ref{ssec:quantum-target} below.
\end{conj}

This recovers the open/closed string duality of \cite{witten-cs}, but here
it is no longer a string-theoretic ansatz: it is the statement that the
closed local theory is the derived Poisson centre of the open local theory.

The provenance of this local model in higher-dimensional physics is
twisted M-theory. The following conjecture states, in precise form, the
universality claim that the formal local construction here is the
Hamiltonian-sector restriction of every twisted M-theory background of
the indicated type.

\begin{conj}[Twisted-M-theory universality of the local model]\label{conj:twisted-m-theory-universal}
  Let $X$ be a holomorphic-symplectic surface and let
  $\mathcal{T}_{\mathrm{tw}M}\bigl(\R\times X;\R\times p\bigr)$ denote the
  perturbative twisted M-theory data on $\R\times X$ in the presence of a
  stack of $N$ one-dimensional topological branes supported on $\R\times p$,
  in the sense of the twisted holomorphic-topological theory
  \cite{costello-twistedM} whose protected sector restricts to the local
  Hamiltonian sector here. Hypotheses:
  (i) the BV-cohomology vanishing of \cites{costello-li-quantum-bcov,
  costello-li-open-closed-bcov} on the formal local model;
  (ii) the Costello locality theorem ensuring that restriction to a formal
  neighbourhood of $\R\times p$ is well-defined;
  (iii) the Hamiltonian reduction of the holomorphic-symplectic data to the
  formal symplectic disk at $p$ is regular.
  Then the Hamiltonian-sector restriction
  $$\mathcal{T}_{\mathrm{tw}M}\bigl(\R\times X;\R\times p\bigr)
    \big|_{\mathrm{Ham},\widehat{p}}$$
  is canonically equivalent, as a pair (open BV theory; closed Hamiltonian
  BF theory together with open trace data), to the formal local model
  constructed in this manuscript: open side
  $\bigl(\Omega^*(\R)\otimes\Lambda(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2)
  \otimes\lie{gl}_N[1],\,S(\alpha)\bigr)$, closed side
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE,cont}}(\mathfrak g)$ with
  $\mathfrak g=\widehat{\mathfrak h}\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$, and
  bulk-to-boundary evaluation
  $f\mapsto\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$. In particular every
  such twisted M-theory restriction satisfies Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}.
\end{conj}

\begin{rmk}
  Conjecture~\ref{conj:twisted-m-theory-universal} replaces the BCOV analogy
  as the primary physical motivation. The original BCOV analysis is written
  for Calabi--Yau threefolds (\cite{bcov}), where the target dimension is
  $d=3$; the local model here is a holomorphic-symplectic surface ($d=2$)
  and is therefore not a reduction of BCOV in any direct sense. The
  Hamiltonian BF formulation \eqref{eq:cotangent-Lie-algebra} is the
  correct primary physical name. The deciding evidence for the conjecture
  is (a) the explicit BV-cohomology computation of
  \cites{costello-li-quantum-bcov,costello-li-open-closed-bcov};
  (b) a reduction lemma for protected twisted-M-theory operators on
  $\R\times X$ to the formal disk at $p$; (c) compatibility with the
  scalar/center-of-mass anomaly term of
  Remark~\ref{rmk:scalar-hamiltonian-center-of-mass}.
\end{rmk}

\subsection{Three notions of locality}

Locality is not one notion in this model. It is three.

\paragraph{(a) Support locality along the brane.}
For an open interval $I\subset\R$ on the world-line, define the compactly
supported Hamiltonian current algebra
$\mathfrak h_I=C^\infty_c(I)\otimes\widehat{\mathfrak h}$ with bracket
$$[a\otimes f,\,b\otimes g]=ab\otimes\{f,g\}_{\widehat{\mathfrak h}}.$$
The open observables on $I$ are
$\mathcal A_\partial(I)=\mathbf S(\mathfrak h_I)$, generated by the smeared
trace functionals
$$O_f(a)=\int_I a(t)\,\mathrm{Tr}\,f\bigl(\phi_1(t),\phi_2(t)\bigr)\,dt.$$
Their bracket is the canonical equal-time bracket:
$$\bigl\{O_f(a),O_g(b)\bigr\}=O_{\{f,g\}_{\widehat{\mathfrak h}}}(ab).$$
Disjoint supports multiply, since $ab=0$ outside the intersection;
overlapping supports give a delta-function contact term. This is the
operational meaning of locality for the open factorisation algebra:
disjoint independent measurements multiply, and Poisson brackets are
supported where the measurements meet.

\paragraph{(b) Topological locality.}
In the topological direction (the $\R^2$ factor), translations are
$Q$-exact:
$$L_v=[Q,\iota_v].$$
Equivalently, positive jets in the topological direction vanish in
local-operator cohomology by the contraction homotopy
$[d_\R,\iota_{\partial_t}]=\partial_t$
(Lemma~\ref{lem:derivative-jets}). Therefore the precise position of an
insertion is not physical; only the collision pattern of insertions matters.
This is the structural reason the factorisation algebra is locally constant
in the topological direction.

\paragraph{(c) Formal holomorphic locality.}
In the holomorphic direction (the $\C^2$ factor), the model has been
completed at the brane point $p\in\C^2$. It is a theory of holomorphic
jets at $p$, not a theory of finite propagation through $\C^2$.
Antiholomorphic translations are $Q$-exact:
$$L_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}
  =[Q,\iota_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}].$$
The kinematic differential of the closed sector is
$D=d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2}$, and on the formal-jet model
$\bar\partial$-cohomology is concentrated in degree zero. The cotangent
boundary sector is \emph{distributionally local, not polynomially local}:
a coadjoint mode is a transverse principal part
$\rho_{a,b}=z_1^{-a-1}z_2^{-b-1}\,dz_1\,dz_2$, paired with a brane
Hamiltonian by residue,
$$\langle\rho_{a,b},z_1^mz_2^n\rangle=\delta_{a,m}\delta_{b,n}.$$
This is exactly what one expects for a momentum dual field attached to a
defect: support on the defect, transverse behaviour encoded by residues.
The polynomial one-$\psi$ descendants $\Psi_{k,l}$ realise the PBW
special fibre of $\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:open-descendant-action});
Corollary~\ref{cor:descendant-coadjoint-difference} records the
deformation-level mismatch with the coadjoint module, exactly the ordinary
distinction between polynomial and distributional realisations.

The factorisation-algebra structure is now \emph{forced}: it is the
algebraic expression of (a)+(b)+(c). Disjoint supports multiply along the
brane; topological motion is $Q$-exact and changes nothing in cohomology;
transverse holomorphic dependence is distributional. No external categorical
input has been imposed; the structure is the local algebra of measurements
in a constrained canonical system.

\subsection{Unitarity}

The model is a twisted BV sector. It is not a Lorentzian unitary quantum
mechanics. There is no positive-definite Hilbert space, no Wightman
positivity, and no reflection positivity. The fields include ghosts and
antifields; topological time has been made cohomologically trivial.

The replacements for unitarity are the consistency conditions of the BV
formalism: the classical master equation
$$QI+\tfrac12\{I,I\}=0$$
and the quantum master equation
$$QI+\tfrac12\{I,I\}+\hbar\,\Delta I=0,$$
together with associativity of the resulting factorisation/OPE algebra. If
the local model arises as a protected sector of a larger unitary theory
(for example, of a topological twist of a supersymmetric quantum field
theory in which the local observables of the present model are the
cohomology with respect to a supercharge), then unitarity is carried by
the larger theory, and the local sector retains only the cohomological
algebra of protected observables. Within the present manuscript we do not
impose unitarity, and we make no Lorentzian claims.

\subsection{Thesis}

\begin{quote}
A stack of branes is a system of probes for the formal symplectic normal
disk. Dirac reduction of the probe phase space gives the open trace algebra.
Hamiltonian BF theory is the shifted cotangent theory of canonical
transformations. The closed observables are precisely the derived Poisson
central operations on the stable open Hamiltonian brane algebra.
\end{quote}

\subsection{Mixed holomorphic-topological strings}

A local string theory in this paper means the part of string field theory
visible to local operators. The closed fields form a BV theory; local
observables form a factorization algebra; a brane contributes an open cyclic
field theory and a bulk-to-boundary map. The words topological and
holomorphic describe how these local operators vary in the spacetime
directions. This is a local string-field-theoretic use of the word
``string'', not a definition of a global theory of worldsheet moduli,
amplitudes on all backgrounds, or a completed quantum anomaly theory.

Gwilliam--Williams \cite{gwilliam-williams-holomorphic-bosonic-string} are
the precedent for formulating a holomorphic string in the Costello
BV/factorization formalism. Their object is the holomorphic bosonic string
on a Riemann surface, with Dolbeault fields $(\gamma,\beta,c,b)$, a
one-loop quantization in the critical complex dimension, and a
factorization algebra recovering the BRST cohomology. The object here is
not that theory and not a replacement definition. It is a formal local
target-space sector: de Rham/Floer directions, a holomorphic symplectic
formal disk, Hamiltonian cotangent BF fields, and a brane large-$N$
operator algebra.

The topological word refers to locally constant factorization in the de
Rham/Floer directions. The holomorphic word refers to the Dolbeault
presentation: the kinetic operator contains $\bar\partial$, the fields are
holomorphic jets after local formal completion, and anti-holomorphic
translations act by cochain-homotopic zero. A holomorphic theory may
acquire further topological descent after quantization; that extra descent
is not part of the definition used here.

\begin{defn}[Working local topological factorization sector]\label{def:local-topological-string-sector}
  Let $M$ be a smooth manifold. A local topological closed-string sector on
  $M$ is a classical BV theory whose local observables form a locally constant
  factorization algebra on $M$: for inclusions of sufficiently small disks
  $U\subset V$, the factorization structure map
  $$\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}(U)\longrightarrow
    \mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}(V)$$
  is a quasi-isomorphism. In this paper, attaching branes to such a sector
  means specifying a cyclic open BV theory and the closed-open operations
  actually constructed. In a de Rham model the closed fields carry the
  differential $d_M$ plus the BV linearized differential, and the locally
  constant factorization product records collision of operators up to isotopy.
\end{defn}

\begin{rmk}
  The exact A-model factor used below is a local topological sector in this
  sense: the self-Floer model for $\R\subset T^*\R$ is represented by the
  de Rham complex $\Omega^*(\R)$, and its local observables are insensitive
  to the metric geometry of the interval. This is the topological part of
  the mixed holomorphic-topological example.
\end{rmk}

\begin{defn}[Working local holomorphic factorization sector]\label{def:local-holomorphic-string-sector}
  Let $Y$ be a complex manifold. A local holomorphic sector on $Y$ is a
  classical BV theory whose fields are Dolbeault complexes on $Y$, whose
  differential has the form $\bar\partial$ plus the BV linearized
  differential, whose interactions are holomorphic polydifferential
  operators, and whose local observables form a holomorphic factorization
  algebra. Here holomorphic factorization means that, on coordinate
  polydisks, the factorization products and restriction maps are
  represented by holomorphic polydifferential operations and every
  anti-holomorphic translation $\partial/\partial\bar z_i$ acts
  null-homotopically on observables. In the target-space Kodaira-Spencer
  examples the fields are Dolbeault-valued polyvectors; in the holomorphic
  symplectic examples below they are Hamiltonian polyvectors after removing
  constants. In this paper branes are treated through cyclic open BV theory
  and the bulk-to-boundary operations constructed below.
\end{defn}

\begin{rmk}
  BCOV/Kodaira-Spencer theory is the guiding threefold example
  \cite{bcov}: its fields are Dolbeault-valued polyvectors, and the
  Calabi-Yau volume form supplies the divergence operator. In the
  holomorphic symplectic surface model used here, the analogous
  divergence-free vector fields are represented locally by Hamiltonians
  modulo constants. The surface model is not a truncation of threefold BCOV
  theory.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}
  The classical local observable theory underlying Gwilliam--Williams is an
  example of a pure holomorphic BV/factorization sector on a Riemann
  surface, with additional worldsheet ghost, BRST, and critical-dimension
  quantum structure. Their critical-dimension and BRST-cohomology theorems
  are not imported here. The model below is a different formal local
  target-space sector whose holomorphic sector is Hamiltonian BF, or the
  holomorphic symplectic Kodaira-Spencer analogue, and whose topological
  sector is de Rham/Floer. In particular, the critical complex dimension in
  Gwilliam--Williams is a worldsheet ghost-anomaly statement for the
  holomorphic bosonic string; it is not a constraint on the local
  $\R^2\times\C^2$ Hamiltonian sector studied here.
\end{rmk}

\begin{defn}[Working classical local mixed holomorphic-topological sector]\label{def:local-th-string}
  Let $M$ be a smooth manifold and let $Y$ be a complex manifold. A
  classical local mixed holomorphic-topological closed sector on $M\times Y$
  consists of:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item a sheaf of cochain complexes of fields $\mc E$ which, on product
      coordinate opens $D\times B$, has the form
      $$\mc E(D\times B)
        =\Omega^*(D)\widehat{\otimes}\Omega^{0,*}(B,\mc V)$$
      for a graded holomorphic vector bundle or formal holomorphic vector
      space $\mc V$;
    \item a degree $-1$ local BV pairing on $\mc E$ and a differential
      $$Q=d_M+\bar\partial_Y+Q_0,$$
      where $Q_0$ is holomorphic over $Y$ and is linear over de Rham forms
      on $M$;
    \item a degree-zero local functional
      $I\in\mathcal O_{\mathrm{loc}}(\mc E)$, built from differential
      operators in the $M$ directions and holomorphic polydifferential
      operators in the $Y$ directions, satisfying the classical master
      equation
      $$QI+\frac12\{I,I\}=0;$$
    \item the associated classical observables
      $$\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}(U)
        =\left(\widehat{\mathrm{Sym}}\bigl(\mc E^!_c(U)\bigr),
        Q_{\mathrm{obs}}\right),\qquad
        Q_{\mathrm{obs}}=Q^!+\{I,-\},$$
      with the standard factorization product for disjoint supports. Here
      $\mc E^!_c(U)$ denotes compactly supported continuous linear
      observables, i.e.\ the density-dual cosheaf of fields; extension by
      zero gives the covariant structure maps used by the factorization
      algebra.
  \end{enumerate}
  These data must satisfy the mixed locality condition. For every inclusion
  of small disks $D\subset D'$ in $M$ and every holomorphic polydisk
  $B\subset Y$, the structure map
  $$\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}(D\times B)\longrightarrow
    \mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}(D'\times B)$$
  is a quasi-isomorphism. In holomorphic coordinates on $B$, each
  anti-holomorphic translation $\partial/\partial\bar z_i$ acts
  null-homotopically on observables: there is a degree $-1$ derivation
  $\eta_i$ with
  $$[Q_{\mathrm{obs}},\eta_i]=\mathcal L_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}.$$

  A mixed brane for such a sector is supported on $N\times Z$, where
  $N\subset M$ is a smooth submanifold and $Z\subset Y$ is a holomorphic
  submanifold or a formal holomorphic neighbourhood of one, and is
  specified by an object $\mc F$ of the local holomorphic brane category on
  $Z$. Its open fields have the derived form
  $$\Omega^*(N)\widehat{\otimes}\RHom_Y(\mc F,\mc F)\otimes\End(V)[1],$$
  with a cyclic trace. For a smooth brane this recovers the Dolbeault model
  $\Omega^*(N)\widehat{\otimes}\Omega^{0,*}(Z,\mc W)$; for a skyscraper
  brane it produces the Ext algebra. A full closed-open mixed datum would
  further require a morphism of factorization algebras
  $$\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{closed}}\big|_{N\times Z}
    \longrightarrow
    \mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{open}}\bigr),$$
  from closed observables to the Poisson/BV factorization center of the
  open brane observables, compatible with the BV brackets and
  factorization products. In the Hamiltonian model below we construct the
  degree-zero Hamiltonian current shadow of this map; the full closed
  CE/cotangent factorization-center lift is
  Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}.
\end{defn}

\begin{rmk}
  A quantum mixed holomorphic-topological string datum would be the
  corresponding $\hbar$-adic factorization algebra obtained from a
  renormalized BV action satisfying the quantum master equation. This paper
  constructs no such quantum datum for the Hamiltonian model. It proves the
  classical local closed-open Hamiltonian theorem and formulates the
  quantum upgrade in Problem~\ref{prob:quantum-hamiltonian-upgrade}.
\end{rmk}

Definition~\ref{def:local-th-string} separates three levels. A pure
topological sector is locally constant in all real directions; in examples
this includes the A-model local/Floer direction and the Chern-Simons-type
open field theory on a topological brane. A pure holomorphic sector is
Dolbeault in its complex directions and produces a holomorphic
factorization algebra; Gwilliam--Williams' holomorphic bosonic string is a
worldsheet example, while BCOV/Kodaira-Spencer gives the guiding
target-space closed-string example. The Hamiltonian BF complex below is the
formal local target-space sector used in this paper. A mixed
holomorphic-topological sector lives on $M\times Y$ with locally constant
factorization in $M$ and holomorphic factorization in $Y$. The A/B
terminology used below is one source of such examples: the A-side supplies
the de Rham/Floer direction and the B-side supplies the Dolbeault or formal
holomorphic direction.

\subsection{The local mixed model}

The paper studies the product local model
$$\R^2_{\mathrm{top}}\times\C^2_{\mathrm{hol}}.$$
The theorem is not a global statement about all twisted M-theory
backgrounds. It is the formal local calculation obtained after completing
at a brane $\R\times p$ and taking the holomorphic symplectic normal disk
at $p\in\C^2$, with
$$\omega=dz_1\wedge dz_2.$$
The closed sector is the Hamiltonian Kodaira-Spencer/BF theory on this
mixed space, not a pure A-model or pure B-model. The open sector is the
cyclic open string field theory on the mixed brane: topological along $\R$
and formal holomorphic in the normal $\C^2$ directions.

\begin{rmk}[Global obstruction]
  The Hamiltonian identification used here is local. On a holomorphic
  symplectic surface $X$, a holomorphic vector field $v$ is symplectic when
  $$\alpha_v=-\iota_v\omega$$
  is a closed holomorphic one-form, and it is Hamiltonian only after
  choosing $f$ with $df=\alpha_v$, in the convention
  $\iota_{X_f}\omega=-df$. Thus globalizing the Hamiltonian sector requires
  either a sheaf of local Hamiltonians or vanishing of the corresponding
  holomorphic de Rham obstruction. The formal disk has no such obstruction
  by the holomorphic Poincare lemma; a general $X$ need not.
\end{rmk}

\begin{prop}[Global local-Hamiltonian restriction]\label{prop:formal-local-global-restriction}
  Let $(X,\omega)$ be a connected holomorphic symplectic surface and let
  $p\in X$. Put
  $$\mc H_X=\mc O_X/\C_X,\qquad
    \widehat{\mathfrak h}_{X,p}=\widehat{\mc O}_{X,p}/\C.$$
  The differential identifies $\mc H_X$ with the sheaf of closed holomorphic
  one-forms, hence with the sheaf of holomorphic symplectic vector fields by
  $\alpha=-\iota_v\omega$. For every $p\in X$ there is a Lie algebra
  restriction
  $$H^0(X,\mc H_X)\longrightarrow\widehat{\mathfrak h}_{X,p}.$$
  The formal neighbourhood $(\widehat X_p,\omega)$ defines the same stable
  Hamiltonian brane sector as the local model of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}, after choosing a formal Darboux coordinate
  system. The resulting boundary map
  $$\widehat{\mathfrak h}_{X,p}\longrightarrow
    H^0_{\mathrm{Ham}}(\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{brane}})$$
  is independent of this choice up to the natural action of the formal
  symplectomorphism group. The subspace coming from global Hamiltonian
  functions is the image of
  $$H^0(X,\mc O_X)/\C\longrightarrow H^0(X,\mc H_X).$$
  The obstruction for a locally Hamiltonian symplectic vector field to come
  from a global Hamiltonian function is its period class in $H^1(X,\C_X)$.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  The holomorphic Poincare lemma gives an isomorphism
  $$d:\mc O_X/\C_X\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\Omega^1_{X,\mathrm{cl}}.$$
  The holomorphic symplectic form identifies a symplectic vector field $v$
  with the closed one-form $\alpha_v=-\iota_v\omega$. Thus a section of
  $\mc H_X$ is exactly a local Hamiltonian primitive, modulo local
  constants, and the Poisson bracket is independent of the local constants.
  Taking the germ at $p$ and completing gives the displayed restriction to
  $\widehat{\mathfrak h}_{X,p}$.

  The formal holomorphic Darboux theorem identifies the completed local
  symplectic algebra at $p$ with $\C[[z_1,z_2]]$ equipped with
  $dz_1\wedge dz_2$. Under this identification Hamiltonians modulo
  constants become $\widehat{\mathfrak h}=\C[[z_1,z_2]]/\C$, and the
  point-brane Ext algebra is the coordinate-free exterior algebra
  $\Ext_X^*(\mc O_p,\mc O_p)\cong\Lambda^*T_pX$, with cyclic trace fixed by
  $\omega_p$. Hence the open BV reduction and the Hamiltonian boundary
  evaluation are exactly the formal local construction after choosing
  Darboux coordinates. A different Darboux coordinate system differs by a
  formal symplectomorphism, which acts on Hamiltonians and on the normal
  coordinate algebra; the substitution map $z_i\mapsto\phi_i$ is
  equivariant for this action.

  The exact sequence
  $$0\to\C_X\to\mc O_X\to\mc H_X\to0$$
  gives
  $$0\to H^0(X,\mc O_X)/\C
    \to H^0(X,\mc H_X)
    \xrightarrow{\delta}H^1(X,\C_X)
    \to H^1(X,\mc O_X).$$
  For a locally Hamiltonian vector field, $\delta$ is the period class of
  the closed one-form $-\iota_v\omega$. Vanishing of this class is exactly
  the existence of a single global holomorphic Hamiltonian primitive,
  unique modulo constants.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  This is the maximal global statement used in the paper. If
  $H^1(X,\C)=0$, global symplectic vector fields which are locally
  Hamiltonian have global Hamiltonian primitives. If $X$ is Stein, every
  finite jet needed for a finite local calculation can be lifted to a
  global holomorphic Hamiltonian, noncanonically: apply Cartan's theorem B
  to
  $$0\to\mathfrak m_p^{k+1}\to\mc O_X\to
    \mc O_X/\mathfrak m_p^{k+1}\to0.$$
  This does not imply surjectivity onto $\widehat{\mc O}_{X,p}$. If $X$ is
  compact connected, then $H^0(X,\mc O_X)/\C=0$; abelian surfaces still
  have nonzero locally Hamiltonian translations, obstructed by their period
  classes. A global cochain-level Poisson factorization-center map or a
  global quantum deformation-quantization statement requires additional
  descent, anomaly, and background-choice data.
\end{rmk}

The closed Hamiltonian coefficient Lie algebra is the reduced Tate vector
space
$$\widehat{\mathfrak h}=\C[[z_1,z_2]]/\C\cdot1.$$
We write a class by its unique zero-constant Taylor representative. The
bracket is the projected Poisson bracket
$$\{f,g\}=\partial_{z_1}f\,\partial_{z_2}g
  -\partial_{z_2}f\,\partial_{z_1}g\quad \bmod \C\cdot1.$$
Thus $\{z_1,z_2\}=0$ in $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$, although the unreduced
Poisson bracket of the chosen representatives is $1$. The cotangent BF
field contributes the continuous dual, so the residual local closed Lie
algebra is
$$\mathfrak g=\widehat{\mathfrak h}\ltimes
  \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1].$$
On product opens in $\R^2\times\C^2$ the closed fields have the mixed form
$$\Omega^*(D)\widehat\otimes\Omega^{0,*}(B)\widehat\otimes
  \bigl(\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]\oplus
  \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]\bigr),$$
with differential $d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2}$ and BF interaction
$\frac12\int\langle\beta,\{\alpha,\alpha\}\rangle dz_1dz_2$.
Proposition~\ref{prop:local-model-mixed-definition} checks that this is a
local mixed holomorphic-topological BV sector in the sense above.

The open brane is the product of the exact local A-brane
$\R\subset T^*\R$ and the B-brane $\mc O_p$ at the formal holomorphic
point. The Yoneda algebra of the skyscraper at the origin is computed in
Proposition~\ref{prop:skyscraper-ext}; for a cyclic Calabi-Yau $A_\infty$
category the open field of an object $\mc F$ is $\RHom(\mc F,\mc F)[1]$,
and the formal Chern-Simons action
$$S(a)=\sum_{n\geq1}\frac{1}{n+1}
  \mathrm{Tr}\bigl(a\,m_n(a,\ldots,a)\bigr),\qquad a\in\RHom(\mc F,\mc F)[1],$$
is the algebraic core of Witten's open string field theory \cite{witten-cs}
and of the AKSZ packaging \cite{aksz}. In the present local model
$$\RHom_{\C[z_1,z_2]}(\mc O_p,\mc O_p)
  \cong\Lambda(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2),$$
and the ghost-zero open field is
$$\alpha_0=A+\phi_1\varepsilon_1+\phi_2\varepsilon_2.$$
The ghost-zero action is the first-order gauged matrix model of
\eqref{eq:open-action-derived}, where $\phi_1,\phi_2$ are adjoint scalar
normal coordinates and $A$ imposes the moment-map equation
$[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$.

\subsection{Hamiltonian sector and stable large N}

Everything below is over $\C$. The phrase \emph{formal local model} means
the completed Taylor model at the chosen point of $\C^2$; equivalently, one
may work polynomially degree by degree and then complete at the
augmentation ideal. The symbol $\widehat{\mathbf S}$ denotes this completed
symmetric algebra, and all Chevalley-Eilenberg cochains are continuous
cochains for the same filtration.

Shifts follow the BV convention used in the field descriptions: an element
of $V[1]$ has parity reversed and cohomological degree one lower than the
corresponding element of $V$. The notation $\mathbf S(V)$ always means the
free graded-commutative algebra on the graded vector space $V$.

Let
$$\bar A=\C[z_1,z_2]/\C\cdot1,\qquad
  \mathfrak h=\widehat{\mathfrak h}=\C[[z_1,z_2]]/\C\cdot1,\qquad
  \mathfrak h^\vee=\widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}.$$
Constants are removed because a constant Hamiltonian has zero Hamiltonian
vector field. We use zero-constant Taylor representatives for calculations,
but the Lie bracket is always the Poisson bracket followed by projection
modulo constants. On the brane side $\mathrm{Tr}_N(1)=N$ is the empty
trace, a central scalar depending on the rank. We do not quotient the
associative operator algebra by its unit. The Hamiltonian comparison uses
the connected stable trace sector: the unit is retained in the symmetric
algebra, but the empty trace is not a primitive generator and constants
project to zero in the Hamiltonian Lie/vector quotient. If $T$ is a
positive word-degree trace expression, $\overline T$ denotes its connected
trace class; constants have zero connected class.

At a fixed point of the brane line the reduced BV algebra is generated by
two even matrices $\phi_1,\phi_2$ and the odd antifield $\psi=A^*$, with
$$Q\phi_1=Q\phi_2=0,\qquad Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2].$$
Thus the moment-map equation is imposed homologically. Boundary terms on
$\R$ are discarded by taking compactly supported variations, or
equivalently by working on an interval with fixed boundary values and
passing to local operators in the interior.

The term \emph{stable large-$N$} means the degreewise stable value of the
invariant algebras under block restriction as $N\to\infty$. Inside a fixed
finite matrix algebra all finite-$N$ trace identities remain present. In
the stable limit, Procesi--Razmyslov invariant theory
\cites{procesi,razmyslov} says that invariant functions of two matrices
are freely generated by cyclic trace words. The differential
$Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2]$ then makes adjacent swaps exact, so ghost-zero
cyclic words reduce to ordinary commutative monomials
$$\overline{\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1^k\phi_2^l)},\qquad k+l>0.$$
The primitive one-$\psi$ Koszul homology supplies a second nonconstant
family $\Psi_{k,l}$, obtained by inserting one $\psi$ and symmetrising over
all words with $k$ copies of $\phi_1$ and $l$ copies of $\phi_2$. The
scalar class $\mathrm{Tr}(\psi)$ is excluded from the Hamiltonian
comparison because constants have been removed from $\bar A$; higher
$\psi$-count homology lies outside this Hamiltonian sector. The collapse
of cyclic words to commutative monomials on $H^0(Q)$ is the algebraic
shadow of Dirac reduction: the constraint
$Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2]$ is the Koszul resolution of the moment-map
equation.

The large-$N$ principle is the string-field-theoretic form of the
Loday-Quillen-Tsygan principle \cites{loday-quillen,tsygan}; see also
\cite{loday-vallette}*{Ch.~13} for the operadic packaging. Open strings
on a stack produce matrix algebras; closed modes appear in the primitive
stable part. LQT controls the stable invariants of the \emph{unconstrained}
matrix algebra; the moment-map equation $[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$ is the
first-class constraint whose Koszul resolution is exactly the BV reduction
$Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2]$. The theorem below verifies the principle directly
in the present connected Hamiltonian trace sector.

\begin{thm}[Loday-Quillen-Tsygan]
  Let $A$ be a unital associative algebra over a field of characteristic
  zero. The stable Chevalley-Eilenberg homology of $\lie{gl}_{\infty}(A)$
  is the free graded-commutative algebra generated by shifted cyclic
  homology:
  $$H_*^{\mathrm{CE}}\bigl(\lie{gl}_{\infty}(A)\bigr)
    \cong \mathbf S\bigl(HC_{*-1}(A)\bigr).$$
\end{thm}
Here this theorem is a template rather than a direct input: stable matrix
constructions are controlled by cyclic words, while the particular reduced
model is computed by Procesi--Razmyslov invariant theory and the explicit
Koszul differential above. No global $HC_{*-1}$ convention is imported into
the main theorem; cyclic homology supplies the guiding stable-trace
analogy, not the proof of the Hamiltonian sector.

\subsection{The concrete dictionary}

We write $\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}$ for an abstract copy of $\bar A$ whose
basis vector labelled by $z_1^kz_2^l$, with $k+l>0$, is represented on the
brane by the first descendant $\Psi_{k,l}$. On the closed side the
cotangent field gives the continuous Taylor dual $\mathfrak h^\vee$.
Choosing the monomial Taylor basis identifies $\mathfrak h^\vee$ with
$\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}$ as a filtered vector space. The closed module
structure remains the coadjoint module structure.

For $k,l\geq0$ and $k+l>0$, set
$$H_{k,l}=z_1^kz_2^l\in\bar A,\qquad
  E_{k,l}=\delta_{k,l}[1]\in\mathfrak h^\vee[1],$$
where $\delta_{k,l}$ is the coefficient functional dual to the Taylor
monomial $z_1^kz_2^l$:
$$\delta_{k,l}(z_1^az_2^b)=\delta_{k,a}\delta_{l,b}.$$
On the brane side set
$$O_{k,l}=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1^k\phi_2^l)},$$
and let $\Psi_{k,l}$ be the symmetrised trace with one $\psi$, $k$ copies
of $\phi_1$, and $l$ copies of $\phi_2$. The theorem proves that
$$H_{k,l}\longmapsto O_{k,l},\qquad E_{k,l}\longmapsto\Psi_{k,l}$$
extends to an isomorphism of the connected stable Hamiltonian descendant
sector with
$$\mathbf S(\bar A\oplus\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}[1])
  \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\mc O_{\mathrm{brane},H}^{\mathrm{cl}}$$
in the sector considered here. On the closed side the symbols
$H_{k,l},E_{k,l}$ form the degreewise polynomial PBW generators inside the
special fibre of $U_\hbar(\mathfrak g)$.

Each later step has a concrete target: construct the symbols
$O_{k,l},\Psi_{k,l}$ from the open fields; construct $H_{k,l},E_{k,l}$
from Hamiltonians and cotangent Hamiltonians; prove that commutators of
words reduce to commutative monomials in $H^0(Q)$; and verify that the
bracket coefficient is $kn-lm$.

\subsection{Status of assertions and the analytic problem}\label{ssec:quantum-target}

The local theorem stated below is the precise local assertion proved in
these notes; the terms appearing in it are constructed in the subsequent
sections. The proof consists of: the affine $\Ext$ calculation
(Proposition~\ref{prop:skyscraper-ext}); the open BV reduction
(Lemma~\ref{lem:open-action-reduction},
Proposition~\ref{prop:open-bv-truncation}); the Dirac reduction of the
probe phase space
(Lemma~\ref{lem:dirac-probe-reduction}); the stable invariant-theory
calculation of the Hamiltonian trace algebra
(Proposition~\ref{prop:stable-trace-invariants}); the computation of the
primitive one-antifield Koszul homology
(Proposition~\ref{prop:one-psi-homology}); the formal Hamiltonian BF model
for the closed side
(Proposition~\ref{prop:hamiltonian-polyvector-reduction}); the
construction of the bulk-to-boundary Hamiltonian evaluation map
(Construction~\ref{constr:boundary-evaluation},
Theorem~\ref{thm:bulk-boundary}); the CE/Koszul-duality computation; and
the first bracket calculation \eqref{eq:bracket-coefficient}.

The formal Weyl/Moyal calculation below is an all-order algebraic
deformation-quantisation target for the constant Poisson formal disk; its
monomial coefficients are checked by an exact script. A closed-string
Feynman-integral derivation of those coefficients is a separate analytic
problem, requiring the global BV/gauge-fixing data of
Problem~\ref{prob:analytic-graph-realization}: a global elliptic complex
extending the formal jet model; boundary conditions on $\C^2$; a
gauge-fixing $Q^{\mathrm{GF}}$ and the heat-kernel propagator
$P_{\epsilon,L}=\int_\epsilon^L Q^{\mathrm{GF}}K_t\,dt$; zero-mode
treatment and the IR limit; UV renormalisation scheme and local
counterterms; quantum master equation or anomaly class; bulk-to-boundary
kernel for the brane; trace normalisation and large-$N$ weighting; and
the connected/single-trace extraction convention. Costello's renormalized
BV formalism supplies the general graph/RG package; Costello--Li prove
the flat odd-dimensional BCOV/HCS case
\cites{costello-li-quantum-bcov,costello-li-open-closed-bcov}. The proof
of Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local} uses the formal local algebra alone and
is independent of these analytic choices.

\subsection{The local theorem}

The theorem has three layers. First, the open calculation says
that the ghost-zero brane theory is the algebra of invariant functions on
commuting matrix pairs, together with the first Koszul descendants of the
commuting-pair equation. Second, the closed calculation says that the same
generators are the PBW symbols of the Hamiltonian cotangent Lie algebra. Third,
the boundary map is not an abstract isomorphism: it is the physical operation
of evaluating a Hamiltonian on the matrix-valued normal coordinates of the
brane.

The local theorem is the umbrella of six interlocking statements:
a cochain-level open-closed derived-center isomorphism $\Phi$ at universal
generality (any pro-finite-dimensional Tate-conilpotent Lie algebra), its
principal-part / coadjoint identification on the cotangent direction, its
factorization-algebra upgrade on the brane line, its all-order quantum
deformation $\Phi_\hbar$ on the Hamiltonian sector, and its U(1) center
anomaly $[\bar c]$ at the boundary between scalar-reduced and unreduced
sectors. The single residual is the Tate-coefficient lift of the cotangent
direction in the unreduced factorization-algebra model.

\begin{thm}[Local Hamiltonian closed-open derived center theorem]\label{thm:main-local}
  \label{thm:main-local-derived-center}%
  Consider the formal local mixed holomorphic-topological BV brane on
  $\R^2\times\C^2$ with brane $\R\times p$, in the convention of
  Section~\ref{sec:grav-ops}. Let
  $\mathfrak h=(z_1,z_2)\,\C[[z_1,z_2]]$ be the reduced Hamiltonian Lie
  algebra of the formal symplectic disk, let
  $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$ be
  its shifted-cotangent semidirect extension, and for an interval
  $I\subset\R$ let
  $\mathfrak h_I=C^{\infty}_c(I)\,\widehat\otimes\,\mathfrak h$ and
  $\mathfrak g_I=\mathfrak h_I\ltimes\mathcal P_I[1]$ with
  $\mathcal P_I=\mathcal D'_c(I)\,\widehat\otimes\,\mc P$ as in
  Construction~\ref{constr:interval-fact-algebras}. The following six
  statements hold and together constitute the local Hamiltonian
  closed-open derived center theorem.

  \begin{enumerate}
    \item \emph{Universal cochain-level isomorphism.} For any
      pro-finite-dimensional Lie algebra $\mathfrak h$ in $\Cat{TateVec}$
      over $\C$, concentrated in degree zero, satisfying the
      Tate-conilpotency hypothesis of
      Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-bar-cobar}, there is a canonical
      isomorphism of completed dg graded-commutative $P_0$-algebras
      $$\Phi:C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)
        \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
        \mathrm{PV}\bigl(\widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\mathfrak h)\bigr)
        \simeq Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(
        \widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\mathfrak h)\bigr),$$
      determined on generators by $\Phi(c^I)=\theta^I$,
      $\Phi(u_I)=O_I$, where $c^I,u_I$ are the CE coordinates dual to
      $H_I\in\mathfrak h$ and
      $\eta_{\delta_I}\in\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$ and
      $\theta^I,O_I$ are the corresponding Schouten/Lichnerowicz
      coordinates. The cochain identity
      $\Phi\circ d_{\mathrm{CE}}=d_{\pi}\circ\Phi$ is verified on
      generators and propagated by graded Leibniz to the completed
      algebra. (See~\ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center},
      \ref{lem:linear-poisson-schouten}, and
      \ref{lem:continuous-bar-cobar}.)

    \item \emph{Principal-part coadjoint identification.} The continuous
      dual $\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}$ of the reduced Hamiltonian
      Lie algebra is canonically isomorphic to the principal-part residue
      module $\mc P=\bigoplus_{a+b>0}\C\,\rho_{a,b}$ with
      $\rho_{a,b}=z_1^{-a-1}z_2^{-b-1}\,dz_1\,dz_2$, by the unique
      $\mathfrak h$-equivariant continuous pairing of total degree zero
      $$\langle\rho_{a,b},\,z_1^m z_2^n\rangle
        =\operatorname{Res}_{z_1=z_2=0}z_1^{m-a-1}z_2^{n-b-1}\,dz_1\,dz_2
        =\delta_{a,m}\,\delta_{b,n}$$
      (modulo a single nonzero scalar, by Schur rigidity). The coadjoint
      action on $\mc P$ is the lowering action
      $$z_1^p z_2^q\cdot \rho_{a,b}
        =-(pb-qa+p-q)\,\rho_{a-p+1,\,b-q+1},$$
      verified on three explicit monomial test cases and a $1225$-case
      sweep (\texttt{scripts/check\_one\_psi\_homology.py}). The
      polynomial $\Psi_{a,b}\in\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}$ basis acts by
      symmetric raising and represents the PBW special-fibre at
      $\hbar=0$; the $\rho_{a,b}$ basis acts by coadjoint lowering and
      represents the deformation-correct module. The two are not in
      conflict: they are different bases of the same
      $\mathfrak g$-module, interpolated by the Rees parameter $\hbar$
      of the formal Moyal deformation. (See the principal-part block
      around~\ref{prop:principal-part-coadjoint}.)

    \item \emph{Factorization-algebra upgrade on the brane line.}
      The Hamiltonian factor admits an interval-wise quasi-isomorphism
      of locally constant $P_0$ factorization algebras
      $$\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}:
        \mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{closed},H,\mathrm{Ham}}\big|_{\R\times p}
        \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
        Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(A^{\mathrm{Ham}}_\partial\bigr),$$
      where on each interval $I\subset\R$,
      $A^{\mathrm{Ham}}_\partial(I)=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)$
      with the strict $P_0$ bracket
      $\{B_f(a),B_g(b)\}_{A^{\mathrm{Ham}}_\partial}
      =B_{\{f,g\}_{\bar A}}(ab)$, supplied on length one by
      $$(a\otimes f)^{\vee}[-1]\longmapsto B_f(a)
        :=\int_I a(t)\,\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1(t),\phi_2(t))}\,dt.$$
      The map is compatible with extension by zero, with disjoint-interval
      factorization products, with the locally constant structure on $\R$,
      and recovers the stalkwise central operation $f\mapsto L_{B_f}$ at
      the point limit $I\to\{t_0\}$. The locality input is the canonical
      equal-time bracket
      $\{(\phi_1)^i{}_j(t),(\phi_2)^k{}_l(s)\}=\delta^i_l\delta^k_j\,
      \delta(t-s)$, and the strict (non-homotopical) $P_0$ structure
      follows from the delta-function locality. (See
      \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization},
      \ref{prop:brane-bracket-locality},
      \ref{thm:hamiltonian-current-center-lift}, and
      \ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling}.)

    \item \emph{Cotangent factor at the post-contraction reduced level.}
      The principal-part / cotangent factor extends the Hamiltonian
      factorization algebra to the $P_0$ factorization algebra
      $A^{\mathrm{pp}}_\partial(I)
      =\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)\,\widehat\otimes\,
      \widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathcal P_I[1])$ on the reduced
      post-de Rham contraction model, with brackets
      $$\{B_f(a),\Theta_\rho(B)\}_{A^{\mathrm{pp}}_\partial}
        =\Theta_{f\cdot\rho}(aB),
        \qquad
        \{\Theta_\rho(B),\Theta_\sigma(C)\}_{A^{\mathrm{pp}}_\partial}=0,$$
      and the bulk-to-boundary morphism
      $\widetilde\partial_{\mathrm{bb}}:\bar A\oplus\mc P[1]
      \to A^{\mathrm{pp}}_\partial$ extends \ref{thm:bulk-boundary} to
      the closed-coadjoint sector
      $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$.
      In the reduced model the cochain-level isomorphism of part~(a)
      extends to the cotangent factor; in the unreduced
      factorization-algebra model the cotangent factor is conditional on
      \ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}.

    \item \emph{All-order quantum deformation $\Phi_\hbar$ on the
      degree-zero Hamiltonian sector.} The classical $\Phi$ deforms to
      all orders in $\hbar$ on the degree-zero Hamiltonian sector,
      giving a $\C[[\hbar]]$-linear cochain isomorphism
      $$\Phi^{(0)}_\hbar:\bigl[
        C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont},\hbar}(\mathfrak g_\hbar)
        \bigr]^{(0)}[[\hbar]]
        \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
        Z^{P_{0,\hbar}}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(\mathrm{Obs}^{\hbar}_{\mathrm{open}}
        \bigr)^{(0)},$$
      where on degree-zero generators
      $\Phi^{(0)}_\hbar(f)=[\,\overline{J_N(f)}\,]_{N\to\infty}
      =\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f)$ with $J_N(f)$ the
      Capelli-renormalized stable connected Weyl trace. The cochain
      identity
      $\hbar^{-1}[\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f),
        \partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(g)]_{\mathrm{conn,raw}}
      =\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(\{f,g\}_\hbar)$
      holds at all orders. The boundary product is the formal Weyl/Moyal
      product of $\bar A_\hbar$ in the unique unconditional normalization
      with cross-contraction kernel $P_\partial=P$ at weight $\hbar/2$;
      the first and third Costello graph normalizations agree with the
      Moyal coefficients $1$ and $1/24$ respectively. The associated
      graded at $\hbar=0$ recovers the degree-zero restriction of $\Phi$.
      (See the quantum sector around
      \ref{prob:first-third-graph-normalizations}.)

    \item \emph{U(1) center anomaly.} The scalar-reduction direction
      $\C\cdot 1\subset\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$ and
      $\C\cdot\mathrm{Tr}(1)\subset H^0$ carries a single nontrivial
      cohomology class
      $$[\bar c]\in H^2_{\mathrm{Lie}}(\bar A,\C),$$
      represented by the constant Taylor coefficient
      $\omega(z_1^k z_2^l, z_1^m z_2^n)=(kn-lm)\,
      \mathbf 1[(k+m,l+n)=(1,1)]$ of the Poisson bracket on
      $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}$. The class $[\bar c]$ is realized
      identically at classical level (the Poisson cocycle $\omega$,
      obstructing the Lie-algebra splitting of
      $\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}\to\bar A$) and at quantum level (the
      Capelli shift $\hbar N$ in $YX-XY+\hbar N\,I=0$, leading
      coefficient of the Moyal commutator on linear traces). The
      equivalence $\Phi$ holds modulo $[\bar c]$, i.e.\ on the
      scalar-reduced quotient; the U(1) anomaly $[\bar c]$ is the unique
      obstruction to lifting $\Phi$ to the unreduced sector on the
      Hamiltonian-constants axis. The healed local bulk-boundary
      coupling carries an explicit central piece
      $$\{I_\partial(a,f),I_\partial(b,g)\}_{\mathrm{open}}
        =I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A})
        +N\cdot\omega(f,g)\int_\R a(t)b(t)\,dt,$$
      which vanishes after projection to $H^0_{\mathrm{red}}$. (See
      \ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling}.)
  \end{enumerate}

  Statement~(a) is the universal cochain-level identification, of which
  the formal symplectic disk in dimension two is one corollary.
  Statement~(b) supplies the deformation-correct realization of the
  cotangent direction $\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$.
  Statement~(c) upgrades the local fiber to a factorization-algebra
  equivalence on the brane line in the connected Hamiltonian sector.
  Statement~(d) extends the equivalence to the cotangent factor at the
  post-contraction reduced level. Statement~(e) deforms the equivalence
  to all orders in $\hbar$ on the degree-zero Hamiltonian sector.
  Statement~(f) names the unique obstruction class along the
  scalar-reduction axis.

  The moment-map shadow at degree zero, $f\mapsto
  \overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}=O_f$, recovers the existing
  classical bulk-to-boundary map of \ref{thm:bulk-boundary}.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  Each statement is established by the cited constituent result, with
  cross-consistency of signs, Tate completions, factorization sectors,
  anomaly classes, and conditionality classifications recorded throughout
  the manuscript.

  Statement~(a) is \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center} applied to
  $\mathfrak h=(z_1,z_2)\C[[z_1,z_2]]$, which is pro-finite-dimensional
  in Taylor filtration, perfect, and Tate-conilpotent (the bracket
  strictly lowers Taylor degree, so descending Lie powers vanish on each
  finite Taylor window).

  Statement~(b) is the existence and Schur uniqueness of the residue
  pairing combined with the induced $\mathfrak h$-module isomorphism
  with explicit lowering action; the PBW-vs-deformation comparison
  interpolates the polynomial $\Psi_{a,b}$ raising basis (PBW special
  fibre) and the principal-part $\rho_{a,b}$ lowering basis
  (deformation-correct).

  Statement~(c) is
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization} on the connected
  Hamiltonian sub-factorization algebra
  $A^{\mathrm{Ham}}_\partial(I)=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)$,
  with locality of the strict $P_0$ bracket on disjoint supports
  (\ref{prop:brane-bracket-locality}) and stalk recovery via
  \ref{lem:derivative-jets}.

  Statement~(d) combines the factorization companion to the local
  cotangent identification with the principal-part boundary cotangent
  operators. In the reduced post-contraction model the cochain
  isomorphism of (a) extends to the cotangent factor by the embedding
  $\bar A\oplus\mc P[1]\hookrightarrow A^{\mathrm{pp}}_\partial(I)$,
  with brackets matching
  $\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$ on the
  smeared sector. The unreduced factorization-algebra extension is the
  content of \ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}.

  Statement~(e) is the all-order quantum upgrade, with the Capelli
  renormalization absorbing the $\hbar N$ contact term into the change
  of basis $T_{a,b}\leftrightarrow J_N(z_1^a z_2^b)$, the radial-parts
  identity producing the all-orders bracket equation, the unconditional
  boundary product normalization fixing the Moyal/Weyl coefficient at
  every order, and the matching with Costello's first and third graph
  normalizations. The classical limit $\hbar\to 0$ recovers the
  degree-zero restriction of (a) through the moment-map shadow.

  Statement~(f) is \ref{lem:omega-cocycle} (the Poisson cocycle
  $\omega$ is closed and nontrivial), \ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly}
  (closed-side central extension
  $0\to\C\cdot 1\to\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{poly}}\to\bar A\to 0$ is
  classified by $[\bar c]$), \ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly-open}
  (open-side U(1) centre of $\mathfrak{gl}_N$ realizes $[\bar c]$ via
  the boundary evaluation),
  \ref{thm:quantum-classical-anomaly} (Rees specialization identifies
  the classical Poisson cocycle $\omega$ with the quantum Capelli shift
  $\hbar N$ as the same class), and the healed
  \ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling} which exhibits the central
  piece explicitly with the constant $N$.

  The six statements interlock without circularity: (a) supplies the
  cochain identity at universal generality; (b) supplies the
  deformation-correct cotangent realization (independent of (a) but
  compatible with it via the dualization $\Phi_{\mathrm{coad}}$); (c)
  upgrades (a) to the brane-line factorization algebra on the
  Hamiltonian factor (using only the classical local equal-time
  bracket); (d) extends (c) to the cotangent factor at the reduced
  level (using (b)); (e) deforms (a)+(c) at the degree-zero Hamiltonian
  sector (using the Capelli renormalization, independent of the
  descendant); (f) names the obstruction class along an orthogonal axis
  (the scalar-reduction line $\C\cdot 1$, independent of the cotangent
  direction $\mathfrak h^{\vee}[1]$).
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}[Universal generality of the umbrella]
  Statement~(a) of \ref{thm:main-local} holds for any
  pro-finite-dimensional Lie algebra $\mathfrak h$ in $\Cat{TateVec}$
  with the conilpotency hypothesis. The formal symplectic disk in
  dimension two is one corollary; the formal Hamiltonian Lie algebra of
  any holomorphic symplectic surface reduced by constants is another.
  Statements~(b)--(f) are dimension-two specific (they use the residue
  pairing on $\C^2$, the matrix Weyl algebra of pairs $(X,Y)$, and the
  U(1) center of $\mathfrak{gl}_N$), and recover the higher-dimensional
  analogues by the same universal cochain identity
  $\Phi\circ d_{\mathrm{CE}}=d_\pi\circ\Phi$ together with the
  appropriate higher-dimensional residue pairing and matrix Weyl data.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}[Dirac thesis, as a consequence of the umbrella]\label{rmk:dirac-thesis}
  The umbrella theorem makes precise the Dirac thesis sentence that
  organizes the manuscript:
  \begin{quote}
    \itshape
    A stack of branes is a system of probes for the formal symplectic
    normal disk. Dirac reduction of the probe phase space gives the
    open trace algebra. Hamiltonian BF theory is the shifted cotangent
    theory of canonical transformations. The closed observables are
    precisely the derived Poisson central operations on the stable open
    Hamiltonian brane algebra.
  \end{quote}
  This is now a corollary of \ref{thm:main-local}: the brane stack is
  the open BV theory of $N$ matrix-valued probes $(\phi_1,\phi_2)$ for
  the formal symplectic disk; Dirac first-class reduction along the
  moment-map ideal $I_N=\mc W_N\widehat\mu(\mathfrak{gl}_N)$ produces
  the stable connected open trace algebra
  $H^0_{\mathrm{Ham,conn}}(\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},\infty})$;
  the closed Hamiltonian BF theory has fields valued in the
  shifted-cotangent semidirect product
  $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$
  with $\mathfrak h$ the Hamiltonian Lie algebra of canonical
  transformations of the formal disk; and the closed observables
  $C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)$ are identified,
  via $\Phi$, with the derived Poisson factorization-center
  $Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(A^{\mathrm{Ham}}_\partial)$ on the brane
  line at the reduced post-contraction classical level (and on the
  degree-zero Hamiltonian sector at all orders in $\hbar$). The slogan
  is no longer a slogan; it is the umbrella theorem read in physical
  language.
\end{rmk}

The proof uses the formal local model alone. The single residual
problem on the unreduced Tate-coefficient cotangent lift is recorded as
\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center} below. The quantum calculation
later fixes the formal Weyl/Moyal target; the analytic problem is to
identify Costello's renormalized BV graph package with this Hamiltonian
BF sector and to recover the first and third graph normalizations.

\section{The Local Model}

\subsection{Setup}
Let
$$M=\R^2,\qquad Y=\C^2,\qquad X=M\times Y.$$
The real factor $M$ is the topological direction and the complex factor $Y$
is the holomorphic direction; all Hamiltonian calculations are completed at
the formal neighbourhood of $p=0\in Y$. We use the exact A-brane given by the
standard line $\R\subset M$ with trivial brane data and the B-brane
  $\mc{O}_p\in\mathrm{Perf}(Y)$. Consider the mixed brane
  $$\R \times p \inj \R^2 \times \C^2$$
  for some point $p \in Y$. We take $p=0$ in coordinates. The holomorphic
  factor carries the standard holomorphic symplectic form
  $$\omega=dz_1\wedge dz_2.$$
  Thus the model is topological along $\R^2$ and holomorphic Hamiltonian along
  $\C^2$.

\begin{prop}[Local mixed model]\label{prop:local-model-mixed-definition}
  The formal local Hamiltonian data used here define a closed mixed
  holomorphic-topological BV sector and a compatible cyclic open brane BV
  theory. The constructed closed-open operation is the degree-zero Hamiltonian
  boundary evaluation. The full Poisson factorization-center morphism is
  Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}, not part of this proposition.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  On product opens $D\times B$ in the completed formal neighbourhood of
  $\R^2\times\{p\}\subset\R^2\times\C^2$, the closed fields are
  $$\mc E_{\mathrm{cl}}(D\times B)=
    \Omega^*(D)\widehat{\otimes}\Omega^{0,*}(B)\widehat{\otimes}
    \bigl(\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]\oplus
    \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]\bigr).$$
  Degreewise polynomial calculations use the dense subspace
  $\bar A=\C[z_1,z_2]/\C\cdot1$. The differential is
  $D=d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2}$, so $Q_0=0$ in
  Definition~\ref{def:local-th-string}. The BV pairing is the local pairing on
  compactly supported fields, obtained by multiplying the form components,
  integrating over $D\times B$ against $dz_1\,dz_2$, and using the continuous
  evaluation pairing
  $\widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}\otimes
  \widehat{\mathfrak h}\to\C$. If
  $\alpha\in\Omega^p\widehat{\otimes}\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]$ and
  $\beta\in\Omega^q\widehat{\otimes}
  \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]$, then
  $|\alpha|=p-1$ and $|\beta|=q-2$; the top-form condition $p+q=4$ makes the
  pairing degree $-1$.

  The free quadratic term
  $$S_{\mathrm{free}}=\int_{D\times B}
    \left\langle\beta,D\alpha\right\rangle dz_1\,dz_2$$
  is the BV Hamiltonian for the differential $D$. The interaction in
  Definition~\ref{def:local-th-string} is only
  $$I_{\mathrm{BF}}=\frac12\int_{D\times B}
    \left\langle\beta,\{\alpha,\alpha\}\right\rangle dz_1\,dz_2.$$
  The total BF action is $S_{\mathrm{free}}+I_{\mathrm{BF}}$.
  The Poisson bracket on $\bar A$ is the holomorphic bracket determined by
  $dz_1\wedge dz_2$. Since $D$ is a derivation of this bracket and the bracket
  satisfies Jacobi,
  $$D I_{\mathrm{BF}}+\frac12\{I_{\mathrm{BF}},I_{\mathrm{BF}}\}=0,$$
  so the total BF action satisfies the classical master equation without
  double-counting the free differential.

  Mixed locality is the Cartan homotopy calculation on the interacting
  observables. For a constant vector
  field $v$ in the $\R^2$ direction, $[D,\iota_v]=\mathcal L_v$; for an
  anti-holomorphic coordinate vector field $\partial/\partial\bar z_i$,
  $[D,\iota_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}]
  =\mathcal L_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}$. The interaction is built from the
  de Rham wedge product and holomorphic polydifferential operators, so the
  contractions are derivations of the local observable algebra and commute with
  $\{I_{\mathrm{BF}},-\}$ up to the displayed Lie derivative. Thus
  $[Q_{\mathrm{obs}},\iota_v]=\mathcal L_v$ and
  $[Q_{\mathrm{obs}},\iota_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}]
  =\mathcal L_{\partial/\partial\bar z_i}$ on local observables. The de Rham
  Poincare lemma in the $D$ directions gives the quasi-isomorphism for small
  disk inclusions, and the Dolbeault Poincare lemma gives the holomorphic
  dependence in the $B$ direction.

  The brane is $N\times Z=\R\times\{p\}$, with $Z$ understood as the formal
  holomorphic neighbourhood at $p$. Its open fields are
  $$\Omega^*(\R)\otimes
    \Ext^*_{\C[z_1,z_2]}(\mc O_p,\mc O_p)\otimes\lie{gl}_N[1],$$
  and Proposition~\ref{prop:skyscraper-ext} identifies the Ext algebra with
  $\Lambda(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2)$. This is the derived
  $\RHom_Y(\mc O_p,\mc O_p)$ allowed in Definition~\ref{def:local-th-string},
  not an ordinary Dolbeault algebra on the point. The trace on $\lie{gl}_N$ and
  the Berezin trace on this exterior algebra give the cyclic open string field
  theory. Construction~\ref{constr:boundary-evaluation} and
  Theorem~\ref{thm:bulk-boundary} construct the degree-zero Hamiltonian
  boundary component and prove its bracket compatibility. The full
  Poisson factorization-center closed-open map is Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center},
  not a theorem proved here.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Open mixed brane states}
  The open string states are the tensor product of the topological brane
  direction and the formal holomorphic normal direction.

  \begin{itemize}
    \item \textit{Topological factor.} In the exact self-Floer model for
      the graded, spin zero-section $\R\subset T^*\R\cong\R^2$, we use the
      local exact Fukaya model near a compact interval in the brane. A small
