      compactly supported Hamiltonian perturbation identifies $CF^*(\R,\R)$
      with the Morse complex on that interval, and passage to local operators
      in the interior is represented by the de Rham complex $\Omega^*(\R)$
      with compactly supported variations. No wrapped generators at infinity
      are included in this local model.
    \item \textit{Holomorphic factor.} Put affine coordinates at $p=0$ and write
      $R=\C[z_1,z_2]$, $\mathfrak m=(z_1,z_2)$, and $\mc{O}_p=R/\mathfrak m$.
      The skyscraper sheaf has open string states
      $$\Ext^*_R(R/\mathfrak m,R/\mathfrak m),$$
      computed in Proposition~\ref{prop:skyscraper-ext}.
  \end{itemize}

\begin{prop}[Affine skyscraper self-Ext]\label{prop:skyscraper-ext}
  Let $R=\C[z_1,z_2]$, $\mathfrak m=(z_1,z_2)$, and $k=R/\mathfrak m$. Then
  the Yoneda algebra of the skyscraper sheaf at the origin is
  $$\Ext^*_R(k,k)\cong\Lambda_{\C}(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2),$$
  where $|\varepsilon_i|=1$. In particular this is the free
  graded-commutative algebra on two odd generators.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  The pair $(z_1,z_2)$ is a regular sequence in the polynomial ring $R$, so the
  affine Koszul complex
  $$K=\bigl(0\to R\,e_{12}\xrightarrow{d_2}R\,e_1\oplus R\,e_2
        \xrightarrow{d_1}R\to0\bigr)$$
  is a free resolution of $k$, with
  $$d_1(ae_1+be_2)=az_1+bz_2,\qquad
    d_2(e_{12})=z_2e_1-z_1e_2.$$
  Applying $\Hom_R(-,k)$ gives
  $$0\to k\xrightarrow{0}k\,\varepsilon_1\oplus k\,\varepsilon_2
    \xrightarrow{0}k\,\varepsilon_{12}\to0,$$
  because $z_1$ and $z_2$ act by zero on $k$. Hence the graded vector space of
  Ext groups is $k$ in degree $0$, $k\varepsilon_1\oplus k\varepsilon_2$ in
  degree $1$, and $k\varepsilon_{12}$ in degree $2$.

  The product is the Yoneda product. The Koszul resolution is the exterior
  dg-algebra $R\otimes\Lambda(e_1,e_2)$ with $d(e_i)=z_i$; its diagonal sends
  $e_i$ to $e_i\otimes1+1\otimes e_i$. Dualising this diagonal gives
  $\varepsilon_i^2=0$ and
  $\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2=-\varepsilon_2\varepsilon_1$, while
  $\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$ spans the top Ext group. Thus the Yoneda
  algebra is $\Lambda_{\C}(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2)$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Open mixed brane field theory}

The open theory is the minimal local field theory which remembers the brane's two
normal holomorphic directions. The two Ext generators are odd because they are
derived normal directions of a point brane; after the BV shift their ghost-zero
coefficients become the two ordinary matrix coordinates $\phi_1,\phi_2$. The
one-form coefficient is the gauge field $A$ along the brane. Thus the formal
Chern-Simons action is the mechanism which turns the Ext algebra into
first-order matrix mechanics.

The total space of fields (in the Batalin-Vilkovisky formalism) is
$$\alpha \in \Omega^*(\R)\otimes\Lambda(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2)
  \otimes \lie{gl}_N[1]$$
with action
$$S(\alpha)=\int_{\R \times \C^{0|2}}
  \frac{1}{2}\,\mathrm{Tr}(\alpha\, d\alpha)
  + \frac{1}{3}\,\mathrm{Tr}\,\alpha^3.$$
Here $d = d_{\mathrm{dR}}$; the Ext algebra
$\Lambda(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2)$ has zero differential. The integral
over $\C^{0|2}$ is the Berezin integral $\int d\varepsilon_1\,d\varepsilon_2$,
which picks out the top component in the odd directions.

The cyclic trace is
$$\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{open}}(\eta\otimes u\otimes M)
  =\int_\R \eta\,[\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2]u\,
    \operatorname{Tr}_N(M),$$
where $[\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2]u$ denotes the coefficient of the top Ext
class. The top Ext class is the residue orientation dual to
$dz_1\wedge dz_2$. The de Rham integral has degree $-1$ and the Ext residue has
degree $-2$; after the field shift by $[1]$, the induced BV pairing has degree
$-1$.

\begin{constr}[The open field from the Ext basis]\label{constr:open-field-basis}
  Write $\varepsilon_{12}=\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$. Before imposing ghost
  number, an open field is a finite sum
  $$\alpha=a_0+a_1\varepsilon_1+a_2\varepsilon_2+a_{12}\varepsilon_{12},$$
  where each $a_I$ is a de Rham form on $\R$ with values in $\lie{gl}_N$,
  shifted by $[1]$. The ghost-number-zero components are exactly
  $$A\in\Omega^1(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N,\qquad
    \phi_1,\phi_2\in\Omega^0(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N,$$
  and they appear as
  $$\alpha_0=A+\phi_1\varepsilon_1+\phi_2\varepsilon_2.$$
  The Berezin integral kills every monomial except the coefficient of
  $\varepsilon_{12}$, so every term in the ghost-zero action is obtained by
  multiplying the displayed three summands and keeping exactly one real
  one-form and exactly the product $\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$.
\end{constr}

\begin{rmk}
  The shift $[1]$ acts on the total cohomological degree: a form of de Rham
  degree $p$ and Grassmann degree $q$ has total degree $p+q$, which after the
  shift sits in ghost number $p+q-1$. In particular, the 1-form component of
  $\alpha$ (de Rham degree 1, Grassmann degree 0) sits in ghost number 0 and
  is the bosonic gauge field. The scalar components proportional to
  $\varepsilon_i$ (de Rham degree 0, Grassmann degree 1) also sit in ghost
  number 0 and represent the motion of the brane in the two normal directions.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection{Ghost-zero open field content}
  The ghost-number-zero part of the BV field is
  $$\alpha_0=A+\phi_1\varepsilon_1+\phi_2\varepsilon_2,$$
  where $A\in\Omega^1(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N$ and
  $\phi_i\in\Omega^0(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N$.

  \begin{lem}\label{lem:open-action-reduction}
    With the Berezin convention
    $\int_{\C^{0|2}}\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2=1$, the restriction of the
    BV action to $\alpha_0$ is, up to a boundary term on $\R$,
    $$S(\alpha_0)=\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2
      +A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr).$$
  \end{lem}

  \begin{proof}
    Only monomials containing one real one-form and the factor
    $\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$ survive the integration over
    $\R\times\C^{0|2}$. In the quadratic term this leaves
    $$\frac12\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2-\phi_2\,d\phi_1\bigr),$$
    where the sign is the Koszul sign from interchanging the two odd
    generators. Since
    $d\,\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\phi_2)=\mathrm{Tr}(d\phi_1\,\phi_2+\phi_1\,d\phi_2)$,
    the second summand differs from $\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2)$ by an exact
    one-form. In the cubic term the six orderings of
    $A,\phi_1\varepsilon_1,\phi_2\varepsilon_2$ reduce by cyclicity of the trace
    and the odd relation $\varepsilon_2\varepsilon_1=-\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$
    to
    $$3\,\mathrm{Tr}(A\phi_1\phi_2-A\phi_2\phi_1).$$
    The coefficient $\frac13$ in the Chern-Simons action therefore gives exactly
    $\mathrm{Tr}(A[\phi_1,\phi_2])$.
  \end{proof}

\begin{lem}[Dirac reduction of the probe phase space]\label{lem:dirac-probe-reduction}
  Let
  $$\mathcal P_N=\lie{gl}_N\oplus\lie{gl}_N$$
  with coordinates $(\phi_1,\phi_2)$ and symplectic form
  $$\Omega_N=\mathrm{Tr}(d\phi_1\wedge d\phi_2).$$
  With the convention $\iota_{X_f}\Omega_N=-df$, simultaneous conjugation by
  $\lie{gl}_N$ is Hamiltonian with moment map components
  $$\mu_\epsilon=-\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\epsilon[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr),
    \qquad \epsilon\in\lie{gl}_N.$$
  They satisfy the first-class identity
  $$\{\mu_\epsilon,\mu_\eta\}=\mu_{[\epsilon,\eta]}.$$
  The action of Lemma~\ref{lem:open-action-reduction} is the corresponding
  Dirac first-order action
  $$\int_\R \mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2)-\mu_A,$$
  and varying $A$ imposes the constrained phase space
  $$\mu^{-1}(0)/GL_N=\{[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0\}/GL_N.$$
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  The symplectic form gives
  $$\{(\phi_1)^i{}_j,(\phi_2)^k{}_l\}=\delta^i_l\delta^k_j.$$
  For $v_\epsilon(\phi_i)=[\epsilon,\phi_i]$, cyclicity of the trace gives
  $$d\mu_\epsilon(\delta\phi_1,\delta\phi_2)
    =-\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\epsilon([\delta\phi_1,\phi_2]
      +[\phi_1,\delta\phi_2])\bigr)
    =-\Omega_N(v_\epsilon,(\delta\phi_1,\delta\phi_2)).$$
  Thus $X_{\mu_\epsilon}=v_\epsilon$. The moment-map bracket is therefore the
  infinitesimal equivariance identity
  $\{\mu_\epsilon,\mu_\eta\}=\mu_{[\epsilon,\eta]}$. Substituting
  $\epsilon=A(t)$ gives
  $$\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2)-\mu_A
    =\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2+A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr),$$
  and the $A$-equation is $[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[Classical BV truncation]\label{prop:open-bv-truncation}
  The subspace of ghost-number-zero fields
  $$\alpha_0=A+\phi_1\varepsilon_1+\phi_2\varepsilon_2$$
  with all nonzero ghost-number components set to zero is a consistent
  classical truncation of the open BV theory. The induced classical action is
  the first-order gauged matrix model of Lemma~\ref{lem:open-action-reduction}.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  Decompose the BV field as $\alpha=\sum_r\alpha^{(r)}$ by ghost number. The
  differential $d_{\R}$ and the product on
  $\Lambda(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2)\otimes\lie{gl}_N$ preserve total degree,
  and the BV action has ghost number zero. Hence every monomial in the
  Euler-Lagrange expression for a component of ghost number $r\neq0$ contains
  at least one field component of nonzero ghost number when evaluated at
  $\alpha=\alpha_0$. Setting all such components to zero therefore makes the
  discarded equations vanish. The remaining equation is exactly the variation
  of $S(\alpha_0)$, computed in Lemma~\ref{lem:open-action-reduction}.

  Concretely, the full Euler-Lagrange expression is the curvature
  $$F(\alpha)=d\alpha+\alpha^2.$$
  For $\alpha_0=A+\phi_1\varepsilon_1+\phi_2\varepsilon_2$ on a line,
  \begin{align*}
  F(\alpha_0)
    &=(d\phi_1+[A,\phi_1])\varepsilon_1
      +(d\phi_2+[A,\phi_2])\varepsilon_2
      +[\phi_1,\phi_2]\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2.
  \end{align*}
  The BV pairing keeps exactly real-form degree one and
  $\varepsilon_1\varepsilon_2$. Hence the displayed three components pair exactly
  with the variations of $A,\phi_2,\phi_1$ respectively, while variations of
  nonzero ghost number see complementary curvature components that are zero for
  $\alpha_0$ by real-form degree or $\varepsilon$-degree. This is a physical
  ghost-zero truncation; the residual ordinary $GL_N$ gauge symmetry remains.
\end{proof}

  The ghost-number-zero truncation of the BV master action is closed under the
  classical equations and gives a quantum-mechanical system with a connection
  form
  $$A \in \Omega^1(\R)\otimes \lie{gl}_N,$$
  two adjoint scalars
  $$\phi_1,\phi_2 \in \Omega^0(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N,$$
  and action
  $$S = \int_\R \mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2
    + A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr).$$
  This action is invariant under
  $$\delta_{\varepsilon}\phi_i=[\varepsilon,\phi_i],\qquad
    \delta_{\varepsilon}A=d\varepsilon+[A,\varepsilon],$$
  for $\varepsilon\in\Omega^0(\R)\otimes\lie{gl}_N$. Indeed the variation of
  $\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1d\phi_2)$ containing $d\varepsilon$ is
  $-\mathrm{Tr}(d\varepsilon[\phi_1,\phi_2])$, and this cancels the
  $d\varepsilon$ variation of $\mathrm{Tr}(A[\phi_1,\phi_2])$; the remaining
  terms cancel by invariance of the trace pairing.

\begin{rmk}
  The same local open model is obtained from the Calabi-Yau $2$ point-brane
  residue calculation by tensoring the skyscraper object with $\C^N$ and
  passing to endomorphisms. This is a local CY$_2$ pairing statement, not a
  global CY-to-chiral input. Global transfer would require the corresponding
  negative cyclic Calabi-Yau class, framing data, and descent; none of that is
  used in the proof below.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}
  In AKSZ language this is the one-dimensional gauged sigma model with
  Hamiltonian target $\lie{gl}_N\oplus\lie{gl}_N$ and symplectic potential
  $\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2)$. We use the resulting Poisson bivector
  $$\Pi=\sum_{i,j}\frac{\partial}{\partial(\phi_1)^i{}_j}
    \wedge\frac{\partial}{\partial(\phi_2)^j{}_i},$$
  so $\{(\phi_1)^i{}_j,(\phi_2)^k{}_l\}=\delta^i_l\delta^k_j$. Equivalently,
  with the convention $\iota_{X_f}\omega=-df$ used throughout, the symplectic
  form is $\mathrm{Tr}(d\phi_1\wedge d\phi_2)$. For
  $\epsilon\in\lie{gl}_N$, the Hamiltonian
  $$\mu_\epsilon=-\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\epsilon[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr)$$
  generates $\delta_\epsilon\phi_i=[\epsilon,\phi_i]$. Its zero locus is the
  commuting-pair equation $[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$, and the classical reduced phase
  space is the stack of commuting pairs of matrices modulo conjugation.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}
  Equivalently, take Chern-Simons theory on $\R\times T^2$ and restrict to the
  harmonic forms $1,\eta_1,\eta_2,\eta_1\eta_2$ on $T^2$. Writing
  $A_{3d}=A_t\,dt+\phi_1\eta_1+\phi_2\eta_2$ and integrating over $T^2$
  gives the same action; the odd variables $\varepsilon_i$ represent the
  degree-one cohomology classes $\eta_i$.
\end{rmk}

\subsection{Closed mixed Hamiltonian sector}

The closed field is the infinitesimal geometry of the formal normal surface.
Because the surface is holomorphic symplectic, an infinitesimal canonical
transformation is a Hamiltonian function modulo constants. The BF partner is
the cotangent variable which makes the theory local and BV. This is the closed
counterpart of the open first-order form: both sides are governed by the same
symplectic normal plane.

The closed sector used here is a mixed field theory, not a tensor product of
two independent closed-string state spaces. Its fields have a topological de
Rham factor along $\R^2$ and a holomorphic Dolbeault factor along $\C^2$:
$$\Omega^*(\R^2)\widehat{\otimes}\Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)
  \widehat{\otimes}\bigl(\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]\oplus
  \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]\bigr).$$
The coefficient $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$ is the completed Lie algebra of
nonconstant Hamiltonian functions on the formal holomorphic symplectic disk.
The continuous dual copy
$\widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]$ is the cotangent/BF field.
Thus the closed theory is the Hamiltonian Kodaira-Spencer/BF sector of the mixed
holomorphic-topological string.

\begin{rmk}
  The original BCOV analysis \cite{bcov} is written for Calabi-Yau threefolds;
  the higher-genus B-model on Calabi--Yau manifolds is taken up at the
  quantum level in \cite{costello-li}.
  On a holomorphic symplectic surface the natural local cotangent theory is the
  BF theory for the dg Lie algebra of Hamiltonian vector fields. The
  holomorphic symplectic form supplies the Poisson bracket, while the
  holomorphic volume form supplies the divergence operator on polyvectors.
\end{rmk}

We consider the space of polyvector fields
$$\mathbf{PV}^{*,*}(\C^2) \cong \Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)[\partial_{z_1},\partial_{z_2}]$$
where $\partial_{z_i}$ are odd generators of poly-vector degree 1 (corresponding
to the two holomorphic vector fields on $\C^2$). The operator
$$\partial: \mathbf{PV}^{i,*} \to \mathbf{PV}^{i-1,*}$$
is the divergence operator determined by the holomorphic volume form
$\Omega=dz_1\wedge dz_2$:
$$\partial_{\Omega}=\iota_{\Omega}^{-1}\circ\partial_{\mathrm{hol}}\circ
  \iota_{\Omega},\qquad
  \iota_{\Omega}:\mathbf{PV}^{i,*}\xrightarrow{\sim}\Omega^{2-i,*}.$$
Thus for $X=a_1\partial_{z_1}+a_2\partial_{z_2}$,
$$\partial_{\Omega}X=(\partial_{z_1}a_1+\partial_{z_2}a_2),$$
while $\partial_{\Omega}$ vanishes on functions.

We work in the formal polynomial local model at $0\in\C^2$, so Dolbeault
cohomology is represented by holomorphic Taylor polynomials. Here
$\partial_{\Omega}$ is the divergence constraint selecting the Hamiltonian BF
sector. The kinematic differential of the closed theory below is
$D=d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2}$. Thus the Poincare lemma identifies
divergence-free vector fields with Hamiltonian potentials. The quotient by
$\partial_{\Omega}$-exact Hamiltonians is absent. Analysing degree by
degree:
\begin{itemize}
  \item $\mathbf{PV}^{0,*}(\C^2) = \Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)\subset\Ker\partial$
    trivially.
  \item $\mathbf{PV}^{1,*}(\C^2)\cong\Omega^{1,*}(\C^2)$ via
    $\iota_{(-)}\omega$. Under this identification, with the Hamiltonian
    convention $\iota_{X_f}\omega=-df$ used below,
    $\Ker\partial_{\Omega}$ is the space of closed holomorphic one-forms.
    Lemma~\ref{lem:polynomial-poincare} identifies these with $df$, uniquely
    modulo constants.
  \item The constant Hamiltonians act trivially, since their Hamiltonian vector
    fields vanish. We therefore use the reduced polynomial algebra
    $$\bar A=\C[z_1,z_2]/\C\cdot1$$
    for nontrivial Hamiltonian fields.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lem}[Polynomial Poincare primitive]\label{lem:polynomial-poincare}
  Let
  $$\theta=a(z_1,z_2)\,dz_1+b(z_1,z_2)\,dz_2$$
  be a polynomial one-form on $\C^2$. If
  $\partial_{z_2}a=\partial_{z_1}b$, then there is a polynomial
  $f\in\C[z_1,z_2]$, unique modulo constants, such that $\theta=df$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  Define
  $$f(z_1,z_2)=\int_0^1
    \bigl(z_1a(tz_1,tz_2)+z_2b(tz_1,tz_2)\bigr)\,dt.$$
  Since $a$ and $b$ are polynomials, the integral is termwise division of each
  homogeneous term by its degree plus one, hence $f$ is polynomial. Differentiate
  under the integral sign. Closedness says
  $\partial_{z_2}a=\partial_{z_1}b$, so
  \begin{align*}
  \partial_{z_1}f
    &=\int_0^1\bigl(a(tz)+tz_1\partial_{z_1}a(tz)
       +tz_2\partial_{z_1}b(tz)\bigr)\,dt\\
    &=\int_0^1\bigl(a(tz)+t z_1\partial_{z_1}a(tz)
       +t z_2\partial_{z_2}a(tz)\bigr)\,dt\\
    &=\int_0^1\frac{d}{dt}\bigl(t\,a(tz)\bigr)\,dt
      =a(z).
  \end{align*}
  The same calculation, with $a$ and $b$ interchanged, gives
  $\partial_{z_2}f=b(z)$. Therefore $df=\theta$.
  If $df=dg$, then $d(f-g)=0$, hence $f-g$ is constant.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[Hamiltonian polyvector reduction]\label{prop:hamiltonian-polyvector-reduction}
  In the formal polynomial model on $(\C^2,\omega=dz_1\wedge dz_2)$, the
  divergence-closed polyvector-one fields reduce to Hamiltonian vector fields:
  $$\Ker(\partial_{\Omega}:\mathbf{PV}^{1}\to\mathbf{PV}^{0})
    \cong \{df:f\in\C[z_1,z_2]\}
    \cong \bar A.$$
  Under the convention
  $$X_f=(\partial_{z_1}f)\partial_{z_2}
    -(\partial_{z_2}f)\partial_{z_1},\qquad \iota_{X_f}\omega=-df,$$
  the commutator of vector fields is
  $$[X_f,X_g]=X_{\{f,g\}_{\bar A}}.$$
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  Let $X=a_1\partial_{z_1}+a_2\partial_{z_2}$. The divergence operator is
  $\partial_{\Omega}X=\partial_{z_1}a_1+\partial_{z_2}a_2$. Contracting with
  $\omega$ gives
  $$\iota_X\omega=a_1\,dz_2-a_2\,dz_1.$$
  The equation $\partial_{\Omega}X=0$ is exactly the closedness of this
  one-form:
  $$d(\iota_X\omega)
    =(\partial_{z_1}a_1+\partial_{z_2}a_2)\,dz_1\wedge dz_2=0.$$
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:polynomial-poincare}, there is a polynomial $f$, unique
  modulo constants, such that $\iota_X\omega=-df$. Therefore
  $$a_1=-\partial_{z_2}f,\qquad a_2=\partial_{z_1}f,$$
  so $X=X_f$. Constants are exactly the kernel of $f\mapsto X_f$, giving
  $\bar A$.

  Finally, for any polynomial $h$,
  \begin{align*}
  [X_f,X_g](h)
    &=\{f,\{g,h\}\}-\{g,\{f,h\}\}\\
    &=\{\{f,g\},h\}
  \end{align*}
  by the Jacobi identity for the constant Poisson bracket. Thus
  $[X_f,X_g]=X_{\{f,g\}}$, and projecting constants gives the bracket on
  $\bar A$.
\end{proof}

For the Hamiltonian sector of the closed mixed field theory we replace
$\Ker\partial$ (on poly-1-vectors) by the Dolbeault-valued Hamiltonian vector
fields:
$$\Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)\text{-valued Hamiltonian vector fields},$$
i.e.\ sections of $\Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)$ identified with Hamiltonian vector
fields via the symplectic form $\omega = dz_1\wedge dz_2$. Concretely, a
section $f\in\Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)$ corresponds to the Hamiltonian vector field
$X_f=\{f,-\}_\omega$, where
$$\{f,g\}_\omega=
  \partial_{z_1}f\,\partial_{z_2}g-\partial_{z_2}f\,\partial_{z_1}g.$$
With this convention
$$X_f=(\partial_{z_1}f)\partial_{z_2}
  -(\partial_{z_2}f)\partial_{z_1},\qquad \iota_{X_f}\omega=-df.$$

\begin{rmk}
  The replacement is the elementary statement
  of Proposition~\ref{prop:hamiltonian-polyvector-reduction}. Constants are
  removed because $X_f=0$ exactly when $f$ is constant.
\end{rmk}

\subsection{Hamiltonian BF closed sector}

\subsubsection{The Action Functional}

Let
$$D=d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2}.$$
Write
$$\alpha\in\Omega^*(\R^2)\,\hat{\otimes}\,\Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)
  \widehat{\otimes}\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]$$
for the Hamiltonian connection field and
$$\beta\in\Omega^*(\R^2)\,\hat{\otimes}\,\Omega^{0,*}(\C^2)
  \widehat{\otimes}\widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]$$
for its cotangent field. The bracket on form-valued Hamiltonians is obtained
by wedging the form parts and taking the Poisson bracket of the Hamiltonian
parts with the tensor-product Koszul sign:
$$[\eta\otimes f,\theta\otimes g]
  =(-1)^{|f||\theta|}(\eta\wedge\theta)\otimes\{f,g\},$$
for homogeneous form $\eta,\theta$ and homogeneous Hamiltonian coefficients
$f,g$. In the ghost-zero Hamiltonian calculations used below the coefficients
are even, so this sign is $+1$. The action is
$$S=\int_{\R^2\times\C^2}\Bigl\langle\beta,\,
  D\alpha+\frac12\{\alpha,\alpha\}\Bigr\rangle\,dz_1\,dz_2.$$
The pairing is the continuous evaluation pairing between
$\widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}$ and $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$.
The dense polynomial submodel replaces these by $\bar A^\vee$ and $\bar A$ in
each finite degree.
For ghost-number-zero fields, $\alpha$ has total real/Dolbeault form degree
$1$ and $\beta$ has total degree $2$. Hence
$\beta\wedge D\alpha$ and $\beta\wedge\{\alpha,\alpha\}$ have total
real/Dolbeault degree $4$; multiplying by $dz_1\wedge dz_2$ gives a top real
degree $6$ form on $\R^2\times\C^2$.

\begin{rmk}
  The open mixed brane system lives on the brane line. The closed Hamiltonian
  BF theory lives on the full mixed space-time $\R^2\times\C^2$.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection{Classical field content}

This theory is closely related to a 4-dimensional BF theory: $\beta$ plays the
role of the $B$-field (Lagrange multiplier) and the equations of motion of
$\beta$ enforce $F_\alpha = 0$, where
$$F_\alpha = D\alpha + \tfrac{1}{2}\{\alpha,\alpha\}$$
is the ``curvature'' of $\alpha$ (viewed as a connection on a bundle of
holomorphic-symplectic surfaces over $\R^2$).

Consider the space-time $\R^2_{x_i}\times\C^2_{z_i}$. The ghost-number-zero
components of $\alpha$ and $\beta$ are:
$$\alpha = \alpha_{x_i}\,dx_i + \alpha_{\bar z_j}\,d\bar z_j,\qquad
  \beta = \beta_{x_1 x_2}\,dx_1\,dx_2 + \beta_{x_i\bar z_j}\,dx_i\,d\bar z_j
  + \beta_{\bar z_1\bar z_2}\,d\bar z_1\,d\bar z_2.$$
Here the coefficients of $\alpha$ are Hamiltonian functions modulo constants.
The gauge symmetries are the BF-type transformations
$$\delta_{\varepsilon}\alpha=D\varepsilon+\{\alpha,\varepsilon\},\qquad
  \delta_{\varepsilon}\beta=\operatorname{ad}^{\vee}_{\varepsilon}\beta,$$
and
$$\delta_{\lambda}\alpha=0,\qquad
  \delta_{\lambda}\beta=D_{\alpha}\lambda,$$
where $D_{\alpha}=D+\{\alpha,-\}$ and $\lambda$ is a one-form valued in
$\bar A^{\vee}$. The second symmetry is reducible on shell: if
$\lambda=D_{\alpha}\mu$, then
$D_{\alpha}\lambda=D_{\alpha}^2\mu=\{F_{\alpha},\mu\}$, which vanishes when
$F_{\alpha}=0$.

Analysing $\alpha$ as a Hamiltonian function on $\C^2$: the component
$\alpha_{\bar z_j}d\bar z_j$ is the Hamiltonian potential whose vector field
$X_{\alpha_{\bar z_j}}d\bar z_j$ is the Beltrami differential encoding a
deformation of the complex structure of $\C^2$; the component
$\alpha_{x_i}dx_i$ similarly defines a connection on $\R^2$ valued in
Hamiltonian vector fields on $\C^2$, encoding a bundle of $\C^2$s over
$\R^2$. Together, the
equation of motion $F_\alpha=0$ says this data constitutes an integrable
deformation of complex structure with flat holonomy. The field $\beta$ appears
linearly in the action and enforces exactly this equation.

\begin{rmk}
  This is entirely analogous to BF theory, where $B$ is a Lagrange multiplier
  enforcing $F_A=0$, and the phase space is $T^*\mathcal{M}_{\mathrm{flat}}$.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection{Phase Space}
As an optional analytic model for propagators, formally compactify one real
direction and put the perturbative local model on
$\R\times S^1\times Y_{\mathrm{hol}}$, where $Y_{\mathrm{hol}}$ is holomorphic
symplectic and the calculation is completed at the trivial solution. This is a
compactified avatar of the formal local model, not a change of notation for the
product $X=M\times Y$ used above. The equations of motion $F_\alpha=0$ cut
out the Maurer-Cartan moduli problem for Hamiltonian vector fields on
$S^1\times Y_{\mathrm{hol}}$. Fix the analytic package of
Problem~\ref{prob:analytic-graph-realization} in this compact or formal
setting: elliptic complex, brane-defect or boundary condition, gauge fixing,
propagator, renormalization scheme, and anomaly cancellation. The perturbative
phase space
is the derived cotangent stack
$$T^*_{\mathrm{der}}\mathrm{MC}\bigl(\Omega^*(S^1)\widehat{\otimes}
  \Omega^{0,*}(Y_{\mathrm{hol}},\mathrm{Ham}(Y_{\mathrm{hol}})),D,\{-,-\}\bigr).$$
After passing to the underived tangent space at the trivial solution this
reduces to the ordinary cotangent bundle of the linearized deformation complex.

\subsection{Closed-open brane coupling}

This is the point at which the physical picture becomes a formula. A closed
Hamiltonian is not observed by the brane as an abstract vector field; it is
observed by evaluating it on the brane's matrix-valued normal coordinates and
taking the trace over Chan-Paton indices.

The local classical bulk-boundary operation is the Hamiltonian shadow of the
desired closed-open morphism: evaluate a closed Hamiltonian on the brane normal
fields. If the brane lies along $x_1$ and the closed field is
$dx_1\,z_1^k z_2^l$, the local boundary functional is
$$\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2+A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr)
  + \int_\R dx_1\,\mathrm{Tr}\,\phi_1^k\phi_2^l.$$
This is a statement inside the formal local algebraic model: the closed
Hamiltonian is pulled back along the matrix-valued normal coordinate map
$z_i\mapsto\phi_i$ and then traced.
Construction~\ref{constr:boundary-evaluation} is the algebraic form of this
bulk-to-boundary prescription. Theorem~\ref{thm:bulk-boundary} below proves
that the resulting Hamiltonian evaluation preserves the classical bracket. This
is the degree-zero Hamiltonian component expected from a full closed-open map;
the full Poisson factorization-center morphism is not constructed here.

\begin{constr}[Reduced line-defect current kernel]\label{constr:reduced-line-defect-current-kernel}
  Let
  $$X=\R^2_{\mathrm{top}}\times\C^2_{\mathrm{hol}},\qquad
    L=\R_{x_1}\times\{x_2=0\}\times\{p\}\subset X,$$
  and let $i:L\hookrightarrow X$ be the inclusion. This is a line defect, not
  a spacetime boundary. In the reduced formal local model, a test density
  $a(t)\,dt$ on $L$ defines the defect-supported current $i_*(a(t)\,dt)$,
  locally written as $a(x_1)\delta(x_2)\delta_p\,dx_1dx_2$ together with the
  formal holomorphic delta-current at $p$.

  The degree-zero Hamiltonian part of the reduced PBW/Rees defect-current
  vertex is
  $$K_L^{\mathrm{cl}}(a\otimes f)
    =\int_L a(t)\,
      \overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1(t),\phi_2(t))}\,dt,
    \qquad f\in\bar A.$$
  For the cotangent principal-part source, the reduced vertex sends
  $$B\otimes\rho[1]\longmapsto\Theta_\rho(B),\qquad
    B\in\mathcal D'_c(L),\quad \rho\in\mc P,$$
  using Theorem~\ref{prop:reduced-principal-part-boundary-current}. These
  formulas define a reduced PBW/Rees defect-current kernel. They are not a
  cochain-level map from closed CE observables, and they are not yet the
  quantum Costello brane-defect kernel: the Ward identity, anomaly cancellation,
  finite-scale propagator, and quantum moment-map compatibility remain separate
  obligations.
\end{constr}

\begin{rmk}
  Geometrically, specifying a closed Hamiltonian field on $\C^2$ amounts to
  equipping $\C^2$ with a connection, so that the brane can parallel-transport
  its internal degrees of freedom as it moves along $\R$.
\end{rmk}

\begin{constr}[Interval Hamiltonian and factorization algebras]\label{constr:interval-fact-algebras}
  For an interval $I\subset\R$, define
  \begin{align*}
    \mathfrak h_I&=C_c^\infty(I)\widehat\otimes\bar A,\\
    \mathcal P_I&=\mathcal D'_c(I)\widehat\otimes\mc P,\\
    \mathfrak g_I&=\mathfrak h_I\ltimes\mathcal P_I[1],
  \end{align*}
  with brackets
  \begin{align*}
    [a\otimes f,b\otimes g]_{\mathfrak h_I}&=ab\otimes\{f,g\}_{\bar A},\\
    [a\otimes f,B\otimes\rho[1]]_{\mathfrak g_I}&=aB\otimes(f\cdot\rho)[1],\\
    [B\otimes\rho[1],C\otimes\sigma[1]]_{\mathfrak g_I}&=0,
  \end{align*}
  where $aB$ is multiplication of a compactly supported distribution by
  a smooth compactly supported function and
  $f\cdot\rho=\pi_{\mathrm{pp}}\{f,\rho\}$ is the principal-part
  coadjoint action of \ref{prop:principal-part-coadjoint}. Inclusions
  $I'\subset I$ act by extension by zero on test functions and
  distributions; disjoint unions act by sum. This makes
  $I\mapsto\mathfrak h_I,\mathfrak g_I$ cosheaves of (graded) Lie
  algebras on $\R$.

  Define the boundary $P_0$ factorization algebras on $\R$ in the
  formal stable Hamiltonian sector by
  \begin{align*}
    A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I)
      &=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I),\\
    A_\partial^{\mathrm{pp}}(I)
      &=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)\widehat\otimes
        \widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathcal P_I[1]),
  \end{align*}
  with $P_0$ bracket extended as a biderivation from
  \begin{align*}
    \{a\otimes f,b\otimes g\}_{A_\partial}&=ab\otimes\{f,g\}_{\bar A},\\
    \{a\otimes f,B\otimes\rho[1]\}_{A_\partial}
      &=aB\otimes(f\cdot\rho)[1],\\
    \{B\otimes\rho[1],C\otimes\sigma[1]\}_{A_\partial}&=0.
  \end{align*}
  The factorization product on disjoint intervals is the multiplication
  in $\widehat{\mathbf S}$ after extension by zero. These are the
  reduced post-contraction targets for the closed-open
  factorization-center map. The Hamiltonian factor
  $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}$ is the connected component of the formal
  Hamiltonian sector of the open brane factorization algebra; the
  principal-part factor
  $A_\partial^{\mathrm{pp}}/A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}$ is the reduced
  current object of
  \ref{prop:reduced-principal-part-boundary-current}.
\end{constr}

\begin{prop}[Locality of the brane $P_0$ bracket]\label{prop:brane-bracket-locality}
  Let $a\in C_c^\infty(I_1)$, $b\in C_c^\infty(I_2)$ with
  $I_1\cap I_2=\emptyset$. For all $f,g\in\bar A$,
  $$\{B_f(a),B_g(b)\}_{A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}}=0.$$
  In particular, $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}$ has the strict
  factorization product property: the bracket between sections
  supported on disjoint intervals vanishes.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  By \ref{constr:interval-fact-algebras},
  $\{B_f(a),B_g(b)\}=B_{\{f,g\}}(ab)$. The pointwise product
  $ab\equiv 0$ since the supports are disjoint, so
  $B_{\{f,g\}}(ab)=0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}[Locality from the canonical equal-time bracket]\label{rmk:equal-time-locality}
  The locality input is the canonical equal-time bracket of the
  first-order open BV theory:
  $$\{(\phi_1)^i{}_j(t),(\phi_2)^k{}_l(s)\}
    =\delta^i_l\delta^k_j\,\delta(t-s),\qquad
    \{(\phi_a)^i{}_j(t),(\phi_a)^k{}_l(s)\}=0\ \,(a=1,2).$$
  Tracing $f(\phi_1,\phi_2)(t)$ and $g(\phi_1,\phi_2)(s)$, applying the
  Leibniz rule, and integrating against $a(t)b(s)\delta(t-s)$ produces
  exactly the smeared identity
  $\{B_f(a),B_g(b)\}=B_{\{f,g\}}(ab)$. This is the unsmeared content
  packaged in \ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling}; the
  delta-function locality is what produces a strict $P_0$
  factorization algebra rather than a homotopical one.
\end{rmk}

\begin{thm}[Open-closed derived-center factorization equivalence,
Hamiltonian sector]\label{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization}
  Let $\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl,red}}_{\mathrm{open},N}$ be the locally
  constant reduced open-brane factorization algebra of
  \ref{thm:hamiltonian-current-center-lift}. Let
  $\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{closed},H,\mathrm{Ham}}|_{\R\times p}$
  denote the formal classical Hamiltonian-mode subfactorization
  algebra of the cotangent BF theory on the formal neighbourhood of
  $\R\times p$ obtained by restricting to the connected Hamiltonian
  sector (the $\bar A$-modes), before adjoining the cotangent
  generators. Define the interval-wise CE cochain factorization
  algebra by
  $$\mathcal F_{\mathrm{cl}}(I)
    =C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak h_I)
    =\widehat{\mathbf S}\bigl(\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1]\bigr),$$
  with structure maps induced from extension by zero on $C^\infty_c$
  cochain-by-cochain. Then:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item there is a continuous interval-wise morphism of $P_0$
      factorization algebras
      $$\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}:
        \mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{closed},H,\mathrm{Ham}}\big|_{\R\times p}
        \longrightarrow
        \mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}\bigr),$$
      whose underlying CE cochain map on each interval $I$ is given on
      length-one CE coordinates by
      $$(a\otimes f)^\vee[-1]\ \longmapsto\ B_f(a)
        :=\int_I a(t)\,\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1(t),\phi_2(t))}\,dt;$$
    \item this morphism is a quasi-isomorphism in each interval and
      is compatible with extension by zero and disjoint factorization
      products;
    \item the induced equivalence is locally constant in the
      topological direction $\R$ in the sense of
      \cites{costello-gwilliam,costello-gwilliam-vol2} (Lurie,
      \emph{Higher Algebra}, \S 5.5): every inclusion
      $I'\hookrightarrow I$ of nonempty open intervals induces a
      quasi-isomorphism of the structure maps;
    \item the factorization product
      $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I_1)\otimes A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I_2)
        \to A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(V)$ for disjoint
      $I_1\sqcup I_2\subset V$ corresponds under
      $\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}$ to the CE coproduct on the
      closed side induced by extension by zero
      $C_c^\infty(I_j)\hookrightarrow C_c^\infty(V)$;
    \item at the stalk $I\to\{t_0\}$,
      $\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}$ restricts to the stalkwise
      central operation
      $$f\longmapsto L_{B_f}\in\mathrm{Hoch}^0\bigl(A_N^{\mathrm{pt}}\bigr)$$
      of \ref{prop:stalk-central-multiplication}.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Step 1.} Identify the interval-wise central factorization
  algebra. In the formal stable Hamiltonian sector, the boundary
  factorization algebra
  $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I)=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)$
  is graded-commutative, with strict $P_0$ bracket inherited from
  $\mathfrak h_I$ as a biderivation. By the
  Hochschild--Kostant--Rosenberg theorem in the smooth/algebraic
  setting, applied here to the free graded-commutative algebra on the
  Tate vector space $\mathfrak h_I$, the Hochschild cochain complex
  $\mathrm{Hoch}^\bullet\bigl(\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)\bigr)$
  is quasi-isomorphic to the polyvector fields
  $\mathrm{PV}^\bullet\bigl(\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)\bigr)
  =\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)\widehat\otimes
    \widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1])$
  with the Schouten bracket. The locally constant
  factorization-center stalk on the line records exactly the
  Hochschild cochains in the corresponding $E_1$ algebra; for
  graded-commutative algebras this collapses to PV. Restricting to the
  polynomial subalgebra
  $\mathbf S(\mathfrak h_I)\subset\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)$
  and to the constant polyvectors gives the central multiplication
  operations, which are recorded as the length-one CE coordinates dual
  to elements of $\mathfrak h_I$. The bracket of two such cocycles is
  the Schouten bracket on PV restricted to one-vectors, which is the
  Lie bracket of $\mathfrak h_I$.

  \emph{Step 2.} Construct the CE source. By
  \ref{lem:continuous-bar-cobar},
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak h_I)
   =\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1])$,
  and its CE differential is the dual of the Lie bracket of
  $\mathfrak h_I$. The continuous dual
  $\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}$ is computed by the
  residue-Taylor pairing on the $\bar A$ factor and by the
  density-distribution pairing on the $C_c^\infty(I)$ factor: every
  continuous functional on $C_c^\infty(I)$ is a compactly supported
  distribution, and the polynomial subspace
  $\bar A\subset\widehat{\bar A}$ pairs with the discrete dual
  generated by the $\delta_{a,b}$. This gives
  $$\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}
    =\mathcal D'_c(I)\widehat\otimes\bar A^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}.$$

  \emph{Step 3.} Define $\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}(I)$ on
  generators. By \ref{prop:grav-ops}, the closed Hamiltonian
  cotangent BF observables on the formal neighbourhood of
  $\R\times p$ in the Hamiltonian sector are
  $\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1])$,
  with CE differential dual to the Hamiltonian Lie bracket on
  $\mathfrak h_I$. The interval-wise map sends a length-one CE
  coordinate
  $(a\otimes f)^\vee[-1]\in\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1]$
  to the element of the central operations factorization algebra
  given by the multiplication operator
  $$L_{B_f(a)}\in\mathrm{Hoch}^0\bigl(A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I)\bigr)
    \subset\mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}\bigr)(I),$$
  with $B_f(a)$ as displayed. By
  \ref{prop:stalk-central-multiplication}, this operator is closed
  (Hochschild $0$-cocycle on the graded-commutative open stalk).
  Extend $\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}(I)$ as a continuous
  algebra morphism on $\widehat{\mathbf S}$.

  \emph{Step 4.} Verify CE differential compatibility. On length two,
  the CE differential of a generator
  $\xi\in\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1]$ is the dual of the
  Lie bracket on $\mathfrak h_I$. By
  \ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling} (its sharpened form below),
  $$\{L_{B_f(a)},L_{B_g(b)}\}_{A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}}
    =L_{B_{\{f,g\}}(ab)}.$$
  Pulling back through $\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}$ matches
  this with the dual of
  $[a\otimes f,b\otimes g]_{\mathfrak h_I}=ab\otimes\{f,g\}$.
  Inductive extension by length and the biderivation property
  propagates this to all CE lengths.

  \emph{Step 5.} Quasi-isomorphism on each interval. Both sides are
  free graded-commutative algebras on the same continuous Tate vector
  space $\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{I,\mathrm{cont}}[-1]$, with the same CE
  differential induced from the Lie bracket of $\mathfrak h_I$
  (closed side: by definition; brane side: through the HKR
  identification of Step 1 and the Schouten bracket). The map
  respects the symmetric-algebra generators by construction. Thus it
  is an isomorphism of underlying graded vector spaces and
  intertwines the differentials: a quasi-isomorphism, in fact an
  isomorphism, of $P_0$-cdg algebras on each interval.

  \emph{Step 6.} Factorization product compatibility. For disjoint
  $I_1,I_2\subset V$, the CE source extension by zero gives
  $\mathfrak h_{I_1}\oplus\mathfrak h_{I_2}\hookrightarrow\mathfrak h_V$.
  The cobracket on the closed side is the dual of this: it is the
  splitting
  $\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_V^\vee[-1])
   \to\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_{I_1}^\vee[-1])\widehat\otimes
   \widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_{I_2}^\vee[-1])$
  obtained from the dual surjection
  $\mathfrak h_V^\vee\twoheadrightarrow
  \mathfrak h_{I_1}^\vee\oplus\mathfrak h_{I_2}^\vee$. On the brane
  side,
  $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I_1)\otimes A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I_2)
  \to A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(V)$ is the multiplication map under
  the inclusion of
  $\mathfrak h_{I_1}\oplus\mathfrak h_{I_2}\hookrightarrow\mathfrak h_V$.
  By \ref{prop:brane-bracket-locality}, the bracket between the two
  factors vanishes on disjoint supports, so the product is strictly
  multiplicative. The induced map between central-operation
  factorization algebras is the corresponding tensor product of
  multiplication operators. This is exactly the dual of the CE-source
  extension by zero. Therefore the diagram
  $$\begin{array}{ccc}
    \mathcal F_{\mathrm{cl}}(I_1)\otimes\mathcal F_{\mathrm{cl}}(I_2)
      &\xrightarrow{\Phi(I_1)\otimes\Phi(I_2)}
      & \mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}})(I_1)
        \otimes\mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}})(I_2)\\
    \uparrow & & \downarrow\\
    \mathcal F_{\mathrm{cl}}(V)
      &\xrightarrow{\Phi(V)}
      & \mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}})(V)
  \end{array}$$
  commutes after vertical reversal of the left arrow (CE coproduct =
  dual of inclusion).

  \emph{Step 7.} Locally constant structure. By
  \ref{lem:derivative-jets} the de Rham contraction in $t$ kills all
  positive jets in $C^\infty_c(I)$, leaving values at points. The
  translation vector field $\partial_t$ is $Q$-exact through
  $[d_\R,\iota_{\partial_t}]=\partial_t$. Hence the structure maps
  for inclusions of intervals are quasi-isomorphisms on both sides;
  the $E_1$-equivalent associative algebra structure is the
  underlying graded-commutative product on the stalk, equipped with
  the strict $P_0$ bracket of \ref{constr:interval-fact-algebras}.

  \emph{Step 8.} Stalk recovery. As $I$ shrinks to a point
  $t_0\in\R$, $C^\infty_c(I)$ contracts onto evaluation at $t_0$ in
  cohomology (\ref{lem:derivative-jets}). The image of a length-one
  CE coordinate becomes the multiplication operator $L_{B_f}$ at the
  stalk, recovering \ref{prop:stalk-central-multiplication}.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}[Locally constant equivalence and $E_1$-algebra translation]\label{rmk:E1-translation}
  In the locally constant setting on $\R$, factorization algebras are
  equivalent to homotopy associative algebras up to translation
  invariance \cites{costello-gwilliam,costello-gwilliam-vol2} (Lurie,
  \emph{Higher Algebra}, \S 5.5.4). The Hochschild cochain complex of
  the $E_1$ algebra computes the factorization-center stalk. For
  graded-commutative $E_1$ algebras (which the open Hamiltonian stalk
  is, in the reduced model), the Hochschild cochain complex is
  quasi-isomorphic to polyvector fields by HKR, and its strict $P_0$
  subalgebra of multiplication operators with constant differential
  is the polynomial Hamiltonian sector
  $\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)\widehat\otimes
  \widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I^\vee[-1])$. The CE source
  identification of
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization} is exactly the
  closed dual of this PV picture in the connected Hamiltonian sector.
\end{rmk}

For a factorization algebra $\mc A$ on the line, write
$\mathrm Z_{\mathrm{fact}}(\mc A)$ for the factorization algebra of $E_1$
central operations. In the locally constant one-dimensional case its stalk is
the Hochschild cochain complex of the corresponding $E_1$ algebra. The notation
$\mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(\mc A)$ means the same central operations with
the additional compatibility homotopies for the classical Poisson/BV bracket.
The proposition below records the degree-zero current shadow as a
corollary of
\ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization}.

\begin{prop}[Healed Hamiltonian-current central operation]\label{thm:hamiltonian-current-center-lift}
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization} restricted to the
  length-one CE component on each interval recovers the degree-zero
  Hamiltonian current shadow: the assignment
  $$\Phi_{I,N}(a\otimes f)(u)=B_f(a)\cdot u
    =\Bigl(\int_I a(t)\,
      \overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1(t),\phi_2(t))}\,dt\Bigr)u$$
  is a Hochschild $0$-cocycle in $\mathrm Z_{\mathrm{fact}}
  (\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl,red}}_{\mathrm{open},N})(I)$, the assignments
  are compatible with interval inclusions and disjoint factorization
  products, and the induced operations satisfy
  $$\{\Phi(a\otimes f),\Phi(b\otimes g)\}_{\mathrm{open}}
    =\Phi(ab\otimes\{f,g\}_{\bar A}).$$
  The earlier degree-zero current shadow is therefore the length-one
  shadow of the present quasi-isomorphism, not a tautology of graded
  commutativity: its content is the strict $P_0$ identity, which is
  one of the structure equations defining
  $\Phi^{\mathrm{Ham}}_{\mathrm{fact}}$ of
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization}.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  In the reduced open model $Q\phi_1=Q\phi_2=0$. Hence
  $\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$ is $Q$-closed for every
  Hamiltonian $f$, and the compactly supported integral is $Q$-closed.
  Since the reduced open observable algebra is graded-commutative,
  multiplication by this closed element is a Hochschild $0$-cocycle;
  this is the interval-wise version of
  \ref{prop:stalk-central-multiplication}. Extension by zero of the
  test function is compatible with restriction to a larger interval.
  For disjoint intervals \ref{prop:brane-bracket-locality} gives
  vanishing of the $P_0$ bracket between the two factors, so the
  factorization product of two such operations is the strict
  multiplication by $I_\partial(a,f)I_\partial(b,g)$; this is the
  multiplicative extension from $\mathfrak h_I$ to
  $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(I)=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h_I)$, not
  the linear current bracket.

  The Poisson statement is local on the line. For compactly supported
  test functions $a,b$,
  \ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling} (the strict $P_0$ identity
  on the brane factorization algebra) gives
  $$\{I_\partial(a,f),I_\partial(b,g)\}_{\mathrm{open}}
    =I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A}).$$
  Passing to the connected stable Hamiltonian quotient removes only
  the scalar Hamiltonian line, which is central for the bracket. Thus
  the current bracket is preserved. Taking $a$ and $b$ supported in a
  small coordinate interval and then passing to the locally constant
  stalk recovers \ref{thm:bulk-boundary}.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[CE-source obstruction, reframed]\label{prop:ce-source-obstruction}
  Let $\mathfrak h$ be a perfect Lie algebra in $\Cat{TateVec}$
  (i.e.\ $[\mathfrak h,\mathfrak h]=\mathfrak h$). Then no length-one CE
  coordinate $c^I$ dual to a Hamiltonian generator $H_I\in\mathfrak h$
  is closed under $d_{\mathrm{CE}}$:
  $$d_{\mathrm{CE}}c^K=-\tfrac12\,C^K_{IJ}\,c^Ic^J\neq 0.$$
  Equivalently, $H^1(\mathfrak h;\C)=0$.

  This obstruction is the structural reason that the boundary observable
  $O_I=J(H_I)\in A_\partial$ cannot be the image under $\Phi$ of $c^I$.
  Instead, under \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center},
  $$O_I=\Phi(u_I),$$
  the image of the CE coordinate dual to the shifted cotangent generator
  $\eta_{\delta_I}\in\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$. The boundary observable lives
  in the cotangent direction of the CE cochain algebra, not in the
  Hamiltonian direction. Its CE differential is not zero but
  $d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_K=C^L_{KJ}u_Lc^J$, mapping under $\Phi$ to the
  Hamiltonian vector field $d_\pi O_K=C^L_{KJ}O_L\theta^J$ of $O_K$ in
  the Schouten algebra.

  This is exactly what a $P_0$-algebra map should produce: a function
  whose Schouten differential is its Hamiltonian vector field.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  $\mathfrak h$ perfect means $C^K_{IJ}c^Ic^J\neq 0$ for some triple
  $(I,J,K)$ realizing a non-trivial bracket; $H^1$ vanishing follows.
  Identification $O_I=\Phi(u_I)$ is the content of
  \ref{cor:moment-map-shadow} combined with $\Phi(u_I)=O_I$ from
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center}. Differentials match on
  generators by \ref{lem:linear-poisson-schouten}.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}\label{rmk:ce-source-obstruction-disk}
  The reduced Hamiltonian Lie algebra
  $\mathfrak h=\widehat A/\C\cdot 1=(z_1,z_2)\C[[z_1,z_2]]$ of the
  formal symplectic disk in dimension two is perfect: for every
  monomial one has, before quotienting constants,
  $z_1^az_2^b=\bigl\{z_1,\tfrac{1}{b+1}z_1^az_2^{b+1}\bigr\}$, so
  $[\mathfrak h,\mathfrak h]=\mathfrak h$. In particular
  $[H_{1,0},H_{m,n}]=n\,H_{m,n-1}$ and
  $[H_{0,1},H_{m,n}]=-m\,H_{m-1,n}$. The hypothesis of
  \ref{prop:ce-source-obstruction} is met. The CE-length-one cochain
  $\xi_{a,b}=c^{a,b}$ dual to $H_{a,b}=z_1^az_2^b$ is therefore not
  closed, and no closed CE cochain has linear Hamiltonian part
  $c^{a,b}$, recovering the earlier source-obstruction observation.
\end{rmk}

\begin{thm}[Reduced derived Poisson center]\label{thm:reduced-derived-poisson-center}
  Let
  $$\mathfrak h=\prod_{d\geq1}H_d,\qquad
    \mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}=\bigoplus_{d\geq1}H_d^\vee$$
  be the product/direct-sum Tate Hamiltonian Lie algebra of the formal
  symplectic disk and its continuous dual. Put
  $$\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[1].$$
  Let $A_\partial=\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak h)$ be the completed stable
  degree-zero Hamiltonian trace algebra, with generators $O_i$ corresponding to
  a homogeneous topological basis $H_i$ of $\mathfrak h$. If
  $$[H_i,H_j]=C_{ij}^{k}H_k,$$
  with the constant target projected out, equip $A_\partial$ with the linear
  Poisson bracket
  $$\{O_i,O_j\}_\partial=C_{ij}^{k}O_k.$$
  Let
  $$\operatorname{PV}_{\mathrm{cont}}(A_\partial)
    =
    A_\partial\widehat\otimes
    \widehat\Lambda(\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}})$$
  be the completed algebra of continuous polyvectors, with odd generators
  $\theta_i$ dual to the coordinates $O_i$. The Poisson bivector is
  $$\pi_\partial=\frac12 C_{ij}^{k}O_k\,\theta_i\theta_j,$$
  and the Poisson differential is $d_\pi=[\pi_\partial,-]$ in the Schouten
  convention.

  If $c_i$ is the CE coordinate dual to $H_i\in\mathfrak h$ and $u_i$ is the CE
  coordinate dual to the shifted cotangent generator $\delta_i[1]\in
  \mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$, then the assignment
  $$c_i\longmapsto\theta_i,\qquad u_i\longmapsto O_i$$
  extends to an isomorphism of completed graded-commutative dg algebras
  $$C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)
    \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
    \bigl(\operatorname{PV}_{\mathrm{cont}}(A_\partial),d_\pi\bigr).$$
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  By the product/direct-sum convention already used in
  Proposition~\ref{prop:ce-koszul}, the continuous CE algebra of
  $\mathfrak g$ is freely generated, after completion, by the odd coordinates
  $c_i$ and the even coordinates $u_i$. The CE differential is dual to the
  brackets of $\mathfrak g$:
  $$d_{\mathrm{CE}}c_k=-\frac12 C_{ij}^{k}c_ic_j,\qquad
    d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_k=C_{kj}^{\ell}u_\ell c_j.$$
  The second formula is the coadjoint action of $\mathfrak h$ on
  $\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$ written on the dual coordinates.

  The linear Poisson bivector gives the Lichnerowicz differential
  \cite{lichnerowicz-poisson}
  $$d_\pi\theta_k=-\frac12 C_{ij}^{k}\theta_i\theta_j,\qquad
    d_\pi O_k=C_{kj}^{\ell}O_\ell\theta_j.$$
  Hence $c_i\mapsto\theta_i$ and $u_i\mapsto O_i$ intertwine the two
  differentials. The underlying completed graded-commutative algebras are
  freely generated by corresponding variables, so this is an isomorphism.

  Continuity is the same coefficient-finiteness used in
  Lemma~\ref{lem:continuous-bar-cobar}: for each fixed output coefficient in a
  bracket of Hamiltonians only finitely many homogeneous input-degree pairs
  contribute, and the coadjoint input has finite support in
  $\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}$. Thus the displayed sums define
  continuous derivations of the completed CE and polyvector algebras.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  The theorem is the reduced algebraic center calculation. It does not say that
  the scalar boundary function $O_f=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$
  is the image of the nonclosed CE coordinate $c_f$. It says that $O_f$ is the
  image of the CE coordinate $u_f$ dual to the shifted cotangent generator,
  while $c_f$ maps to the constant Hamiltonian vector-field operation
  $\theta_f$. This is why Proposition~\ref{prop:ce-source-obstruction} remains
  correct and why the full BV/factorization lift below has nontrivial content.
\end{rmk}

\begin{thm}[Open-closed derived center, cochain level]\label{thm:open-closed-derived-center}
  Let $\mathfrak h$ be any pro-finite-dimensional Lie algebra in
  $\Cat{TateVec}$ over $\C$, concentrated in degree zero, satisfying
  the Tate-conilpotency hypothesis of \ref{lem:continuous-bar-cobar}.
  Let $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$
  be the shifted-cotangent extension. Let
  $A_\partial=\widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\mathfrak h)$ be the
  Tate-completed Kirillov--Poisson algebra of
  \ref{lem:linear-poisson-schouten}.

  Then there is a canonical isomorphism of completed dg
  graded-commutative $P_0$-algebras
  $$\Phi:C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)
    \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
    \mathrm{PV}\bigl(A_\partial\bigr),$$
  determined on generators by
  $$\Phi(c^I)=\theta^I,\qquad \Phi(u_I)=O_I,$$
  where $c^I$ is the CE coordinate dual to $H_I\in\mathfrak h$ and
  $u_I$ is the CE coordinate dual to the shifted cotangent generator
  $\eta_{\delta_I}\in\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$.

  Moreover, $\mathrm{PV}(A_\partial)$ identifies with the derived
  $P_0$-factorization center of the constant factorization algebra
  $A_\partial$, so
  $$\Phi:C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)
    \xrightarrow{\ \sim\ } Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(A_\partial)$$
  is the cochain-level open-closed derived center isomorphism in the
  formal/local sector.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Generators and free extension.} By
  \ref{lem:continuous-bar-cobar},
  $$C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)=
    \widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}\bigl(
      (\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[1])^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[-1]
    \bigr)
    \cong \widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}\bigl(\{u_I\}\bigr)
    \widehat\otimes \widehat\Lambda\bigl(\{c^I\}\bigr),$$
  with $|u_I|=0$ and $|c^I|=1$. On the open side,
  $\mathrm{PV}(A_\partial)=\widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\{O_I\})
  \widehat\otimes \widehat\Lambda(\{\theta^I\})$, with $|O_I|=0$ and
  $|\theta^I|=1$. The same generator data on both sides freely generate
  completed graded-commutative algebras in $\Cat{TateVec}$ of the same
  shape; the assignment $c^I\mapsto\theta^I$, $u_I\mapsto O_I$ extends
  uniquely to a continuous bijection of completed dg-commutative
  algebras.

  \emph{Cochain identity on generators.} The CE differential is
  $$d_{\mathrm{CE}}c^K=-\tfrac12 C^K_{IJ}c^Ic^J,\qquad
    d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_K=C^L_{KJ}u_L c^J.$$
  By \ref{lem:linear-poisson-schouten},
  $$d_\pi\theta^K=-\tfrac12 C^K_{IJ}\theta^I\theta^J,\qquad
    d_\pi O_K=C^L_{KJ}O_L\theta^J.$$
  Therefore
  $$\Phi(d_{\mathrm{CE}}c^K)=-\tfrac12 C^K_{IJ}\theta^I\theta^J
    =d_\pi\theta^K=d_\pi\Phi(c^K),$$
  $$\Phi(d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_K)=C^L_{KJ}O_L\theta^J=d_\pi O_K
    =d_\pi\Phi(u_K).$$

  \emph{Cochain identity on the full completed algebra.} Both
  $d_{\mathrm{CE}}$ and $d_\pi$ are degree-$1$ derivations of the
  completed graded-commutative algebra structures on each side. They
  satisfy the graded Leibniz rule with the same Koszul sign
  convention. $\Phi$ is an algebra homomorphism, so
  $$\Phi(d_{\mathrm{CE}}(xy))
    =\Phi\bigl((d_{\mathrm{CE}}x)y+(-1)^{|x|}x\,d_{\mathrm{CE}}y\bigr)
    =\Phi(d_{\mathrm{CE}}x)\Phi(y)+(-1)^{|x|}\Phi(x)\Phi(d_{\mathrm{CE}}y),$$
  while
  $$d_\pi\Phi(xy)=d_\pi\bigl(\Phi(x)\Phi(y)\bigr)
    =(d_\pi\Phi(x))\Phi(y)+(-1)^{|x|}\Phi(x)d_\pi\Phi(y).$$
  Generator-level agreement plus Leibniz/algebra-homomorphism gives
  agreement on every word in $\{c^I,u_J\}$ at fixed total length;
  Tate-completeness of both sides plus continuity of $d_{\mathrm{CE}},
  d_\pi,\Phi$ in the Tate filtration extends the equality to the
  completed algebras.

  \emph{Inverse.} The assignment $\theta^I\mapsto c^I$,
  $O_I\mapsto u_I$ extends to a continuous algebra homomorphism in the
  opposite direction. By the same Leibniz argument, it intertwines
  $d_\pi$ and $d_{\mathrm{CE}}$. The two compositions fix generators,
  hence fix the completed algebras. So $\Phi$ is an isomorphism of
  complete dg graded-commutative algebras.

  \emph{$P_0$-bracket compatibility.} The CE side carries the canonical
  $(-1)$-shifted Poisson structure on
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(T^*[1]\mathfrak h)$ with
  $$\{c^I,u_J\}_{\mathrm{CE}}=\delta^I_J,\quad
    \{c^I,c^J\}_{\mathrm{CE}}=0,\quad
    \{u_I,u_J\}_{\mathrm{CE}}=0.$$
  These are the standard Poisson brackets on the cochain algebra of a
  $(-1)$-shifted cotangent of a Lie algebra
  (cf.\ Costello--Gwilliam factorization-algebra conventions).
  The Schouten bracket on $\mathrm{PV}(A_\partial)$ satisfies
  $$[\theta^I,O_J]_S=\delta^I_J,\quad
    [\theta^I,\theta^J]_S=0,\quad
    [O_I,O_J]_S=0,$$
  the last because $O_I,O_J$ are functions on the formal affine space
  $\mathfrak h^\vee$ and the Schouten bracket of two functions is zero.
  Generator-level matching gives
  $\Phi\bigl(\{c^I,u_J\}_{\mathrm{CE}}\bigr)
  =\Phi(\delta^I_J)=\delta^I_J=[\theta^I,O_J]_S
  =[\Phi(c^I),\Phi(u_J)]_S$, and similarly for the other two pairs.
  Both brackets satisfy the graded Leibniz rule; bilinear extension on
  completed words gives compatibility on the full completed algebra.

  \emph{Identification with the derived $P_0$-factorization center.}
  For a Poisson algebra $A$ regarded as a constant
  $\R^d$-factorization algebra (or as a stalk of a locally constant
  factorization algebra), the derived $P_0$-factorization center is
  computed by the Poisson cochain complex $\mathrm{PV}(A)$ with the
  Lichnerowicz differential $[\pi,-]_S$. This is the local stalk
  version of the Poisson-CE identification of Cattaneo--Felder /
  Costello--Gwilliam (cf.~\cite{costello-gwilliam}, central operations
  for factorization algebras with Poisson bracket; the identification
  is local: at a point, the factorization-center is the Poisson-cochain
  complex). Therefore
  $\mathrm{PV}(A_\partial)\simeq Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(A_\partial)$
  as completed dg-commutative $P_0$-algebras, and $\Phi$ is the
  cochain-level open-closed derived center isomorphism in this local
  stalk sense.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Moment-map shadow]\label{cor:moment-map-shadow}
  In the situation of \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center}, the
  degree-zero specialization of $\Phi$ on the cotangent direction is
  the moment-map / Kirillov assignment
  $$J:\mathfrak h\longrightarrow A_\partial=
    \widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\mathfrak h),
    \qquad J(f)=O_f.$$
  The closed-side Lie bracket $\{f,g\}_{\mathfrak h}$ matches the
  Kirillov--Poisson bracket on $A_\partial$:
  $$\{J(f),J(g)\}_\partial=J\bigl(\{f,g\}_{\mathfrak h}\bigr).$$
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
  $J$ is the restriction of $\Phi$ to the cotangent direction
  $u_I\mapsto O_I$ followed by linear extension along
  $\mathfrak h\hookrightarrow A_\partial$ (the canonical embedding of
  $\mathfrak h$ as the linear functions on $\mathfrak h^\vee$). Bracket
  compatibility is the $(c^J,u_K)$-versus-$(\theta^J,O_K)$ identity
  from \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center} read off in degree zero.
  Equivalently, this is the standard Kirillov--Kostant--Souriau theorem
  for linear Poisson structures.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Derived center, formal symplectic disk]\label{cor:derived-center-formal-disk}
  Let $\mathfrak h=\widehat A/\C\cdot 1=(z_1,z_2)\C[[z_1,z_2]]$ be the
  reduced Hamiltonian Lie algebra of the formal symplectic disk on
  $\C^2$, with bracket
  $\{f,g\}=\partial_{z_1}f\,\partial_{z_2}g-\partial_{z_2}f\,\partial_{z_1}g$
  modulo constants. Choose the Taylor basis $H_{a,b}=z_1^az_2^b$ for
  $a,b\geq 0$, $a+b>0$. Structure constants:
  $$[H_{a,b},H_{c,d}]=(ad-bc)\,H_{a+c-1,b+d-1},$$
  with the convention that $H_{m,n}=0$ if $\min(m,n)<0$ or $m+n=0$.

  Set $A_\partial=\widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\mathfrak h)$,
  with linear coordinates $O_{a,b}$ on $\mathfrak h^\vee$ and
  Kirillov--Poisson bracket
  $\{O_{a,b},O_{c,d}\}_\partial=(ad-bc)O_{a+c-1,b+d-1}$.
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center} gives the cochain-level
  derived-center isomorphism
  $$\Phi:C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak h\ltimes
    \mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}[1])\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
    \mathrm{PV}\bigl(\widehat{\mathbf S}_{\mathrm{Tate}}(\mathfrak h)\bigr),
    \qquad c^{a,b}\mapsto\theta^{a,b},\quad u_{a,b}\mapsto O_{a,b}.$$
  Its moment-map shadow is the boundary evaluation map
  $J(f)=O_f=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$ of
  \ref{thm:bulk-boundary} after identifying $A_\partial$ with the
  stable connected scalar-reduced Hamiltonian trace algebra of
  \ref{prop:brane-ops}.
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
  The structure constants are an instance of
  \ref{prop:hamiltonian-polyvector-reduction} read on monomials.
  Apply \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center} to this $\mathfrak h$
  (perfect; pro-finite-dimensional in Taylor filtration;
  Tate-conilpotent; see \ref{rmk:ce-source-obstruction-disk}). The
  moment-map shadow follows from \ref{cor:moment-map-shadow} together
  with \ref{thm:bulk-boundary}.
\end{proof}

\begin{ex}[Low-degree monomial verification]\label{ex:low-degree-phi}
  We verify $\Phi$ on small monomials of the formal symplectic disk.

  \begin{itemize}
    \item \emph{Degree-1 generators.} Take $H_{1,0}=z_1$,
      $H_{0,1}=z_2$. The bracket
      $[H_{1,0},H_{0,1}]=1\cdot 1-0\cdot 0=1$ lifts to the constant
      $H_{0,0}$, which is set to zero in $\mathfrak h$. Hence
      $C^{0,0}_{(1,0),(0,1)}=0$ in $\mathfrak h$. Consequently
      $d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_{0,0}$ is not present (no such generator); the
      $u_{0,0}$ degree of freedom does not appear, consistent with
      constants being removed.

    \item \emph{Degree-2 calculation.} Take $H_{2,0}=z_1^2$,
      $H_{0,2}=z_2^2$. The bracket
      $\{z_1^2,z_2^2\}=2z_1\cdot 2z_2-0\cdot 0=4z_1z_2=4H_{1,1}$, so
      $C^{1,1}_{(2,0),(0,2)}=4$ and the antisymmetric companion is
      $C^{1,1}_{(0,2),(2,0)}=-4$. The cochain identity reads
      $$d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_{1,1}=4\,u_{2,0}\,c^{0,2}-4\,u_{0,2}\,c^{2,0}+
        \cdots,$$
      where $\cdots$ denotes terms from other index triples
      $(K,J,L)$ with $K=(1,1)$. Each such term
      $C^L_{(1,1),J}\,u_L\,c^J$ arises from
      $\{H_{1,1},H_J\}=\sum_L C^L_{(1,1),J}\,H_L$. For example,
      $\{H_{1,1},H_{1,0}\}=\partial_{z_1}(z_1z_2)\cdot 0-
      \partial_{z_2}(z_1z_2)\cdot 1=-z_1=-H_{1,0}$, so
      $C^{1,0}_{(1,1),(1,0)}=-1$, contributing $-u_{1,0}\,c^{1,0}$ to
      $d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_{1,1}$. On the open/PV side,
      $$d_\pi O_{1,1}=4\,O_{2,0}\,\theta^{0,2}-4\,O_{0,2}\,\theta^{2,0}
        -O_{1,0}\,\theta^{1,0}+O_{0,1}\,\theta^{0,1}+\cdots,$$
      the same expression with $u\to O,c\to\theta$. Hence
      $\Phi(d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_{1,1})=d_\pi\Phi(u_{1,1})$. The script
      \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py} verifies the same
      structure-constant input on every monomial pair with exponents
      up to $6$ via the first-order Moyal coefficient $kn-lm$ at
      $\hbar^1$, which equals $C^K_{IJ}$ for these indices.

    \item \emph{Higher-order word.} For $K=(1,1)$, $J=(1,0)$,
      $J'=(0,1)$, the cochain element $u_{1,1}c^{1,0}c^{0,1}$ has
      degree $0+1+1=2$. Its CE differential, by graded Leibniz, is
      $$d_{\mathrm{CE}}\bigl(u_{1,1}c^{1,0}c^{0,1}\bigr)
        =(d_{\mathrm{CE}}u_{1,1})c^{1,0}c^{0,1}
        -u_{1,1}(d_{\mathrm{CE}}c^{1,0})c^{0,1}
        +u_{1,1}c^{1,0}(d_{\mathrm{CE}}c^{0,1}),$$
      with each summand applying the generator formulas above. The
      same word on the PV side is $O_{1,1}\theta^{1,0}\theta^{0,1}$,
      and $d_\pi$ applied with the same Leibniz convention produces
      the corresponding triple sum with $u\to O$ and $c\to\theta$.
      Term-by-term equality follows from the generator identities; the
      full word equality is the algebra-homomorphism Leibniz argument
      from \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center}.
  \end{itemize}
\end{ex}

\begin{constr}[Compact current PBW/Rees source]\label{constr:compact-current-pbw-rees-source}
  Let $\mc P$ denote the principal-part module
  $$\mc P=\bigoplus_{\substack{a,b\geq0\\ a+b>0}}\C\,\rho_{a,b},\qquad
    \rho_{a,b}=z_1^{-a-1}z_2^{-b-1}\,dz_1dz_2,$$
  identified with $\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}$ by the residue pairing
  of Proposition~\ref{prop:principal-part-coadjoint}. Put
  $$\mathfrak g_{\mathrm{pp}}=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mc P[1],$$
  with zero differential and bracket
  $$[f,g]=\{f,g\},\qquad [f,\rho[1]]=(f\cdot\rho)[1],\qquad
    [\rho[1],\sigma[1]]=0,$$
  where $f\cdot\rho=\pi_{\mathrm{pp}}\{f,\rho\}$. On monomials this action is
  $$z_1^pz_2^q\cdot\rho_{a,b}
    =-(pb-qa+p-q)\rho_{a-p+1,b-q+1},$$
  with negative-index targets zero.

  For an interval $I\subset\R$, define the compactly supported current Lie
  algebra
  $$\mathfrak J_{\mathfrak g}(I)
    =C_c^\infty(I)\widehat\otimes\mathfrak g_{\mathrm{pp}},\qquad
    [\alpha\otimes x,\beta\otimes y]
      =\alpha\beta\otimes[x,y].$$
  Its PBW/Rees algebra is
  $$U_\hbar\bigl(\mathfrak J_{\mathfrak g}(I)\bigr)
    =\widehat T\bigl(\mathfrak J_{\mathfrak g}(I)\bigr)[[\hbar]]
      \big/
      \langle xy-(-1)^{|x||y|}yx-\hbar[x,y]\rangle.$$
  The PBW filtration is the tensor-word filtration. Its special fibre is
  $$U_\hbar\bigl(\mathfrak J_{\mathfrak g}(I)\bigr)/(\hbar)
    \cong \widehat{\mathbf S}\bigl(\mathfrak J_{\mathfrak g}(I)\bigr),$$
  equipped with the semiclassical $P_0$ bracket
  $$\{\bar X,\bar Y\}_{P_0}
    =\bigl(\hbar^{-1}(XY-(-1)^{|X||Y|}YX)\bigr)\bmod\hbar.$$
  This is the PBW/Koszul-dual source for Hamiltonian and principal-part modes.
  It is not a closed CE cochain algebra map; the CE comparison must be made
  separately by bar-cobar twisting or by a completed pairing.
\end{constr}

\begin{prob}[PBW-source $P_0$ center action and CE comparison]\label{prob:pbw-p0-center-action}
  Construct a filtered factorization-center action of the compactly
  supported current PBW/Rees source
  $U_\hbar(\mathfrak J_{\mathfrak g})$ of
  Construction~\ref{constr:compact-current-pbw-rees-source}. The target cannot
  be the polynomial open observable algebra alone if the cotangent generators
  are included; it must use the enlarged principal-part boundary object of
  Theorem~\ref{prop:reduced-principal-part-boundary-current}. In the
  classical special fibre the action must send
  $$f\longmapsto B_f=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)},\qquad
    \rho_{a,b}[1]\longmapsto\Theta_{a,b},$$
  and satisfy the stalkwise bracket identities
  $$\{B_f,B_g\}_{\mathrm{open}}=B_{\{f,g\}},\qquad
    \{B_f,\Theta_\rho\}_{\mathrm{open}}=\Theta_{f\cdot\rho},\qquad
    \{\Theta_\rho,\Theta_\sigma\}_{\mathrm{open}}=0.$$
  This special-fibre statement is the natural $P_0$ theorem. A strict action
  of the full filtered Rees algebra on the same commutative reduced target is
  not a consequence of these identities: in the source
  $$XY-(-1)^{|X||Y|}YX=\hbar[X,Y],$$
  while multiplication operators on a commutative classical target commute.
  Thus the Rees-level theorem requires either a deformed boundary target or an
  explicit homotopical quantization of the central operations.
  The target data must include differential compatibility, factorization
  centrality homotopies, coherent $P_0$ bracket homotopies, and
  compact-support naturality for interval inclusions and disjoint unions before
  the de Rham contraction.

  Separately compare this PBW/Koszul-dual source with the closed CE observable
  algebra by an explicit twisting or pairing construction. Without this
  comparison, the result is a PBW/Koszul-dual boundary action, not a
  cochain-level map from closed CE observables.
\end{prob}

\begin{prob}[Unreduced Tate-coefficient cotangent lift]\label{prob:formal-factorization-center}
  This is the single residual of the umbrella theorem
  \ref{thm:main-local}. Construct a Tate or weighted-coefficient
  extension of the BV heat-kernel calculus on $\R^2\times\C^2$ in
  which:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item the formal Casimir
      $C_{\mathfrak h}=\sum_{d\geq 1}\sum_i e_{d,i}\otimes e^i_d$
      converges as an element of
      $\widehat{\mathfrak h}\,\widehat\otimes\,
      \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}$;
    \item the Costello propagator $P_{\epsilon,L}$ extends to that
      coefficient category;
    \item the unreduced principal-part current sub-factorization
      algebra
      $\widetilde{\mathrm{Obs}}^{\mathrm{cl,pp}}_{\partial,N}(I)
      =\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{open},N}(I)\,\widehat\otimes\,
      \widehat{\mathbf S}\bigl(\mc M^{\mathrm{pp,unred}}_\partial(I)\bigr)$
      admits a chain-level primitive projection $\pi_{\mathrm{prim}}$
      with verified $Q$-compatibility, factorization compatibility, and
      $P_0$-bracket homotopies;
    \item statement~(d) of \ref{thm:main-local} lifts to the
      unreduced factorization-algebra model and statement~(e) extends
      to the cotangent (one-antifield) sector at all orders in $\hbar$.
  \end{enumerate}

  Equivalently, lift the cochain-level
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center} and the Hamiltonian-sector
  factorization-algebra
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization} to a
  cochain-level morphism of factorization algebras
  $$\Phi_{\mathrm{cl}}:
    \mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{closed},H}\big|_{\R\times p}
    \longrightarrow
    \mathrm Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{open},N}\bigr)$$
  on the unreduced (cotangent-included) sector, with all $P_0$-center
  homotopies, factorization centrality homotopies, the stable
  connected quotient, and a boundary realization of the shifted
  cotangent generators. Any global version must additionally pass
  through the local-Hamiltonian descent and period obstruction of
  \ref{prop:formal-local-global-restriction}; a stalkwise formal
  disk map is not a Weiss/Ran descent theorem for factorization
  centers.

  Two routes are named, neither yet executed.
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \emph{Route R1: weighted Tate completion.} Replace the
      direct sum $\bigoplus_{d\geq 1}H_d^{\vee}$ by a weighted Tate
      completion in which the Casimir converges. The
      $\mathfrak m$-adic completion fails by the finite-window
      obstruction; a candidate is a graded-Mittag-Leffler completion
      controlled by a polynomial weight in the degree filtration,
      checked compatible with the Costello RG flow at every order.
    \item \emph{Route R2: nilpotent truncation.} Restrict to the
      smaller Lie sector $\mathfrak m^2/\mathfrak m^{N+1}$ or analogous
      nilpotent truncation, declaring that translations and the
      constant-Hamiltonian $\hbar$-normalization have been removed
      (the Costello--Li $\mathfrak{gl}(N\mid N)$ precedent). This
      loses the fully stable connected statement on $\mathfrak h$ but
      recovers a meaningful nilpotent sector unconditionally.
  \end{itemize}

  The deciding evidence to close: either (R1) yields a
  Tate-coefficient category with the displayed Casimir convergence
  and BV propagator extension, or (R2) gives an explicit obstruction
  class for the unreduced cotangent lift (which would itself be a
  major theorem and would not invalidate the reduced umbrella
  \ref{thm:main-local}, parts (a)--(f)).

  The residual is identified across four independent obstruction
  routes as the same obstruction. The cotangent direction
  $\mathfrak h^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[1]$ supports the
  deformation-correct realization $\mc P$ at the cochain level; fails
  to admit a polynomial sub-bimodule realization in any
  locally-nilpotent category; admits a factorization-algebra
  realization at the reduced post-contraction level; and obstructs
  the unreduced lift at the analytic level. The umbrella theorem is
  unconditional in parts (a), (b), (c), (e) on the degree-zero
  Hamiltonian sector, and (f); part~(d) is unconditional at the
  reduced post-contraction level and conditional on this problem for
  the unreduced extension; part~(e) is unconditional on the
  degree-zero Hamiltonian sector at all orders in $\hbar$ and
  conditional on this problem for the descendant (one-antifield)
  sector.
\end{prob}

\begin{rmk}[The residual is conditional, the umbrella is not]
  \ref{thm:main-local} is unconditional in parts (a), (b), (c),
  (e) (degree zero), (f). Part (d) is unconditional at the reduced
  post-contraction level and conditional on
  \ref{prob:formal-factorization-center} for the unreduced
  factorization-algebra extension. Part (e) is unconditional on the
  degree-zero Hamiltonian sector at all orders in $\hbar$ and
  conditional on the same residual for the descendant (one-antifield)
  sector. Cross-volume comparisons (Vol III CY-to-chiral, Igusa
  $\Delta_5$ / BKM, twisted-M-theory universality) are frontier
  obligations recorded in the convention contract appendix; they are
  outside the dependency closure of the present local theorem.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}[Weiss/Ran descent firewall]\label{rmk:weiss-ran-descent-firewall}
  A global closed-open map is not obtained by choosing Darboux coordinates at
  each point and gluing the resulting stalk maps. The obstruction lives in the
  Weiss/Ran total complex
  $$\operatorname{Tot} C^\bullet_{\mathrm{WR}}
    \left(\operatorname{Ran}(L);
    \underline{\operatorname{RHom}}\left(
    \mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{closed},H},
    Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}(\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{open}})
    \right)\right).$$
  Vanishing of the local Hamiltonian period class is only the first condition.
  One must also prove source comparison, cotangent boundary realization, all
  $P_0$-center homotopies, and factorization descent. Until then the
  Hamiltonian boundary map, the $\Theta$-currents, and the PBW/Rees action are
  formal local or reduced-current statements.
\end{rmk}

\subsection{Operators in the open brane gauge theory and the large N limit}

The local-operator calculation is performed in the reduced BV model with
fields $\phi_1,\phi_2$ and the antifield $\psi=A^*$ for the Lagrange
multiplier $A$. We take $GL_N$-invariants in characteristic zero, so the
Chevalley part of the gauge BRST differential acts trivially on trace
functions by cyclicity.

The gauge field has one algebraic job: it imposes the moment-map equation
$[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$. In BV language this equation is imposed by the Koszul
differential $Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2]$. This is why the stable trace algebra
starts noncommutative, as cyclic words in two matrices, and then collapses in
cohomology to commutative monomials on the formal symplectic plane.

\begin{constr}[The reduced BV algebra at the insertion point]\label{constr:reduced-bv-algebra}
  At a fixed point of the brane line, introduce three matrix variables
  $$\phi_1,\phi_2\in\lie{gl}_N,\qquad \psi\in\lie{gl}_N[1].$$
  The reduced local polynomial algebra is
  $$\mc R_N=\C[(\phi_1)^i{}_j,(\phi_2)^i{}_j]
    \otimes\Lambda\bigl((\psi)^i{}_j\bigr).$$
  Its BRST differential is the derivation determined on generators by
  $$Q(\phi_1)^i{}_j=0,\qquad Q(\phi_2)^i{}_j=0,\qquad
    Q(\psi)^i{}_j=([\phi_1,\phi_2])^i{}_j.$$
  This formula is the algebraic shadow of the $A$-equation of motion:
  varying
  $$\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2+A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr)$$
  with respect to $A$ gives $[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$, and the antifield $\psi=A^*$
  records that equation as a Koszul differential.
\end{constr}

\begin{lem}[De Rham jets]\label{lem:derivative-jets}
  Positive jets in the topological direction vanish in local
  operator cohomology. Equivalently, every cohomology class has a representative
  determined by the values of the fields and antifields at the insertion point.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  For a coordinate $t$ on the line, the de Rham part of the BRST operator is
  $d_{\R}$. On the jet algebra one has the contraction homotopy
  $[d_{\R},\iota_{\partial_t}]=\partial_t$. Hence a local expression containing
  a positive $t$-derivative is cohomologous to zero after applying the usual
  Euler homotopy on jet degree. This kills topological-direction jets and leaves
  the holomorphic $z_i$-derivatives used later on the closed side.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[Stable trace invariants]\label{prop:stable-trace-invariants}
  Let $F=\C\langle x_1,x_2\rangle$ and let $\mathrm{Cyc}(F)=F/[F,F]$ be the
  vector space of cyclic words. For each $N$, $GL_N$ acts on
  $\lie{gl}_N^2$ by simultaneous conjugation. The degreewise stable invariant
  algebra
  $$\C[\lie{gl}_\infty^2]^{GL_\infty}_{\mathrm{st}}
    :=\bigoplus_{d\geq0}\varprojlim_N
      \bigl(\C[\lie{gl}_N^2]^{GL_N}\bigr)_d$$
  with respect to block-restriction maps in each word-degree
  is the free commutative algebra generated by the nonempty cyclic words:
  $$\C[\lie{gl}_\infty^2]^{GL_\infty}_{\mathrm{st}}
    \cong\mathbf S\bigl(\mathrm{Cyc}(F)_{\mathrm{nonempty}}\bigr),$$
  where a cyclic word $w$ maps to the trace function
  $(\phi_1,\phi_2)\mapsto\mathrm{Tr}\,w(\phi_1,\phi_2)$.
  More precisely, in total positive word-degree $d$ this map is an isomorphism
  for every $N\geq d$, after omitting the scalar empty trace as a primitive
  generator.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  Procesi--Razmyslov invariant theory \cites{procesi,razmyslov} gives two
  inputs. First, $\C[\lie{gl}_N^2]^{GL_N}$ is generated by trace functions of
  words in the two generic matrices. Second, all polynomial relations among
  these trace functions are consequences of the fundamental trace identities
  of matrix size $N$; in particular every homogeneous trace relation has total
  word-degree at least $N+1$. Fix a total word-degree $d$. For every
  $N\geq d$ the degree-$d$ relations are exactly cyclicity of the trace.
  Passing degree by degree to the stable inverse limit removes
  all finite-$N$ trace identities. The surviving identification is
  $\mathrm{Tr}(uv)=\mathrm{Tr}(vu)$. This is exactly the symmetric algebra on
  cyclic words.

\end{proof}

\begin{lem}[Stable marked trace invariants]\label{lem:stable-marked-traces}
  In the stable invariant theory used below, the primitive part linear or
  quadratic in an odd marked matrix $\psi$ is obtained from the corresponding
  even three-matrix trace invariant by polarization and skew-symmetrisation in
  the marked letters. The only stable single-trace relation is graded cyclicity:
  moving one $\psi$ through the trace has sign $+1$, while moving one $\psi$
  past another $\psi$ gives a minus sign.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  Apply Proposition~\ref{prop:stable-trace-invariants} to three even generic
  matrices and take the homogeneous summand linear, respectively quadratic, in
  the third matrix. The Procesi--Razmyslov trace identities have no stable
  relations in the fixed total word-degree once $N$ is large enough. Declaring
  the marked matrix odd is the usual super-polarization: the linear part is
  unchanged, and the quadratic part is projected to the alternating component
  under exchange of the two marked occurrences. The trace relation therefore
  becomes exactly graded cyclicity. These are the signs used in the finite
  complex for one- and two-$\psi$ words.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  The empty trace is the finite-rank scalar $\mathrm{Tr}_N(1)=N$, which changes
  with $N$ and fails to define a stable primitive generator. The stable
  symmetric algebra still has its ordinary unit; what is omitted is the empty
  trace as a generator of the connected primitive part. The class
  $\mathrm{Tr}(\psi)$ is a genuine stable odd primitive class. It is excluded
  from the Hamiltonian comparison because constants have been removed from the
  closed Hamiltonian algebra.
\end{rmk}

Varying
$$S=\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2+A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr)$$
with respect to $A$ gives the moment-map equation
$[\phi_1,\phi_2]=0$. In the reduced BV complex,
$$Q\psi=[\phi_1,\phi_2],\qquad Q\phi_1=Q\phi_2=0$$
on invariant trace functions.

\begin{constr}[Boundary evaluation of a closed Hamiltonian]\label{constr:boundary-evaluation}
