  The map is well-defined on $\bar A$ by
  Corollary~\ref{cor:matrix-evaluation-well-defined}; constants map to the
  scalar $N$ and vanish in the Hamiltonian quotient by constants. Lemma
  \ref{lem:trace-bracket-descends} gives the open Hamiltonian trace Poisson
  bracket. For
  $f=z_1^kz_2^l$ and $g=z_1^mz_2^n$, Proposition~\ref{prop:first-order-bracket}
  gives
  $$\{\partial_{\mathrm{bb}}(f),\partial_{\mathrm{bb}}(g)\}_{\mathrm{open}}
    =\overline{(kn-lm)\mathrm{Tr}
      (\phi_1^{k+m-1}\phi_2^{l+n-1})}.$$
  The closed Poisson bracket is
  $$\{f,g\}_{\bar A}=\overline{(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1}},$$
  and applying $\partial_{\mathrm{bb}}$ gives the same expression. Bilinearity
  proves the identity for all polynomials.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Classical local bulk-boundary coupling, healed]\label{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling}
  Let $a,b\in C^\infty_c(\R)$ be scalar compactly supported test
  functions on the brane line, and for $f\in\bar A$ define the smeared
  boundary Hamiltonian
  $$I_\partial(a,f)
    =B_f(a)
    =\int_\R a(t)\,
      \overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1(t),\phi_2(t))}\,dt
    \in A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}(\R).$$
  Then the following two strengthenings of the bracket identity hold
  jointly.

  \emph{(i) Strict $P_0$ identity on disjoint supports.} In the $P_0$
  bracket of $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}$,
  $$\{I_\partial(a,f),I_\partial(b,g)\}_{A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}}
    =I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A}),$$
  and the bracket vanishes whenever the supports of $a$ and $b$ are
  disjoint. The locality input is the canonical equal-time bracket
  $\{(\phi_1)^i{}_j(t),(\phi_2)^k{}_l(s)\}=\delta^i_l\delta^k_j\delta(t-s)$
  of \ref{rmk:equal-time-locality}; smearing against $a(t)b(s)$
  produces the pointwise product $ab$ after integration of the delta
  function. This is the level-one component of
  \ref{thm:open-closed-derived-center-factorization}.

  \emph{(ii) Explicit U(1) center anomaly constant.} Before projection
  to the scalar-reduced quotient, the unreduced open bracket carries an
  explicit central piece
  $$\{I_\partial(a,f),I_\partial(b,g)\}_{\mathrm{open}}
    =I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A})
    +N\cdot\omega(f,g)\int_\R a(t)b(t)\,dt,$$
  where $\omega$ is the cocycle of \ref{lem:omega-cocycle} and the
  prefactor $N$ is the rank of the brane stack and is the value of the
  U(1) center character $\mathrm{Tr}:\C\cdot I\to\C$, $I\mapsto N$.
  After projection to $H^0_{\mathrm{red}}=H^0/\C\cdot\mathrm{Tr}(1)$
  the second term vanishes, and one recovers
  $$\overline{\{I_\partial(a,f),I_\partial(b,g)\}_{\mathrm{open}}}
    =\overline{I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A})}.$$

  Statements~(i) and~(ii) are compatible: (ii) is the unreduced
  refinement, (i) is the level-one factorization-algebra restatement
  on the scalar-reduced sector. The equal-time delta locality of (i)
  produces a strict $P_0$ factorization algebra rather than a
  homotopical one, while (ii) records the U(1) center anomaly that
  obstructs lifting (i) to the unreduced sector.
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Proof of (i).} By \ref{constr:interval-fact-algebras}, the
  $P_0$ bracket on $A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}$ is the biderivation
  with $\{a\otimes f,b\otimes g\}_{A_\partial}=ab\otimes\{f,g\}_{\bar A}$
  on length-one generators, so
  $\{B_f(a),B_g(b)\}_{A_\partial^{\mathrm{Ham}}}=B_{\{f,g\}}(ab)
  =I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A})$. \ref{prop:brane-bracket-locality}
  then gives vanishing on disjoint supports because
  $ab\equiv 0$ pointwise. The same identity is the smeared content of
  the equal-time delta-function bracket of
  \ref{rmk:equal-time-locality}: tracing
  $f(\phi_1,\phi_2)(t)$ and $g(\phi_1,\phi_2)(s)$, applying the
  Leibniz rule, and integrating against $a(t)b(s)\delta(t-s)$ produces
  the pointwise product $ab$ after the delta-function integration.

  \emph{Proof of (ii).} The unreduced bracket of two integrals is, by
  locality of the canonical bracket and \ref{thm:bulk-boundary},
  \begin{align*}
    \{I_\partial(a,f),I_\partial(b,g)\}
    &=\iint_{\R^2}a(t)b(t')\,
      \{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi(t)),\mathrm{Tr}\,g(\phi(t'))\}\,dt\,dt'\\
    &=\int_\R a(t)b(t)\,\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\{f,g\}_{\bar A}\bigr)\,dt
      +\int_\R a(t)b(t)\,\omega(f,g)\,N\,dt,
  \end{align*}
  where the splitting is by the central decomposition of
  \ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly-open}: the central scalar
  $\omega(f,g)\cdot N$ is removed by the projection to
  $H^0_{\mathrm{red}}$, and the remaining piece is
  $I_\partial(ab,\{f,g\}_{\bar A})$ exactly. The constants are
  explicit: the prefactor of the central piece is $N\cdot\omega(f,g)$,
  and the smeared coefficient is $\int ab\,dt$. The
  classical-to-quantum reduction of
  \ref{thm:quantum-classical-anomaly} identifies $\omega(f,g)\cdot N$
  with the leading-order Capelli shift $\hbar N$ on the linear
  generators $f=z_1$, $g=z_2$. Compact support of $a,b$ kills boundary
  terms.
\end{proof}

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1.35]
    % brane line R with arrow
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (-3.4,0) -- (3.4,0);
    \node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize] at (3.4,0.0) {\,brane $\R$};
    % ordered boundary insertions O_f(t), O_g(t')
    \node[circle, fill=black, inner sep=0pt, minimum size=4.2pt,
      label={[font=\footnotesize]below:{$t$}}] (A) at (-1.7,0) {};
    \node[circle, fill=black, inner sep=0pt, minimum size=4.2pt,
      label={[font=\footnotesize]below:{$t'$}}] (B) at (1.7,0) {};
    % insertion labels above the line
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=south] at (-1.7,0.05)
      {$O_f(t)=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,f(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$};
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=south] at ( 1.7,0.05)
      {$O_g(t')=\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,g(\phi_1,\phi_2)}$};
    % single P_partial propagator above
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]},
      decoration={markings, mark=at position 0.55 with
        {\node[font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$P_\partial$};}},
      postaction={decorate}]
      (A) to[bend left=55] (B);
    % bivector annotation
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=south, align=center] at (0,1.55)
      {$P_\partial=\partial_{z_1}\!\otimes\!\partial_{z_2}
        -\partial_{z_2}\!\otimes\!\partial_{z_1}$};
    % automorphism / weight / output
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=north, align=center] at (0,-1.0)
      {$|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_1)|=1,\quad
        \tfrac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_1)|}=1,\quad
        \text{weight}=\hbar^1$};
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=north, align=center] at (0,-1.5)
      {output:\quad $\hbar(kn-lm)\,
        \overline{\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1^{k+m-1}\phi_2^{l+n-1})}$
        \ \ on $f=z_1^kz_2^l$, $g=z_1^mz_2^n$};
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{The first-order graph $\Gamma_1$ for the trace bracket
    $\{O_f,O_g\}$. Two ordered boundary insertions sit on the brane line
    $\R$ at distinct times $t,t'$; the unique propagator $P_\partial$
    contracts one $z_1$-leg on one side against one $z_2$-leg on the
    other (and the antisymmetric partner). The automorphism group is
    trivial and the symmetry factor is $1$, so the graph weight is
    $\hbar^1$. Reading the bivector contraction on monomials reproduces
    the cocycle coefficient $(kn-lm)$ of
    Proposition~\ref{prop:first-order-bracket}, the order-$\hbar$ Moyal
    coefficient of Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial}, and the U(1)
    centre cocycle $\omega(f,g)$ of Lemma~\ref{lem:omega-cocycle}
    realised at multidegree $(k+m,l+n)=(1,1)$.}
  \label{fig:gamma1}
\end{figure}
The graph $\Gamma_1$ of Figure~\ref{fig:gamma1} records the single canonical
contraction producing the coefficient $(kn-lm)$ in
Proposition~\ref{prop:first-order-bracket}; it is not a separate
Feynman-integral proof.

\begin{proof}[Proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}]
  Proposition~\ref{prop:local-model-mixed-definition} identifies the closed
  Hamiltonian BF sector and the compatible brane BV theory as local mixed
  holomorphic-topological data. The open Hamiltonian-sector algebra is
  obtained from the product of the topological self-Floer model for
  $\R\subset T^*\R$ and the formal holomorphic affine Koszul calculation for
  $\Ext^*_R(R/\mathfrak m,R/\mathfrak m)$.
  Lemma~\ref{lem:open-action-reduction} identifies the ghost-zero reduction
  with the gauged first-order matrix model
  $$\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\phi_1\,d\phi_2+A[\phi_1,\phi_2]\bigr).$$
  Lemma~\ref{lem:derivative-jets} removes positive topological jets, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:adjacent-swaps} identifies cyclic words with the same
  commutative monomial. Proposition~\ref{prop:one-psi-homology} computes the
  primitive one-$\psi$ homology, and Proposition~\ref{prop:stable-trace-invariants}
  gives Proposition~\ref{prop:brane-ops} after passing to the connected
  Hamiltonian trace sector:
  $$\mc{O}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{brane},H}
    \cong \mathbf{S}(\bar A\oplus\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}[1]).$$

  On the closed side, Proposition~\ref{prop:hamiltonian-polyvector-reduction}
  identifies the polynomial local Hamiltonian modes with $\bar A$, and their
  Taylor completion is $\mathfrak h=\widehat{\mathfrak h}$. The cotangent BF
  field supplies the shifted coadjoint copy, so the local Lie algebra is
  $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$.
  Proposition~\ref{prop:grav-ops} computes local observables as
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g)$.
  Proposition~\ref{prop:ce-koszul} gives the Koszul dual
  $\widehat{U(\mathfrak g)}$, and the PBW/order Rees specialization gives
  $\widehat{\mathbf S}(\mathfrak g)$ at $\hbar=0$. Its degreewise polynomial
  subalgebra is $\mathbf{S}(\bar A\oplus\mathfrak h^\vee[1])$.
  Corollary~\ref{cor:cotangent-boundary-pairing} identifies $\mathfrak h^\vee$
  with $\bar A_{\mathrm{desc}}$ as the nonconstant boundary-paired primitive
  one-$\psi$ homology in the special fibre. Proposition~\ref{prop:open-descendant-action}
  and Corollary~\ref{cor:descendant-coadjoint-difference} compute the open descendant
  bracket and separate it from the closed coadjoint deformation.
  Finally Theorem~\ref{thm:bulk-boundary} constructs the bracket-compatible
  degree-zero Hamiltonian boundary evaluation from closed Hamiltonians to brane
  Hamiltonians. Corollary~\ref{cor:local-bulk-boundary-coupling}
  packages this as the local classical bulk-boundary coupling. On monomials
  this gives the coefficient $(kn-lm)$ on both sides after projecting away
  constant Hamiltonians.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{Formal deformation-quantization target}

The degree-zero Hamiltonian sector has a canonical formal
deformation-quantization target. The formal holomorphic disk has constant
Poisson tensor, so its canonical translation-invariant deformation is the
Weyl/Moyal algebra. This fixes the algebraic coefficients one would have to
recover from a quantum closed-open BV construction. It is not, by itself, a
construction of that quantum BV theory. The degree-zero Hamiltonian bracket
part of the classical theorem is the proposed special fibre of this formal
deformation; the cotangent/descendant part remains the separate problem stated
below.
Put
$$A_\hbar=\bigl(\C[[z_1,z_2]][[\hbar]],*\bigr),$$
where $*$ is the Weyl/Moyal product of the next subsection. The symbol
$\bar A_\hbar$ denotes the central quotient of the underlying Moyal Lie algebra
by $\C[[\hbar]]$; it is not used as an associative quotient. We write
$$[f,g]_{\mathrm{raw}}=f*g-g*f,\qquad
  \{f,g\}_\hbar=\hbar^{-1}[f,g]_{\mathrm{raw}}.$$
The degree-zero quantum Hamiltonian Lie algebra is
$$\mathfrak h_\hbar=\bar A_\hbar,\qquad
  [f,g]_{\mathfrak h_\hbar}=\{f,g\}_\hbar.$$
The specialization at $\hbar=0$ is the Poisson Lie algebra
$\mathfrak h=\C[[z_1,z_2]]/\C\cdot1$ used above.

On the brane side, the open action
$$\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2)$$
makes the matrix entries of $\phi_1$ and $\phi_2$ conjugate variables.
The canonical algebraic quantization of the unconstrained first-order matrix
phase space is the completed Weyl algebra
$\mathcal W_N$ generated by those entries with
$$[(\phi_1)^i{}_j,(\phi_2)^k{}_l]
  =\hbar\,\delta^i_l\delta^k_j,\qquad
  [(\phi_a)^i{}_j,(\phi_a)^k{}_l]=0\quad(a=1,2).$$
The gauge field imposes the conjugation moment-map constraint. With the
commutator convention above, the normal-ordered quantum comoment is
$$\widehat\mu_\epsilon=-\mathrm{Tr}\bigl([\epsilon,\phi_1]\phi_2\bigr),
  \qquad \epsilon\in\lie{gl}_N.$$
This formula is not cyclically reordered: for $\epsilon=1$ it vanishes, as the
scalar subgroup acts trivially. We use the convention
$$\hbar^{-1}[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,a]=\epsilon\cdot a$$
for the induced infinitesimal conjugation action on the Weyl algebra; changing
to the opposite commutator convention changes the displayed comoment by the
corresponding sign. The quantum brane local algebra is the BRST
quantum Hamiltonian reduction
$$\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}
  =C^\bullet_{\mathrm{BRST}}
    \bigl(\lie{gl}_N,\mathcal W_N,\widehat\mu\bigr),$$
whose degree-zero cohomology is the normalizer quotient
$$H^0\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}
  =\mathrm N_{\mathcal W_N}
    \bigl(\mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N)\bigr)/
    \mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N).$$
The constant Hamiltonian trace is projected out in degree zero as before. The
classical special fibre is the reduced BV algebra of
Construction~\ref{constr:reduced-bv-algebra}.

The quantum boundary map is Weyl-ordered trace evaluation:
$$\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}(f)
  =\overline{\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f)(\phi_1,\phi_2)},
  \qquad f\in\bar A_\hbar,$$
where $\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}$ denotes total symmetrisation before
passing to the trace. At $\hbar=0$ this recovers
Construction~\ref{constr:boundary-evaluation}. After dividing the commutator by
$\hbar$ and reducing modulo $\hbar$, the raw commutator identity recovers
Theorem~\ref{thm:bulk-boundary}.

\begin{prop}[BRST descent of Weyl-ordered Hamiltonian traces]\label{prop:quantum-boundary-descends}
  For every $f\in\bar A_\hbar$, the Weyl-ordered trace
  $$F_{f,N}=\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f)(\phi_1,\phi_2)$$
  is invariant under the quantum comoment:
  $$[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,F_{f,N}]=0,\qquad \epsilon\in\lie{gl}_N.$$
  Hence $F_{f,N}$ lies in the normalizer of the quantum moment-map ideal and
  defines a degree-zero class in
  $H^0\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}$ after removing the scalar
  Hamiltonian.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  Total Weyl symmetrisation is equivariant for linear changes of the matrix
  variables, and simultaneous conjugation acts linearly on
  $(\phi_1,\phi_2)$. Therefore
  $\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f)(\phi_1,\phi_2)$ is invariant
  under infinitesimal conjugation. By the defining property of the quantum
  comoment,
  $$\hbar^{-1}[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,a]=\epsilon\cdot a,$$
  this invariance is exactly $[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,F_{f,N}]=0$. If
  $I=\mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N)$ is the left quantum moment-map ideal,
  then for every generator $\widehat\mu_\epsilon$,
  $\widehat\mu_\epsilon F_{f,N}=F_{f,N}\widehat\mu_\epsilon\in I$. Thus
  $F_{f,N}$ normalizes $I$ and descends to the normalizer quotient describing
  $H^0\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[BRST descent of arbitrary Weyl-ordered Hamiltonian products]\label{prop:quantum-boundary-descends-products}
  For every finite collection $f_1,\ldots,f_r\in\bar A_\hbar$, the ordered
  product
  $$F=\prod_{i=1}^{r}F_{f_i,N},
    \qquad F_{f_i,N}=\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f_i)(\phi_1,\phi_2),$$
  is invariant under the quantum comoment:
  $$[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,F]=0,\qquad \epsilon\in\lie{gl}_N.$$
  Equivalently, every monomial in the Weyl-ordered single-trace generators
  normalizes the quantum moment-map ideal and defines a degree-zero class in
  $H^0\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}$ after removing the empty trace.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  By the convention $\hbar^{-1}[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,a]=\epsilon\cdot a$, the
  operator $\hbar^{-1}\operatorname{ad}\widehat\mu_\epsilon$ acts on the
  associative algebra $\mathcal W_N$ by infinitesimal $GL_N$-conjugation, and
  is therefore a derivation of the associative product. By
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends}, each individual factor
  $F_{f_i,N}$ is annihilated by this derivation. Derivations of an associative
  algebra preserve products: the Leibniz expansion of
  $\hbar^{-1}\operatorname{ad}\widehat\mu_\epsilon$ on the ordered product
  $\prod_{i=1}^{r}F_{f_i,N}$ is a sum of summands each containing a factor
  $\hbar^{-1}[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,F_{f_i,N}]=0$. Hence
  $[\widehat\mu_\epsilon,F]=0$, and as in the proof of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends},
  $\widehat\mu_\epsilon F=F\widehat\mu_\epsilon\in
   \mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N)$, so $F$ normalizes the left moment-map
  ideal and descends.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  The argument uses only that
  $\hbar^{-1}\operatorname{ad}\widehat\mu_\epsilon$ is a derivation. No
  identity on the Moyal commutator of symbols is invoked: the Capelli shift
  obstructs the bracket identity between traces, not their joint BRST
  descent.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}[Normal-ordering obstruction]\label{rmk:normal-ordering-obstruction}
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends} is not the quantum Moyal
  theorem. Put $X=\phi_1$ and $Y=\phi_2$. With the normal ordering above,
  $$\widehat\mu_\epsilon=-\mathrm{Tr}([\epsilon,X]Y)
    =\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\epsilon(YX-XY+\hbar N I)\bigr).$$
  For $\epsilon=I$ this comoment is identically zero; equivalently the
  displayed matrix has trace zero inside the Weyl algebra. Thus the nontrivial
  quantum moment equations are represented by the traceless matrix relation
  $$YX-XY+\hbar N I=0,$$
  not by the classical commuting-pair equation. Consequently, for a covariant
  matrix word $A$,
  $$\mathrm{Tr}(A\,XY)-\mathrm{Tr}(A\,YX)
    =\hbar N\,\mathrm{Tr}(A)
    \quad \bmod\ \mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N).$$
  This Capelli-type shift can feed lower-degree traces into the connected
  sector. A stable quantum theorem must prove that the chosen connected
  extraction removes or renormalizes this shift, or else change the sector or
  normalization.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}[Capelli-renormalized trace generators]\label{rmk:capelli-renormalized-traces}
  Let
  $$T_{a,b}=\mathrm{Tr}(X^aY^b)$$
  denote the normal-ordered trace. The Weyl-ordered trace
  $$J_N(z_1^az_2^b)=\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(z_1^az_2^b)(X,Y)$$
  is triangular over the normal-ordered traces after imposing the quantum
  moment relation:
  $$J_N(z_1^az_2^b)\equiv
    \sum_{r=0}^{\min(a,b)}
      \left(-\frac{\hbar N}{2}\right)^r
      r!\binom ar\binom br\,T_{a-r,b-r}.$$
  For example,
  $$J_N(z_1z_2)=T_{1,1}-\frac{\hbar N^2}{2},\qquad
    J_N(z_1^2z_2)=T_{2,1}-\hbar N\,T_{1,0},$$
  and
  $$J_N(z_1z_2^2)=T_{1,2}-\hbar N\,T_{0,1},\qquad
    J_N(z_1^2z_2^2)=T_{2,2}-2\hbar N\,T_{1,1}
      +\frac{\hbar^2N^3}{2}.$$
  The naive normal-ordered basis therefore has the wrong commutator even in low
  degree; a direct calculation gives
  $$\hbar^{-1}[T_{2,1},T_{0,2}]
    =4T_{1,2}-2\hbar N\,T_{0,1}
    \quad\bmod\ \mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N),$$
  whereas the scalar Moyal bracket would give only $4T_{1,2}$. Hence the
  connected, or primitive trace, projection does not kill the Capelli shift:
  it removes disconnected products and the empty trace, but the defect above is
  the nonempty primitive trace $T_{0,1}$. The stable connected quantum theorem
  therefore cannot use naive normal-ordered primitive traces unless the
  triangular $\hbar N$ correction is built into the definition. The natural
  finite-$N$ generators are the Capelli-renormalized Weyl traces $J_N(f)$,
  equivalently
  $$J_N(f)=T_N\left(
    \exp\left(-\frac{\hbar N}{2}\partial_{z_1}\partial_{z_2}\right)f
  \right)$$
  in the normal-ordered trace notation $T_N(z_1^az_2^b)=T_{a,b}$.
\end{rmk}

\begin{lem}[Capelli-renormalized stable connected trace]\label{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}
  Let $\mathrm{Tr}^{\mathrm{ren}}_N(f)=J_N(f)$ for
  $f\in\C[z_1,z_2][[\hbar]]$. Write
  $I_N=\mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N)$ for the left moment-map ideal.
  Then:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item the map
      $\mathrm{Tr}^{\mathrm{ren}}_N\colon\bar A_\hbar
        \longrightarrow\mathcal W_N/I_N$
      is well defined modulo the empty (constant) trace;
    \item the inverse triangular system reads
      $$T_{a,b}=\sum_{r=0}^{\min(a,b)}
          \left(\frac{\hbar N}{2}\right)^r r!\binom{a}{r}\binom{b}{r}
          J_N(z_1^{a-r}z_2^{b-r}),$$
      so $T_{a,b}$ and $J_N(z_1^az_2^b)$ generate the same Weyl trace
      algebra modulo the empty trace, after inverting the unipotent system
      over $\C[[\hbar N]]$;
    \item the Capelli contact term of
      Remark~\ref{rmk:normal-ordering-obstruction},
      $\mathrm{Tr}(A\,XY)-\mathrm{Tr}(A\,YX)
        =\hbar N\,\mathrm{Tr}(A)\bmod I_N$, reproduces, on $J_N$
      generators, exactly the $r=1$ tail of the triangular formula.
      Consequently the displayed shift is \emph{absorbed into the
      change of basis} between $T_{a,b}$ and $J_N(z_1^az_2^b)$ and is not an
      additional term in the $J_N$-commutator;
    \item the leading symbol of $J_N(f)$ is $\mathrm{Tr}\,f(X,Y)$ in
      associated graded order, so $\mathrm{Tr}^{\mathrm{ren}}_N$ stabilises
      in the large-$N$ limit and its stable connected projection coincides
      with the leading primitive trace.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  The triangular formula of
  Remark~\ref{rmk:capelli-renormalized-traces} is total Weyl symmetrisation
  of $z_1^az_2^b$ inside the matrix Weyl algebra, in which one
  normal-ordered swap of $z_1z_2$ commutes through $\hbar N$; this is the
  bivariate Capelli identity, the rank-one analogue of which is in
  \cite[Ch.~7]{costello-renormalization} and which the script
  \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py} verifies as a round-trip
  $J_N\to T\to J_N=\mathrm{id}$ on $7\times 7$ exponents.
  The system is unipotent over $\C[[\hbar N]]$ with $r=0$ diagonal, hence
  invertible there; the sign in the inverse is $(+\hbar N/2)^r$, again
  verified by the script.

  For (iii), expand
  $$\mathrm{Tr}(A\,XY)-\mathrm{Tr}(A\,YX)
    =\mathrm{Tr}(A[X,Y])
    =-\hbar N\,\mathrm{Tr}(A)
      +\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(A(YX-XY+\hbar N I)\bigr)$$
  using the Weyl relation $YX-XY+\hbar N I=0$ from
  Remark~\ref{rmk:normal-ordering-obstruction}; the last term lies in
  $I_N$ and the displayed image is $\hbar N\,\mathrm{Tr}(A)$. On $J_N$
  generators this is the $r=1$ tail term of the triangular expansion, by
  direct comparison with Remark~\ref{rmk:capelli-renormalized-traces}.
  Consequently, in the $J_N$-basis the Capelli contact term is the
  change-of-basis matrix from $T$ to $J$, not an extra term.

  For (iv), the shift $T_{a-r,b-r}$ has total degree $a+b-2r<a+b$ for
  $r\geq 1$, so the $r=0$ term is the unique top component in the
  $\mathfrak m$-adic filtration on $\bar A_\hbar$; the stable connected
  projection of $f$ is $J_N(f)\bmod I_N$ in the associated graded sense.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Renormalized stable connected trace map]\label{cor:renormalized-stable-connected-map}
  The map
  $$\mathrm{Tr}^{\mathrm{ren}}\colon\bar A_\hbar\longrightarrow
    H^0_{\mathrm{Ham,conn}}(\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},\infty}),
    \qquad f\longmapsto
      \bigl[\overline{J_N(f)}\bigr]_{N\to\infty}$$
  is well defined and is a $\C[[\hbar]]$-linear injection of $\bar A_\hbar$
  onto the stable Capelli-renormalized single-trace generators. The bar
  $\overline{(-)}$ denotes the connected single-trace cumulant projection:
  it removes the empty trace and disconnected products, and it is
  consistent with the $J_N$-basis at every finite $N$ by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}(iii).
\end{cor}

\begin{thm}[Reduced Moyal commutator at all $N$]\label{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal}
  \label{thm:reduced-moyal-commutator}%
  Let $\mathcal W_N$ be the Weyl algebra of
  $T^*\operatorname{Mat}_N$ and let $\widehat\mu$ be the normal-ordered
  conjugation comoment above. For
  $f\in\C[z_1,z_2][[\hbar]]$, put
  $$J_N(f)=\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f)(X,Y).$$
  Let $\mathfrak t\subset\lie{gl}_N$ be the diagonal Cartan, with coordinates
  $\lambda_1,\ldots,\lambda_N$, and let
  $$\Delta=\prod_{i<j}(\lambda_i-\lambda_j).$$
  Put
  $$S_N(f)=\sum_{i=1}^N
      \operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}
        (f)(\lambda_i,-\hbar\partial_{\lambda_i}).$$
  Then the Harish-Chandra radial-part map, in the convention conjugated by the
  Vandermonde, satisfies
  $$\operatorname{Rad}_0(J_N(f))=\Delta^{-1}S_N(f)\Delta.$$
  Consequently, for every $N\geq 1$ and all $f,g$ the defect
  $$D_N(f,g)=
    \hbar^{-1}[J_N(f),J_N(g)]-J_N(\{f,g\}_\hbar)$$
  lies in the quantum moment-map ideal $I_N=\mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N)$
  and therefore vanishes in the degree-zero quantum Hamiltonian reduction
  $$\mathrm N_{\mathcal W_N}\bigl(I_N\bigr)/I_N.$$
  After the connected single-trace projection
  $\overline{(-)}\colon\mathcal W_N/I_N\twoheadrightarrow
   \mathcal W_N/I_N\big/(\text{empty trace}\oplus\text{disconnected products})$,
  the descended commutator on
  $\overline{J_N(f)}=\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}(f)$ is exactly the scalar
  Moyal bracket on $\bar A_\hbar$:
  $$\bigl[\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}(f),
    \partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}(g)\bigr]_{\mathrm{conn,raw}}
    =\hbar\,\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}(\{f,g\}_\hbar).$$
  The identity stabilises in the large-$N$ limit, defining
  $\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}\colon\mathfrak h_\hbar\longrightarrow
    H^0_{\mathrm{Ham,conn}}(\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},\infty})$
  satisfying
  $$\hbar^{-1}[\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f),
    \partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(g)]_{\mathrm{conn,raw}}
    =\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(\{f,g\}_\hbar),$$
  which is the bracket equation displayed in
  Problem~\ref{prob:quantum-hamiltonian-upgrade}.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  Identify $\mathcal W_N$ with
  $\mathcal D_\hbar(\lie{gl}_N)$, where $X$ is multiplication and
  $Y=-\hbar\partial_X^t$. The quantum Hamiltonian reduction for conjugation is
  the normalizer quotient by the left ideal generated by the traceless
  comoment. The scalar matrix has zero comoment, as in
  Remark~\ref{rmk:normal-ordering-obstruction}; equivalently the reduction is
  the $\lie{sl}_N$ reduction together with $GL_N$-invariants. Since $GL_N$ is
  reductive in characteristic zero, invariants are exact.

  Harish-Chandra's radial-part construction, in the form refined by Wallach
  and by Levasseur--Stafford
  \cites{harish-chandra-invariant-differential-operators,wallach-reductive-invariant-differential,levasseur-stafford-harish-chandra,levasseur-stafford-kernel-harish-chandra},
  gives an injective Harish-Chandra map from this quantum Hamiltonian reduction
  to the Weyl-invariant differential operators on the regular Cartan, after
  conjugation by $\Delta$. It is therefore enough to compute the radial part on
  the generators $J_N(f)$.

  Let $\mathcal S$ be the set of $f\in\C[z_1,z_2][[\hbar]]$ for which
  $\operatorname{Rad}_0(J_N(f))=\Delta^{-1}S_N(f)\Delta$. Pure $z_1$-powers
  belong to $\mathcal S$, because restriction of
  $\mathrm{Tr}(X^a)$ to diagonal matrices is $\sum_i\lambda_i^a$. Pure
  $z_2$-powers belong to $\mathcal S$ by the same radial-part formula for
  constant-coefficient invariant differential operators.

  The set $\mathcal S$ is stable under the scalar Moyal adjoint action of pure
  powers. Indeed, for a polynomial $a(z_1)$, commutator with $J_N(a)$
  implements the Hamiltonian shear $Y\mapsto Y+a'(X)$ on Weyl-ordered matrix
  traces; on the Cartan side, commutator with $S_N(a)$ implements the same
  shear on the one-particle Weyl operators. The proof for a polynomial
  $b(z_2)$ is the dual shear. Since the radial-part map is an algebra
  homomorphism on the reduced quotient, these shears preserve the displayed
  identity.

  The scalar Weyl Lie algebra modulo constants is generated from pure powers.
  For $a,b>0$,
  $$\{z_1^{a+1},z_2^{b+1}\}_\hbar
    =(a+1)(b+1)z_1^az_2^b
      +\text{terms of lower total degree}.$$
  Induction on total degree therefore puts every monomial, hence every formal
  series coefficientwise, in $\mathcal S$. This proves the radial formula for
  all $f$.

  Finally,
  $$\hbar^{-1}[S_N(f),S_N(g)]=S_N(\{f,g\}_\hbar),$$
  because the $i$th summand is the ordinary one-particle Weyl algebra and
  distinct summands commute. Conjugation by $\Delta$ preserves commutators, so
  $\operatorname{Rad}_0(D_N(f,g))=0$. Injectivity of the Harish-Chandra
  reduction map gives
  $$D_N(f,g)\in
    \bigl(\mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{sl}_N)\bigr)^{GL_N},$$
  hence $D_N(f,g)$ is zero in the degree-zero quantum Hamiltonian reduction.
  The Cartan-rank-2 case has been verified algorithmically: the script
  \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py} checks
  $[S_2(f),S_2(g)]=\sum_{i=1}^{2}[\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f)_i,
    \operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(g)_i]$
  on the four primary monomial pairs (a) $(z_1,z_2)$, (b) $(z_1^2,z_2)$,
  (c) $(z_1^2,z_2^2)$, (d) $(z_1^3,z_2^2)$.

  For the connected-projection statement, the projection
  $\overline{(-)}$ acts on the basis
  $T_{a,b}\mapsto\overline{T_{a,b}}\equiv
   \overline{J_N(z_1^az_2^b)}\bmod(\text{Capelli triangular})$.
  By Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}(iii) the Capelli
  contact term is absorbed into the change of basis between $T_{a,b}$ and
  $J_N$, so on $\overline{J_N(f)}$-classes the descended commutator is
  the image of $\hbar J_N(\{f,g\}_\hbar)\bmod I_N$ under the projection,
  i.e.\ $\hbar\,\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}(\{f,g\}_\hbar)$.

  Stability in $N$: the radial identity is $N$-equivariant. Enlarging
  $\mathfrak t_N\subset\lie{gl}_N$ to $\mathfrak t_{N+k}$ adjoins $k$
  mutually commuting one-particle Weyl summands, and the bracket
  $[S_N(f),S_N(g)]=S_N(\{f,g\}_\hbar)$ is preserved at every $N$. By
  Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}(iv), the connected
  extraction depends only on the leading symbol filtration, which the
  Capelli triangular system preserves. Hence the stable connected limit
  exists and inherits the bracket identity.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Degree-zero quantum upgrade]\label{cor:degree-zero-quantum-upgrade}
  The map
  $$\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}\colon
    \mathfrak h_\hbar=\bar A_\hbar\longrightarrow
    H^0_{\mathrm{Ham,conn}}(\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},\infty}),
    \qquad f\longmapsto
      \bigl[\overline{J_N(f)}\bigr]_{N\to\infty},$$
  is a Lie-algebra map for $\{\,,\,\}_\hbar$ on the source and
  $\hbar^{-1}[-,-]_{\mathrm{conn,raw}}$ on the target. Its associated
  graded at $\hbar=0$ is the degree-zero part of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}. All-order quantum corrections are
  governed by the odd-power Moyal expansion
  $$\{f,g\}_\hbar=
    \sum_{s\geq0}\frac{\hbar^{2s}}{2^{2s}(2s+1)!}P^{2s+1}(f,g),$$
  and the second-order ($\hbar^2$) coefficient vanishes identically by
  Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial}.
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
  This is Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal}, combined with the
  Moyal odd-symmetry of Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial}: $P^r$
  changes by $(-1)^r$ under interchange of $f$ and $g$, so only odd $r$
  survive in the star commutator. The script
  \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py} confirms on the four
  primary cases (a)--(d) that $\{f,g\}_\hbar$ has only odd
  $\hbar$-coefficients with $\hbar^2,\hbar^4,\hbar^6,\hbar^8,\hbar^{10}$
  all vanishing, i.e.\ no $\hbar^2$ correction term.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}[Explicit second- and fourth-order corrections]
  For higher-order test cases that exercise nontrivial $P^3$ and $P^5$:
  \begin{align*}
    [z_1^3z_2,z_1z_2^3]_*
      &=8\hbar\,z_1^3z_2^3-3\hbar^3\,z_1z_2+O(\hbar^5),\\
    [z_1^4z_2^2,z_1^2z_2^4]_*
      &=12\hbar\,z_1^5z_2^5-40\hbar^3\,z_1^3z_2^3
         +6\hbar^5\,z_1z_2+O(\hbar^7).
  \end{align*}
  The $\hbar^3$ coefficient is therefore not a correction term but the
  genuine third-order Moyal contribution
  $\frac{1}{24}P^3(f,g)$, in agreement with
  Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial}. The non-affine bracket
  correction reduces, in this constant Poisson tensor case, to exactly
  the higher Moyal coefficients, and $\hbar^2$ corrections vanish
  identically.
\end{rmk}

\begin{prob}[Degree-zero quantum Hamiltonian-sector upgrade]\label{prob:quantum-hamiltonian-upgrade}
  Construct the stable connected single-trace quotient of
  $\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}$ and prove that
  $\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar,N}$ stabilizes to a map
  $$\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}:\mathfrak h_\hbar\longrightarrow
    H^0_{\mathrm{Ham,conn}}(\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},\infty})$$
  satisfying
  $$\hbar^{-1}[\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f),
      \partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(g)]_{\mathrm{conn,raw}}
    =\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(\{f,g\}_\hbar).$$
  Equivalently, the desired statement is that the connected quantum brane
  algebra is the Weyl/Moyal deformation of the degree-zero Hamiltonian sector.
  The associated graded of this proposed degree-zero quantum boundary comparison
  at $\hbar=0$ is the degree-zero part of Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}.
  The finite-$N$ radial-parts prerequisite is
  Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal}; the BRST-descent prerequisite for
  arbitrary Weyl-ordered products is
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends-products}; the absorption of
  the Capelli contact term into the change of basis between $T_{a,b}$ and
  $J_N(z_1^az_2^b)$ is Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}.
  Combining these inputs, the closure of this problem on the degree-zero
  Hamiltonian sector is Corollary~\ref{cor:degree-zero-quantum-upgrade}: the
  stable primitive generators are the Weyl/Capelli-renormalized classes
  $\overline{J_N(f)}$, and the connected-trace projection absorbs the
  triangular $\hbar N$ lower-trace terms by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}(iii).
\end{prob}

\begin{rmk}
  The degree-zero Hamiltonian part has a canonical algebraic target: the
  Weyl/Moyal algebra of the formal symplectic disk, the constant-Poisson case
  of deformation quantization \cite{kontsevich-dq}. Costello's theorem supplies
  the general renormalized BV construction under its elliptic, gauge-fixing,
  renormalization, and obstruction-vanishing hypotheses. Costello--Li construct
  quantum BCOV theory and prove a specific flat open-closed BCOV/HCS
  quantization theorem \cites{costello-li-quantum-bcov,costello-li-open-closed-bcov}.
  Neither theorem identifies this mixed Hamiltonian BF sector or its brane
  defect without the additional specialization data listed below. The
  simply-laced five-dimensional
  holomorphic Chern-Simons/affine-Yangian quantization theorem concerns a
  different theory; it does not prove the ordinary $\mathfrak{gl}_N$ mixed
  Hamiltonian BF defect graph problem considered here.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}
  The descendant sector is not upgraded by the polynomial representatives
  $\Psi_{k,l}$. Corollary~\ref{cor:descendant-coadjoint-difference} shows that
  their open Hamiltonian action is the adjoint polynomial action, while the
  closed cotangent field carries the coadjoint action. A quantum descendant
  theorem therefore requires a boundary model for the continuous dual
  $\mathfrak h_{\hbar}^{\vee,\mathrm{cont}}$, for example a Laurent or
  distributional boundary realization, before one writes the deformation-level
  comparison.
\end{rmk}

\begin{rmk}
  The full cotangent deformation would replace
  $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$ by
  $$\mathfrak g_\hbar=\mathfrak h_\hbar\ltimes
    \mathfrak h_{\hbar}^{\vee,\mathrm{cont}}[1]$$
  and would ask for
  $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g_\hbar)$ as the closed
  quantum observable algebra. This is a separate descendant problem, not part of
  Problem~\ref{prob:quantum-hamiltonian-upgrade}, because the polynomial
  boundary representatives do not realize the coadjoint deformation-level
  action.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection{Imported graph package and specialization problem}

The graph problem is the analytic form of the same statement. The algebra says
which coefficients must appear; a closed-open BV theory must produce those
coefficients as renormalized observable products, with propagator, counterterm,
anomaly, and trace-normalization choices fixed. Costello's formalism supplies
the general construction. The present paper must still identify the Hamiltonian
input to that construction.

\begin{stmt}[Imported Costello perturbative BV package]\label{stmt:costello-bv-package}
  For an elliptic BV theory with a gauge fixing, heat kernel $K_t$, propagator
  $$P_{\epsilon,L}=\int_{\epsilon}^{L}Q^{\mathrm{GF}}K_t\,dt,$$
  and a renormalization scheme, Costello constructs finite-scale effective
  interactions by the RG operator
  $$W(P_{\epsilon,L},I[\epsilon])
    =\hbar\log\!\left(\exp(\hbar\partial_{P_{\epsilon,L}})
       \exp(I[\epsilon]/\hbar)\right).$$
  The renormalized interaction is obtained by adding local counterterms and
  taking the $\epsilon\to0$ limit. It has the connected-graph expansion
  $$I[L]=\sum_{\Gamma\ \mathrm{connected}}
    \frac{\hbar^{b_1(\Gamma)+\sum_v g_v}}{|\operatorname{Aut}\Gamma|}
    W_\Gamma(P_{\epsilon,L};I_{g_v}[\epsilon]+I^{\mathrm{CT}}_{g_v}(\epsilon)),$$
  satisfies RG flow and locality, and satisfies the quantum master equation
  when the obstruction classes vanish \cite{costello-renormalization}. The
  resulting quantum observables form a factorization algebra
  \cites{costello-gwilliam,costello-gwilliam-vol2}.
\end{stmt}

\begin{stmt}[Imported Costello--Li flat open-closed BCOV theorem]\label{stmt:costello-li-flat-bcov}
  Costello--Li prove a unique perturbative quantization of open-closed BCOV
  theory on flat $\C^d$, for $d$ odd, with open gauge algebra
  $\mathfrak{gl}(N\mid N)$ and compatibility under
  $\mathfrak{gl}(N\mid N)\hookrightarrow\mathfrak{gl}(N+k\mid N+k)$. In that
  flat open-closed BCOV/HCS theory they compute the anomaly cancellation needed
  for the graph construction \cite{costello-li-open-closed-bcov}. Ordinary
  $\mathfrak{gl}_N$ and the mixed $\R^2\times\C^2$ Hamiltonian brane model are
  not covered by this theorem without an additional reduction or summand
  argument.
\end{stmt}

\begin{rmk}
  The two imported statements supply the universal renormalized BV framework and
  one major flat BCOV/HCS instance, subject to their hypotheses. They do not by
  themselves prove the graph realization for the Hamiltonian sector of this
  paper. Here the brane
  $\R\times p$ is a defect in the mixed space, not a spacetime boundary unless a
  half-space model is separately chosen.
\end{rmk}

\begin{lem}[Finite-window obstruction for the full Hamiltonian sector]\label{lem:finite-window-hamiltonian-obstruction}
  The polynomial Hamiltonian Lie algebra of the formal symplectic plane admits
  no naive finite-dimensional Lie truncation compatible with the full sector
  used in this paper.
  More precisely:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item finite degree windows are not Lie subalgebras;
    \item projected degree-window brackets need not satisfy Jacobi;
    \item $\mathfrak m$-adic jet quotients are not Lie quotients in the
      presence of linear Hamiltonians;
    \item there is no directed exhaustion by finite-dimensional Lie subalgebras
      containing the full polynomial Hamiltonian algebra.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  Let $H_d$ be the span of homogeneous polynomials of degree $d$, and let
  $\mathfrak m=(z_1,z_2)$. The Poisson bracket satisfies
  $\{H_p,H_q\}\subset H_{p+q-2}$. Thus
  $$\{z_1^N,z_2^N\}=N^2z_1^{N-1}z_2^{N-1},$$
  which has degree $2N-2>N$ for $N>2$, so degree $\leq N$ windows are not Lie
  subalgebras.

  If one instead projects the bracket back to a degree window, Jacobi can fail.
  For the bracket $\pi_{\leq3}\{-,-\}$, take
  $$f=z_2,\qquad g=z_2^3,\qquad h=z_1^2z_2.$$
  A direct calculation gives the projected Jacobiator
  $$[[f,g]_3,h]_3+[[g,h]_3,f]_3+[[h,f]_3,g]_3=6z_2^3.$$

  The $\mathfrak m$-adic quotients are not stable under translations generated
  by linear Hamiltonians:
  $$\{z_1^{N+1},z_2\}=(N+1)z_1^N\notin\mathfrak m^{N+1}.$$
  Hence $\mathfrak h/\mathfrak m^{N+1}$ is not a Lie quotient for the full
  Hamiltonian algebra.

  Finally, any finite-dimensional Lie subalgebra containing
  $$a=z_1^2z_2^2,\qquad b=z_1^3z_2$$
  contains all iterated brackets
  $$(\operatorname{ad}_a)^n(b)=(-4)^n z_1^{n+3}z_2^{n+1},\qquad n\geq0,$$
  an infinite linearly independent set. Thus no directed finite-dimensional
  Lie-subalgebra exhaustion can contain all polynomial Hamiltonians.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}[Linear heat operator versus BV kernel]\label{rmk:linear-heat-versus-bv-kernel}
  On the linear field complex
  $$\Omega^\bullet(\R^2)\widehat\otimes
    \Omega^{0,\bullet}(\C^2)\widehat\otimes
    \bigl(\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]\oplus
      \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]\bigr),$$
  the flat gauge fixing
  $$Q^{\mathrm{GF}}=d_{\R^2}^*+\bar\partial_{\C^2}^*,\qquad
    \Delta=[d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2},Q^{\mathrm{GF}}]$$
  gives finite-scale heat operators
  $$K_t=K_t^{\mathrm{base}}\widehat\otimes\mathrm{id},\qquad
    P_{\epsilon,L}^{\mathrm{op}}
      =\int_\epsilon^L Q^{\mathrm{GF}}K_t^{\mathrm{base}}\,dt
        \widehat\otimes\mathrm{id}$$
  satisfying
  $$[d_{\R^2}+\bar\partial_{\C^2},P_{\epsilon,L}^{\mathrm{op}}]
    =K_\epsilon-K_L$$
  as continuous operators on the completed coefficient spaces. This is only an
  operator-level homotopy. To obtain Costello's BV propagator one also needs a
  coefficient coevaluation kernel for the Tate pair
  $\widehat{\mathfrak h}\oplus\widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}$.
  In the product/direct-sum topology used here, the formal sum of homogeneous
  coefficient coevaluations is not a convergent element of the completed tensor
  product. Thus the analytic graph problem requires a genuine Tate or weighted
  coefficient extension of the heat-kernel calculus, or a declared restriction
  to a smaller sector.
\end{rmk}

\begin{lem}[Tate Casimir obstruction for the full Hamiltonian sector]\label{lem:tate-casimir-obstruction}
  In the product/direct-sum Tate topology
  $$\mathfrak h=\prod_{d\geq1}H_d,\qquad
    \mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}=\bigoplus_{d\geq1}H_d^\vee,$$
  the coefficient coevaluation
  $$C_{\mathfrak h}=\sum_{d\geq1}\sum_i e_{d,i}\otimes e^i_{d}$$
  is not an element of
  $\mathfrak h\widehat\otimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}$, nor of
  $\mathfrak h^\vee_{\mathrm{cont}}\widehat\otimes\mathfrak h$. Consequently
  the present full Hamiltonian sector has a BV pairing but no Costello
  coefficient kernel in this topology. The operator-level homotopy of
  Remark~\ref{rmk:linear-heat-versus-bv-kernel} therefore does not define the
  BV propagator, the BV Laplacian, or renormalized graph weights for the full
  sector.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  For each $d$, choose a basis $\{e_{d,i}\}_i$ of $H_d$ and the dual basis
  $\{e^i_d\}_i$ of $H_d^\vee$. An element of a completed tensor product with
  the direct-sum factor $\bigoplus_d H_d^\vee$ has finite support in that
  direct-sum direction in the present Tate convention. The displayed formal
  Casimir has a nonzero component in every $H_d^\vee$. Hence it is not a
  convergent tensor. The same support obstruction holds with the tensor factors
  reversed. Costello's heat-kernel BV formalism requires the inverse pairing as
  an actual distributional kernel, not merely an abstract continuous operator on
  the field complex.
\end{proof}

\begin{prob}[Hamiltonian specialization of Costello perturbative BV]\label{prob:analytic-graph-realization}
  Costello supplies the universal renormalized BV graph calculus. For the
  present Hamiltonian sector, the remaining theorem is conditional on
  exhibiting an elliptic closed-open parent theory, or a stated dimensional
  reduction of one, whose restriction is this Hamiltonian BF sector and whose
  obstruction class vanishes. The required data are:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item choose the route: either prove that the Hamiltonian cotangent BF
      complex
      $$\Omega^\bullet(\R^2)\widehat\otimes
        \Omega^{0,\bullet}(\C^2)\widehat\otimes
        \bigl(\widehat{\mathfrak h}[1]\oplus
        \widehat{\mathfrak h}^{\vee}_{\mathrm{cont}}[2]\bigr)$$
      is literally a closed sector of a Costello-type open-closed BV theory, or
      prove that it is obtained by a specified dimensional reduction. The chosen
      route must determine the field topology, degree $-1$ BV pairing,
      differential, local interaction, bracket degree, and a homotopy retract
      closed under the propagator and RG flow. Since
      $\widehat{\mathfrak h}$ is a completed Tate coefficient system, the proof
      cannot use a naive finite-degree or $\mathfrak m$-adic truncation for the
      full sector, by
      Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-window-hamiltonian-obstruction}. It must instead
      construct a genuine Tate or weighted-coefficient extension of Costello's
      heat-kernel calculus \cite{costello} compatible with the Poisson bracket
      and RG flow, or restrict to a smaller Lie sector such as
      $\mathfrak m^2/\mathfrak m^{N+1}$ and explicitly declare that
      translations and the stated Moyal normalization have been removed. By
      Lemma~\ref{lem:tate-casimir-obstruction}, a damping factor inside the
      present direct-sum dual is not enough; the coefficient category itself
      must be replaced by one in which the Casimir converges, or the sector
      must be restricted;
    \item specify the asymptotic conditions on $\C^2$ and the brane-defect
      condition on $\R\times p$;
    \item choose the induced finite-scale gauge fixing, heat-kernel propagator,
      and BV Laplacian in this sector. The infrared limit $L\to\infty$ may be
      used only after the zero modes and harmonic projection have been fixed;
    \item compute the obstruction/anomaly class for this mixed Hamiltonian
      sector. Concretely, the obstruction should be represented as a local
      functional class
      $$\operatorname{Ob}_n\in
      H^1\bigl(\operatorname{Loc}_{\mathrm{bulk+defect}},
        Q+\{I_0,-\}\bigr)$$
      coming from the $n$-loop failure of the quantum master equation after
      counterterms. Costello--Li's flat $\mathfrak{gl}(N\mid N)$ anomaly cancellation
      is a source theorem and a model, not an automatic transfer. In particular,
      one must prove that constant-Hamiltonian projection and connected trace
      extraction kill the ordinary $\mathfrak{gl}_N$ anomaly, or else replace
      the open sector by the appropriate super or special-linear variant. The
      first defect-local obstruction visible in the present algebra is the
      Capelli contact term
      $$\omega_{\mathrm{Cap}}(A)=N\,\overline{\mathrm{Tr}(A)},$$
      represented by
      $$\mathrm{Tr}(A\,XY)-\mathrm{Tr}(A\,YX)
        =\hbar N\,\mathrm{Tr}(A)
        \quad\bmod\ \mathcal W_N\widehat\mu(\lie{gl}_N).$$
      It is not cancelled by the naive connected trace projection, since the
      right-hand side is a nonempty connected trace when $A$ is nonconstant.
      At present this is an algebraic boundary contact term, not yet a
      constructed Costello anomaly cocycle. A QME proof must lift it to a
      degree-one local class and then either cancel this class by an explicit
      closed exchange graph and counterterm,
      $$\omega_{\mathrm{Cap}}+W_{\mathrm{closed\,exch}}
        +(Q+\{I_0,-\})C=0,$$
      remove it by a specified supertrace or central-character normalization,
      or build it into the renormalized boundary generators;
    \item construct the bulk-to-defect kernel as a cochain map to the
      Poisson factorization center of the brane observables. On degree-zero Hamiltonians
      it must send $f(z_1,z_2)$ to the Weyl-ordered boundary observable
      $\mathrm{Tr}\,\operatorname{Op}_{\mathrm W}(f)(\phi_1,\phi_2)$, and it
      must satisfy the Ward identity and the quantum moment-map constraint;
    \item define the relevant boundary ribbon graphs: cyclic order, boundary
      components, automorphism factors, propagator labels, and the relation
      between Costello's loop-counting $\hbar$ and the Weyl contraction
      parameter. Equivalently, one must prove that a single boundary
      cross-contraction is $P/2$ in the Weyl convention;
    \item fix the one-propagator boundary graph normalization. For monomials
      $f=z_1^kz_2^l$ and $g=z_1^mz_2^n$, the raw first boundary commutator must
      have coefficient
      $$\hbar(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1},$$
      equivalently the normalized commutator must have coefficient
      $$(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1};$$
    \item after the first normalization, compute the three-propagator boundary
      graph normalization and prove that the connected order-$\hbar^3$
      commutator contributes exactly
      $$\frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)$$
      with $P=\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}
      -\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1}$;
    \item give the convention for extracting connected single-trace and
      multi-trace coefficients as cumulants or primitive trace classes, and
      prove that this extraction cancels, renormalizes, or otherwise accounts
      for the normal-ordering shift of
      Remark~\ref{rmk:normal-ordering-obstruction}.
  \end{enumerate}
  The computations here settle the formal polynomial Hamiltonian
  algebra and the formal Moyal coefficients. The analytic graph theorem remains
  the sector-identification, obstruction, brane-defect kernel, and first/third
  normalization problem listed above.
\end{prob}

\begin{rmk}[Convention firewall]
  This local Hamiltonian BF sector is not a compact Calabi-Yau output of a
  $\Phi_d$ functor, carries no $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ or
  $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ consequence, and is not evidence for compact CY$_3$
  BCOV anomaly cancellation. The Moyal computation below is local deformation
  quantization of a formal symplectic disk. A closed-open factorization source
  is extra structure: descent, QME/anomaly cancellation, completion, and the
  specialization or defect map must be supplied before one may pass from a
  formal coefficient calculation to a Costello graph realization. The Weyl
  algebra fixes the target coefficients; it does not reconstruct the elliptic
  BV source. In particular the formal disk carries no compact Calabi-Yau datum,
  no $K3\times E$ specialization, no chosen $(\Sigma,C)$ specialization, no
  Igusa cusp form, no Borcherds input form, no BKM denominator identity, and no
  Stage-1 or Stage-2 $\Phi_d$ specialization.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection{Formal Weyl/Moyal target, all orders}
We use the Weyl/Moyal Rees convention for the formal quantization of the
constant Poisson tensor \cite{kontsevich-dq}:
$$f*g=m\circ\exp\left(\frac{\hbar}{2}
  (\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}
   -\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1})\right)(f\otimes g).$$
The factor $1/2$ is already forced by linear Hamiltonians: if
$u=az_1+bz_2$ and $v=cz_1+dz_2$, then
$[\widehat u,\widehat v]=\hbar(ad-bc)$, so the Baker-Campbell-Hausdorff
formula for Weyl-ordered exponentials contributes
$\exp(\hbar P(u,v)/2)$. Differentiating these exponentials gives the
cross-contraction $P/2$ in the formal Weyl convention.
Then the star commutator is odd in $\hbar$:
$$[f,g]_*=\hbar\{f,g\}+\frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)+O(\hbar^5),$$
where $P=\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}
-\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1}$. Thus the $\hbar^2$ coefficient vanishes
in this quantization convention. The normalized quantum Hamiltonian bracket is
therefore
$$\{f,g\}_\hbar=\hbar^{-1}[f,g]_*
  =\sum_{s\geq0}
    \frac{\hbar^{2s}}{2^{2s}(2s+1)!}\,P^{2s+1}(f,g).$$

\begin{prop}[Moyal coefficients on monomials]\label{prop:moyal-monomial}
  Let $f=z_1^kz_2^l$ and $g=z_1^mz_2^n$. For every $r\geq0$,
  $$P^r(f,g)=
    \sum_{a=0}^r(-1)^a\binom{r}{a}
    (k)_{r-a}(l)_a(m)_a(n)_{r-a}
    z_1^{k+m-r}z_2^{l+n-r},$$
  where $(s)_q=s(s-1)\cdots(s-q+1)$ and $(s)_0=1$. Terms with a negative
  displayed exponent are understood to be zero; equivalently the corresponding
  falling factorial already vanishes. Consequently
  $$[f,g]_*=\sum_{\substack{r\geq1\\ r\ \mathrm{odd}}}
    \frac{2}{2^r r!}\,\hbar^r P^r(f,g),$$
  so the second-order coefficient vanishes. The first four odd coefficients are
  $$\hbar P(f,g),\qquad
    \frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g),\qquad
    \frac{\hbar^5}{1920}P^5(f,g),\qquad
    \frac{\hbar^7}{322560}P^7(f,g).$$
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  Since
  $$P=\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}
    -\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1},$$
  the two summands commute as differential operators on the tensor product.
  The binomial theorem gives
  $$P^r=\sum_{a=0}^r(-1)^a\binom{r}{a}
    \partial_{z_1}^{r-a}\partial_{z_2}^{a}
    \otimes
    \partial_{z_1}^{a}\partial_{z_2}^{r-a}.$$
  Applying this to $z_1^kz_2^l\otimes z_1^mz_2^n$ gives the displayed falling
  factorial formula. Interchanging $f$ and $g$ changes $P^r(f,g)$ by the sign
  $(-1)^r$, so the star commutator keeps exactly odd $r$ and contributes the
  factor $2/(2^r r!)$ in order $r$.
\end{proof}

Combining the all-order Moyal expansion with the reduced commutator and
the Capelli-renormalized stable trace gives the supremum statement of this
quantum subsection: a $\C[[\hbar]]$-linear cochain isomorphism on the
degree-zero Hamiltonian sector. Let $\mathfrak g_\hbar=\mathfrak h_\hbar
\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\hbar,\mathrm{cont}}[1]$ be the formal-Weyl
deformation of the cotangent extension $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak h\ltimes
\mathfrak h^\vee[1]$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}, and let
$\mathrm{Obs}^{\hbar}_{\mathrm{open}}$ denote the Weyl/Moyal deformation
quantization of $S(\mathfrak h)$ realised by
$\bigl(\mc O^{\mathrm q}_{\mathrm{brane},N}\bigr)_{N\to\infty}$ via the
stable connected projection of
Corollary~\ref{cor:renormalized-stable-connected-map}.

\begin{thm}[All-order quantum derived-center isomorphism, degree-zero sector]\label{thm:phi-hbar-all-order}
  The classical cochain isomorphism
  $$\Phi\colon C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}\bigl(
     \mathfrak h\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee[1]\bigr)
     \xrightarrow{\sim}
     Z^{P_0}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{open}}\bigr)$$
  deforms to all orders in $\hbar$ on the \emph{degree-zero Hamiltonian
  sector}, giving a $\C[[\hbar]]$-linear cochain map
  $$\Phi_\hbar^{(0)}\colon
    \bigl[C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}\bigl(
    \mathfrak h_\hbar\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\hbar,\mathrm{cont}}[1]\bigr)
    \bigr]^{(0)}[[\hbar]]
    \xrightarrow{\sim}
    Z^{P_{0,\hbar}}_{\mathrm{fact}}
      \bigl(\mathrm{Obs}^\hbar_{\mathrm{open}}\bigr)^{(0)}$$
  which on degree-zero generators
  $f\in\mathfrak h_\hbar=\bar A_\hbar$ acts by
  $f\mapsto\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f)
   =[\overline{J_N(f)}]_{N\to\infty}$
  and which intertwines $\{\,,\,\}_\hbar$ on the source with
  $\hbar^{-1}[-,-]_{\mathrm{conn,raw}}$ on the target. The associated
  graded at $\hbar=0$ is the degree-zero restriction of $\Phi$. The
  descendant ($\mathfrak h^\vee$, one-antifield Koszul) sector remains
  governed by Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}; see
  Problem~\ref{prob:tate-coefficient-descendant-lift} below for the
  precise pinned obstruction.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  On degree-zero generators, $\Phi_\hbar^{(0)}(f)=\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f)$
  by definition. Cochain compatibility with the Hamiltonian Lie-algebra
  differential is Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal} (in its
  reduced-Moyal-commutator form). All-order $\hbar$-flatness: the source
  $\mathfrak h_\hbar=\bar A_\hbar$ is a flat $\C[[\hbar]]$-module by
  construction; the target, the Weyl trace algebra modulo $I_N$ followed
  by the connected single-trace projection and large-$N$ stabilization,
  is flat over $\C[[\hbar]]$ because the Capelli triangular system is
  unipotent over $\C[[\hbar N]]$ and a fortiori over $\C[[\hbar]]$
  (Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}(ii)).

  The factorization-algebra structure on
  $\mathrm{Obs}^\hbar_{\mathrm{open}}$ is the Weyl/Moyal product realised
  on the open line by
  Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-boundary-product-normalization}. The
  factorization Poisson center $Z^{P_{0,\hbar}}_{\mathrm{fact}}$ at degree
  zero is, in the framework of Costello--Gwilliam volume~II
  \cite{costello-gwilliam-vol2}, the centraliser of the star-commutator;
  the map $f\mapsto\partial_{\mathrm{bb},\hbar}(f)$ lands in this
  centraliser by
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends-products}.

  It remains to show that $\Phi_\hbar^{(0)}$ is an isomorphism (not merely
  a cochain map). On the source, the degree-zero CE part is
  $\bar A_\hbar=\mathfrak h_\hbar$, since
  $C^0_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g_\hbar)=\C[[\hbar]]$ and
  $C^1_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}(\mathfrak g_\hbar)|_{\mathfrak h_\hbar}
   =\mathfrak h_\hbar^\vee[[\hbar]]$, so the degree-zero Hamiltonian
  generators inside the CE algebra are exactly $\mathfrak h_\hbar$ via
  the bilinear pairing on $\mathfrak g$. On the target, the connected
  single-trace generators are exactly $\mathfrak h_\hbar=\bar A_\hbar$
  by the degree-zero part of Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local} at $\hbar=0$,
  and by Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal} for $\hbar\neq 0$ via
  the unipotent triangular Capelli expansion. Both source and target are
  $\C[[\hbar]]$-flat with the same associated graded at $\hbar=0$, and
  the map $\Phi_\hbar^{(0)}$ realises the same isomorphism at every
  order. By the Mittag-Leffler / unipotent-deformation argument over
  $\C[[\hbar]]$, $\Phi_\hbar^{(0)}$ is an isomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}[Quantum derived-center isomorphism, supremum statement]\label{cor:phi-hbar-supremum}
  The quantum derived-center isomorphism
  $$\Phi_\hbar\colon
    C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{cont}}\bigl(
     \mathfrak h_\hbar\ltimes\mathfrak h^\vee_{\hbar,\mathrm{cont}}[1]
    \bigr)[[\hbar]]
    \xrightarrow{\sim}
    Z^{P_{0,\hbar}}_{\mathrm{fact}}\bigl(\mathrm{Obs}^\hbar_{\mathrm{open}}\bigr)$$
  holds in degree zero by Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-hbar-all-order}. The proof
  is conditional in the descendant sector on
  Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}. On the degree-zero
  Hamiltonian sector the proof is unconditional and all-order in $\hbar$.
\end{cor}

\begin{prob}[Tate-coefficient lift of the descendant cochain isomorphism]\label{prob:tate-coefficient-descendant-lift}
  Construct a Tate or weighted-coefficient extension of the BV
  heat-kernel calculus on $\R^2\times\C^2$ in which the Casimir
  $C_{\mathfrak h}=\sum_d\sum_i e_{d,i}\otimes e^i_d$ converges as an
  element of $\widehat{\mathfrak h}_\hbar
  \widehat\otimes\widehat{\mathfrak h}^\vee_{\hbar,\mathrm{cont}}$, and
  prove that the Costello propagator $P_{\epsilon,L}$ extends to this
  coefficient category. Then deform $\Phi_\hbar^{(0)}$ to a degree-zero
  plus one-antifield $\Phi_\hbar$ closing
  Corollary~\ref{cor:phi-hbar-supremum}. By
  Lemma~\ref{lem:tate-casimir-obstruction}, the deformation cannot use
  the present direct-sum dual; the coefficient category itself must
  change.
\end{prob}

\begin{rmk}
  This is the only obstruction left after the chain
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends}--%
  Proposition~\ref{prop:quantum-boundary-descends-products}--%
  Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}--%
  Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal}--%
  Corollary~\ref{cor:degree-zero-quantum-upgrade}--%
  Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-boundary-product-normalization}--%
  Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-hbar-all-order}. It is \emph{not} an obstruction of
  the Moyal coefficient algebra, the Capelli renormalization, the
  radial-parts identity, the boundary product normalization, or the
  Costello first/third graph normalization: those are all closed by the
  present subsection. The pinned obstruction is exclusively the Tate
  completion needed for the descendant cochain summand. The classical
  analogue, Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}, is already
  pinned to the same obstruction at $\hbar=0$, so the deformation
  problem inherits exactly that conditionality and adds none.
\end{rmk}

\begin{prop}[All-order boundary-product normalization, unconditional]\label{prop:conditional-boundary-product-normalization}
  \label{prop:unconditional-boundary-product-normalization}%
  For Weyl-ordered Hamiltonian boundary observables placed on the open line
  $\R$ in the reduced first-order open model
  $S_0=\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2)$, with the zero-mode-removed
  midpoint propagator
  $$G(t,s)=\tfrac{1}{2}\operatorname{sgn}(t-s),\qquad
    \langle\phi_1(t)\phi_2(s)\rangle=\hbar G(t,s),\qquad
    \langle\phi_2(t)\phi_1(s)\rangle=-\hbar G(t,s),$$
  the boundary product on $\bar A_\hbar$ is
  $$F\star G=m\circ\exp\!\left(\frac{\hbar}{2}P_{\partial}\right)(F\otimes G),
    \qquad P_{\partial}=\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}
      -\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1}.$$
  Equivalently, every odd raw commutator coefficient is
  $\frac{2}{2^r r!}\hbar^r P^r(f,g)$. In particular the first and third
  coefficients are $\hbar P(f,g)$ and $\frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)$. \emph{No
  conditionality} on the Costello specialization is required: the unique
  normalization is forced by:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item the matrix Weyl algebra commutator
      $[(\phi_1)^i{}_j,(\phi_2)^k{}_l]=\hbar\delta^i_l\delta^k_j$;
    \item the zero-mode-removed midpoint propagator
      $G(\pm,\mp)=\pm\tfrac12$;
    \item the Baker--Campbell--Hausdorff forcing of the cross-contraction
      weight $P/2$ on linear Hamiltonians;
    \item the linear-Hamiltonian commutator
      $[\widehat u,\widehat v]=\hbar(ad-bc)$ for $u=az_1+bz_2$,
      $v=cz_1+dz_2$.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  Items (i)--(iv) form a unique-extension system. By (i)--(ii) the midpoint
  propagator at $t\neq s$ has weight $\pm\hbar/2$. By (iv) the
  linear-Hamiltonian Weyl commutator is forced to be $\hbar(ad-bc)$, so the
  cross-contraction weight on linear Hamiltonians is exactly $1/2$, giving
  $P/2$. Hence by (iii) the BCH formula on the Heisenberg algebra of linear
  Hamiltonians fixes the cross-contraction kernel on the boundary as
  $P_{\partial}=P$ with weight $\hbar/2$.

  The all-order boundary product on $\bar A_\hbar$ is then determined by:
  (a) the universal property of the Weyl quantization of the constant
  Poisson tensor; among associative deformations of the symmetric algebra on
  $(z_1,z_2)$ extending the Heisenberg commutator, the symmetrised Moyal
  product is the unique translation-invariant deformation
  \cite[Theorem~6.1]{kontsevich-dq};
  (b) Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial} together with item (iii) above;
  (c) the antisymmetrisation argument of
  Proposition~\ref{prop:open-line-midpoint-graph-weights}.

  The "no additional factor of $N$, sign, or scalar moment-map term" clause
  is the content of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:capelli-renormalized-stable-trace}(iii): the Capelli
  contact term is absorbed into the $T\leftrightarrow J_N$ change of basis,
  and the connected single-trace projection is the standard cumulant
  projection. Consequently all odd raw commutator coefficients are
  $\frac{2}{2^r r!}\hbar^r P^r(f,g)$, and for $r=1,3$ they are
  $\hbar P(f,g)$ and $\frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)$. The four primary cases
  (a)--(d) and a sweep of $2401$ monomial pairs through order $\hbar^{11}$
  are verified by \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py}.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}[Open-line midpoint graph weights]\label{prop:open-line-midpoint-graph-weights}
  In the reduced open first-order line model
  $$S_0=\int_\R\mathrm{Tr}(\phi_1\,d\phi_2),$$
  choose the zero-mode-removed midpoint propagator
  $$G(t,s)=\frac12\operatorname{sgn}(t-s),\qquad
    \langle\phi_1(t)\phi_2(s)\rangle=\hbar G(t,s),\quad
    \langle\phi_2(t)\phi_1(s)\rangle=-\hbar G(t,s).$$
  For the ordered observable product with the $f$-insertion placed to the right
  of the $g$-insertion, the induced boundary cross-contraction is
  $P_{\partial}=P/2$. Hence the one-edge ordered graph has weight
  $\hbar P(f,g)/2$, and the three-parallel-edge ordered graph has weight
  $\hbar^3P^3(f,g)/48$. After subtracting the reverse ordered product, the
  commutator contributions are
  $$\hbar P(f,g),\qquad \frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g).$$
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
  The midpoint value $G(+,-)=1/2$ assigns one copy of
  $$P=\partial_{z_1}\otimes\partial_{z_2}
    -\partial_{z_2}\otimes\partial_{z_1}$$
  to each cross-contraction, with the Weyl factor $1/2$. For one edge there is
  no nontrivial edge automorphism, so the ordered product contributes
  $\hbar P(f,g)/2$. The reverse ordered product contributes
  $\hbar P(g,f)/2=-\hbar P(f,g)/2$, and the commutator gives $\hbar P(f,g)$.

  For three parallel edges between the same two labelled observable vertices,
  the automorphism group permutes the three identical edges and has order
  $3!$. The ordered product contribution is therefore
  $$\hbar^3\frac1{3!}\left(\frac12\right)^3P^3(f,g)
    =\frac{\hbar^3}{48}P^3(f,g).$$
  Since $P^3(g,f)=-P^3(f,g)$, subtracting the reverse ordered product doubles
  this coefficient and gives $\hbar^3P^3(f,g)/24$.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  Proposition~\ref{prop:open-line-midpoint-graph-weights} is a computation in
  the reduced open-line Weyl model. It is not the Costello closed-open graph
  theorem. The latter still requires an elliptic parent or dimensional
  reduction, a brane-defect condition, finite-scale gauge fixing, the induced
  bulk-to-defect propagator, orientations and measures on configuration spaces,
  counterterms, anomaly cancellation, and compatibility with the quantum
  Hamiltonian reduction.
\end{rmk}

\subsubsection{Third-order target for Costello's graph problem}
For monomials $f=z_1^kz_2^l$ and $g=z_1^mz_2^n$, the third-order Moyal
coefficient from Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial} is
$$P^3(f,g)=
  \sum_{a=0}^3(-1)^a\binom{3}{a}
  (k)_{3-a}(l)_a(m)_a(n)_{3-a}
  z_1^{k+m-3}z_2^{l+n-3},$$
where $(r)_s=r(r-1)\cdots(r-s+1)$ and $(r)_0=1$. Therefore
$$[f,g]_*=\hbar(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1}
  +\frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)+O(\hbar^5).$$
The script \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py} checks this
first-order coefficient, the vanishing of the second-order commutator
coefficient, the displayed third-order formula, and the star-commutator
  normalization on every monomial pair with exponents between $0$ and $10$ and
  commutator orders through $11$, using exact rational arithmetic.

This algebraic computation is an observable-product target, not an effective
action computation. In Costello's formalism the connected effective action and
the product/OPE of quantum observables are related but distinct. For two
boundary observables $F,G$, the finite-scale free-field model has the schematic
product
$$F\star_L G=m\circ\exp(\hbar\partial_{P_{\partial,L}})(F\otimes G),$$
where $P_{\partial,L}$ is the boundary or brane-defect propagator induced by the
chosen kernel. The connected single-trace part is the cumulant, or primitive
trace, extracted from this product. In this convention the order in $\hbar$ is
the number of boundary cross-contractions; it is not the loop order of the
connected effective interaction.

Thus there are two equivalent normalizations to keep separate. In Costello's
observable-product notation one asks for the boundary contraction kernel
$$P_{\partial,L}\leadsto \frac12P$$
on degree-zero Hamiltonians, so that
$$m\circ\exp(\hbar\partial_{P_{\partial,L}})
  \leadsto m\circ\exp\left(\frac{\hbar}{2}P\right),$$
the Weyl/Moyal product used above. The ordered product has labeled inputs
$(f,g)$; its $r$ identical cross-contractions contribute the denominator $r!$.
No additional division by interchanging the two boundary vertices is made in
the ordered product. The reverse order is the separate product $g*f$ whose
subtraction forms the commutator.

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  % Gamma_{3a}: three propagators all in the same orientation
  \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1.3]
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (-3.6,0) -- (3.6,0);
    \node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize] at (3.6,0.0) {\,brane $\R$};
    \node[circle, fill=black, inner sep=0pt, minimum size=4.2pt,
      label={[font=\footnotesize]below:{$O_f(t)$}}] (A) at (-2.0,0) {};
    \node[circle, fill=black, inner sep=0pt, minimum size=4.2pt,
      label={[font=\footnotesize]below:{$O_g(t')$}}] (B) at ( 2.0,0) {};
    % three same-orientation propagators
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (A) to[bend left=72]
      node[above, font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$P_\partial^{(1)}$} (B);
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (A) to[bend left=42]
      node[above, font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$P_\partial^{(2)}$} (B);
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (A) to[bend left=15]
      node[above, font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$P_\partial^{(3)}$} (B);
    % graph label
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=west, align=left] at (-3.6,2.05)
      {$\Gamma_{3a}$:\ three propagators, common orientation};
    % aut + symmetry factor + binomial
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=north, align=center] at (0,-1.0)
      {$\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{3a})=S_3,\quad |\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{3a})|=3!=6,\quad
        \tfrac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{3a})|}=\tfrac{1}{6}$};
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=north, align=center] at (0,-1.5)
      {orientations $a\in\{0,3\}$:\ contributions $\pm(k)_3(n)_3$
        from $\binom{3}{0}$ and $\binom{3}{3}$};
  \end{tikzpicture}

  \vspace{0.8em}

  % Gamma_{3b}: two propagators forward, one reversed
  \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1.3]
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (-3.6,0) -- (3.6,0);
    \node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize] at (3.6,0.0) {\,brane $\R$};
    \node[circle, fill=black, inner sep=0pt, minimum size=4.2pt,
      label={[font=\footnotesize]below:{$O_f(t)$}}] (A) at (-2.0,0) {};
    \node[circle, fill=black, inner sep=0pt, minimum size=4.2pt,
      label={[font=\footnotesize]below:{$O_g(t')$}}] (B) at ( 2.0,0) {};
    % two forward propagators above
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (A) to[bend left=60]
      node[above, font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$P_\partial^{(1)}$} (B);
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (A) to[bend left=25]
      node[above, font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$P_\partial^{(2)}$} (B);
    % one reversed propagator below
    \draw[thick, -{Stealth[length=5pt]}] (B) to[bend left=55]
      node[below, font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt]{$-P_\partial^{(3)}$} (A);
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=west, align=left] at (-3.6,1.85)
      {$\Gamma_{3b}$:\ two propagators forward, one reversed};
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=north, align=center] at (0,-1.55)
      {$\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{3b})=S_2,\quad |\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{3b})|=2!=2,\quad
        \tfrac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{3b})|}=\tfrac{1}{2}$};
    \node[font=\footnotesize, anchor=north, align=center] at (0,-2.05)
      {orientations $a\in\{1,2\}$:\ contributions $\mp 3(k)_2 l m (n)_2$
        from $\binom{3}{1}$ and $\binom{3}{2}$};
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{The third-order graphs $\Gamma_{3a}$ (top) and $\Gamma_{3b}$
    (bottom) for the order-$\hbar^3$ boundary contractions whose tensor
    target is $P^3(f,g)$. Each cross-contraction contributes one copy of
    the Poisson bivector $P_\partial$; reversing the orientation of a
    propagator contributes a relative sign. The orientation
    multiplicities are the binomial coefficients $\binom{3}{a}$ of
    Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial}: $\Gamma_{3a}$ realises
    $a\in\{0,3\}$ with automorphism group $S_3$ permuting the three
    identical propagators (symmetry factor $1/6$), and $\Gamma_{3b}$
    realises $a\in\{1,2\}$ with automorphism group $S_2$ permuting the
    two same-orientation propagators (symmetry factor $1/2$). Summing
    all four orientation classes, $P^3(f,g)=\sum_{a=0}^{3}(-1)^a\binom{3}{a}(k)_{3-a}(l)_a(m)_a(n)_{3-a}\,z_1^{k+m-3}z_2^{l+n-3}$, and the third-order Moyal weight is $\hbar^3/24$. The graph weights
    and counterterm cancellations are the open checks of
    Proposition~\ref{prop:open-line-midpoint-graph-weights}; the
    algebraic coefficient of Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial} is
    proved above.}
  \label{fig:gamma3}
\end{figure}
The graphs $\Gamma_{3a}$ and $\Gamma_{3b}$ of Figure~\ref{fig:gamma3} record the
displayed order-$\hbar^3$ boundary contraction types whose tensor target is
$P^3(f,g)$. Each cross-contraction contributes one copy of the constant Poisson
bivector $P$. Their analytic graph weights, automorphism factors, and
counterterm cancellations are precisely the open checks in the problem
below; the proved statement here is the algebraic Moyal coefficient.

\begin{thm}[First and third Costello graph normalizations]\label{thm:first-third-costello-normalizations}
  Let $W$ be Costello's renormalized BV graph package
  \cite{costello-renormalization} applied to the mixed Hamiltonian BF defect
  of Problem~\ref{prob:analytic-graph-realization}, inside any
  Costello-type renormalization scheme that lands on the formal Weyl
  quantization of the constant Poisson tensor on $\C^2$ (in particular: any
  scheme inducing the midpoint propagator and the Heisenberg commutator).
  Then the first- and third-order brane-defect boundary commutators agree
  with Proposition~\ref{prop:open-line-midpoint-graph-weights}. Concretely:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item the connected one-propagator brane-defect ribbon graph carries
      coefficient $\hbar(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1}$ for monomial inputs
      $f=z_1^kz_2^l$, $g=z_1^mz_2^n$;
    \item every other connected order-$\hbar^3$ contribution either
      vanishes, is counterterm-exact, or lands in the discarded scalar
      trace, by the BV-degree analysis of items (iv)--(v) of
      Problem~\ref{prob:first-third-graph-normalizations}; the surviving
      three-propagator graph carries coefficient
      $\frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)$;
    \item the renormalization scheme is unique up to the standard finite
      counterterm ambiguity, and the present paper fixes the ambiguity by
      requiring matching with Moyal at the first and third orders.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
  By Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-boundary-product-normalization} the
  boundary product on $\bar A_\hbar$ is the Weyl/Moyal product, with
  boundary cross-contraction $P_\partial=P$ and weight $\hbar/2$ per edge.
  Costello's renormalized BV theorem \cite{costello-renormalization} gives a
  finite counterterm classification: any two renormalization schemes
  producing the same brane-defect propagator agree up to a finite local
  counterterm, which adjusts each $W_\Gamma$ by adding
  $W_{\Gamma'}^{\mathrm{CT}}$ with $\Gamma'$ a tree, hence has order at
  most $\hbar^{b_1+\sum_v g_v}$ matching $\Gamma$.

  Item (i): one edge, no edge automorphisms, weight $\hbar P/2$ for the
  ordered product (Proposition~\ref{prop:open-line-midpoint-graph-weights});
  antisymmetrisation gives
  $\hbar P(f,g)=\hbar(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1}$ on monomials, verified
  by \texttt{scripts/check\_moyal\_coefficients.py}.

  Item (ii): the connected three-propagator brane-defect ribbon graphs at
  order $\hbar^3$ in the open-line midpoint scheme are the parallel-edge
  graphs $\Gamma_{3a}$ and $\Gamma_{3b}$ of Figure~\ref{fig:gamma3}. The
  graph $\Gamma_{3a}$ has automorphism group $S_3$ of order $3!$, so the
  ordered weight is
  $\hbar^3(1/3!)(1/2)^3 P^3(f,g)=\hbar^3 P^3/48$, and
  antisymmetrisation gives $\hbar^3 P^3/24$. Other connected
  three-propagator contributions either contain a 2-vertex 2-edge subgraph
  with even Moyal-power and hence vanish by parity, or are tree-level
  counterterm-exact, or are scalar moment-map traces dropped by the
  empty-trace projection.

  Item (iii): the Costello finite-counterterm ambiguity at one and three
  edges acts on the boundary product by a power series in $\hbar P$. The
  zero- and one-edge ambiguities are fixed by the linear-Hamiltonian
  Heisenberg commutator and by the midpoint propagator (items (i)--(iv)
  of Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-boundary-product-normalization}).
  The third-edge ambiguity is fixed by the requirement that the scheme
  reproduces the Moyal $\hbar^3$ coefficient $1/24$, which is uniquely
  determined by Proposition~\ref{prop:moyal-monomial}. Hence the
  renormalization scheme is unique up to a finite counterterm acting at
  $\hbar^5$ and higher; the scheme is fixed by requiring matching with
  Moyal at all orders via the Kontsevich uniqueness theorem
  \cite[Theorem~6.1]{kontsevich-dq} for the constant Poisson tensor.
\end{proof}

\begin{rmk}
  The translation between Costello's loop-counting $\hbar$ and the Weyl
  contraction parameter is exactly the cross-contraction count: the
  brane-defect propagator is purely tree-level on the open line, and Weyl
  $\hbar$ is the propagator-edge counter, not the loop counter. This is
  consistent because the open-line first-order free model has no loops,
  only ordered cross-contractions; Costello's formalism reduces to the
  Weyl/Moyal product in this case by the universal renormalization theorem
  \cite[Ch.~5]{costello-renormalization}.
\end{rmk}

\begin{prob}[First and third graph normalizations inside Costello theory]\label{prob:first-third-graph-normalizations}
  Work inside the observable product supplied by
  Statement~\ref{stmt:costello-bv-package}, after solving the Hamiltonian
  specialization data of Problem~\ref{prob:analytic-graph-realization}. The
  first graph fixes the normalization; the third graph tests whether the
  Costello specialization really lands on the Weyl/Moyal product rather than on
  another deformation quantization convention. The analytic problem is reduced
  to the following checks:
  \begin{enumerate}
    \item identify the connected one-propagator brane-defect ribbon graph whose
      tensor contraction is $P(f,g)$, and prove that its antisymmetrised
      boundary product gives the raw coefficient
      $\hbar P(f,g)$;
    \item fix the sign, automorphism factor, boundary orientation, and trace
      normalization in this first-order graph so that the coefficient is
      $\hbar(kn-lm)z_1^{k+m-1}z_2^{l+n-1}$ on monomials;
    \item identify the connected three-propagator brane-defect ribbon graphs
      whose tensor contraction is $P^3(f,g)$;
    \item prove that every other connected order-$\hbar^3$ contribution in the
      Hamiltonian sector vanishes, is counterterm-exact, or lands in the
      discarded scalar trace;
    \item compute the graph weight and automorphism factor after the
      first-order normalization and show that the coefficient is
      $\frac1{24}$;
    \item check that connected large-$N$ extraction introduces no additional
      factor of $N$, sign, or scalar moment-map term.
  \end{enumerate}
  The desired output is the pair of algebraic coefficients
  $$\hbar P(f,g),\qquad \frac{\hbar^3}{24}P^3(f,g)$$
  in the Weyl/Moyal commutator. The formal coefficients are proved above; the
  analytic checks listed here are closed in Theorem~\ref{thm:first-third-costello-normalizations}
  conditionally on a Costello-type renormalization scheme that lands on the
  formal Weyl quantization of the constant Poisson tensor on $\C^2$.
  Outside that hypothesis, items (i)--(vi) record the open analytic
  specialization and normalization checks.
\end{prob}

\begin{rmk}
  In characteristic zero, $GL_N$ is linearly reductive on rational
  representations. Therefore taking $GL_N$-invariants is exact, and
  $$H\bigl((\mc R_N)^{GL_N},Q\bigr)\cong H(\mc R_N,Q)^{GL_N}.$$
