  This justifies the invariant calculation used above. A Chevalley BRST model
  for the quotient stack introduces Lie algebra ghosts as presentation data.
  Linearly reductive exactness identifies derived algebraic invariants with
  ordinary invariants in this setting.
\end{rmk}

\subsection{Further directions}

The formal local Hamiltonian theorem identifies the connected stable open
Hamiltonian trace sector with the PBW special fibre of the Koszul dual closed
Hamiltonian CE algebra, and proves that degree-zero boundary evaluation
preserves the Poisson bracket. The next closed-open step is the cochain-level
Poisson factorization-center lift of Problem~\ref{prob:formal-factorization-center}.

The quantum Weyl/Moyal formulas give the algebraic target for deformation, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-n-reduced-moyal} proves the finite-$N$ reduced
radial-parts identity for Weyl/Capelli generators. The remaining quantum task
is the factorization-level construction of the stable connected quotient and
its compatibility with the closed-open map. The analytic task is to identify
the Costello graph package with this mixed Hamiltonian BF sector, including the
brane-defect kernel, anomaly comparison, connected trace extraction, and the
first/third graph normalizations of
Problem~\ref{prob:analytic-graph-realization}. With different branes the open
observable algebra may become genuinely factorization- or $E_2$-algebraic; the
corresponding Koszul-duality statement is then an $E_2$ version of the local
comparison, not a consequence of the theorem above. The same caveat applies to
the expected $D_0$-brane analogue on $\R^2\times\C^4$.

\appendix
\section{Cross-volume convention contract}\label{app:convention-contract}

This appendix records the convention contract between the present
manuscript and the two cross-repository frontiers cited in
\texttt{CLAUDE.md}: the Vol III CY-to-chiral programme
(\texttt{\textasciitilde/calabi-yau-quantum-groups}) and the Igusa
square-root / BKM Borcherds programme
(\texttt{\textasciitilde/igusa-cusp-form}).

\subsection{Vol III: CY-to-chiral, holomorphic dimension $d$, framing on $S^3$}

The Vol III programme (Pillar $\alpha$, two-stage factorisation
$\Phi_d=\mathrm{Sp}_{\Sigma_{d-1},C}\circ\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d$)
parametrises by $d=\dim_\C X$ where $X$ is the Calabi--Yau target. The
present manuscript works at $d=\dim_\C X = 2$, i.e.\ on the
holomorphic-symplectic surface $\C^2$. \emph{Vol III statements at $d=3$
are not implied by the local theorem here.} The Hamiltonian BF
formulation distinguishes the local model from a CY$_3$ BCOV reduction:
the closed cotangent fields are $\bar A\oplus\bar A^\vee[1]$, not the BCOV
polyvector field on a CY$_3$.

The brane line $\R$ is the worldsheet $\Sigma$ of the local model. It is
\emph{not} the Vol III specialisation curve $C$ entering Pillar $\alpha$
Stage~2. The convention contract: $\Sigma_{\mathrm{here}}=\R$ (open
worldsheet), $C_{\mathrm{Vol III}}$ is a separate compact curve.

The framing on $S^3$ entering the Vol III Hopf-fibration decomposition
and the derived framing obstruction is exterior to the present
formal-local calculation. \emph{No statement here implies a chain-level
$S^3$-framing on $HC^-_3(C)$ for any compact CY$_3$.} The local model is
defined on $\R^2\times\C^2$, not on a sphere.

\paragraph{Transferable.} The Loday--Quillen--Tsygan invocation in the
Hamiltonian-sector discussion above transfers compatibly with Vol III
Pillar $\alpha$ Stage~1 ($\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d$ as a
CY-category-to-factorisation-algebra functor) \emph{only} after the
scalar reduction is applied and only on the degreewise polynomial
generators. The full CY$_3$ transfer requires Vol III's chain-level
$S^3$-framing data and is not implied here.

\paragraph{Non-transferable.} The brane stack $\R\times p$ supports the
U(1) center anomaly $[\bar c]$ of
Theorems~\ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly}--\ref{thm:u1-center-anomaly-open}.
The corresponding object on Vol III is the Mukai-pairing centre of the
K3 Heisenberg ($\dim S_5(\mathrm{Sp}_4(\Z),\nu_{\Delta_5})=1$).
\emph{These are not the same central extension}: $[\bar c]$ is a
2-cocycle on $\bar A=\C[z_1,z_2]/\C$ valued in $\C$, whereas the Mukai
centre is a Heisenberg cocycle on the Mukai lattice
$\widetilde H^*(K3,\Z)$. Comparison requires a separate matched-conventions
proof and is not claimed here.

\subsection{Igusa: Borcherds product, $\Delta_5$, BKM superalgebra}

The Igusa cusp form $\Delta_5$ and its denominator algebra
$\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ are the ur-example of the Borcherds-product
structure that the Vol III $\kappa$-stratification generalises. The
present manuscript's generating-function coefficients (the Moyal
expansion in the closed-open coupling section,
$[f,g]_*=\hbar\{f,g\}+(\hbar^3/24)P^3+\cdots$) are \emph{not} a
Borcherds product. The corresponding formal generating functions are
exponentials of polynomial differential operators, not infinite products
of weight-zero index-one weak Jacobi forms.

\paragraph{Heuristic only.} The slogan ``BCOV is the physics dual to
the generating function's modular and mock-modular structure'' is a
heuristic and convention-checking bridge. \emph{It is not a BKM
consequence of the local Hamiltonian BF / Moyal calculation.} In
particular:
\begin{itemize}
  \item No statement here implies a Borcherds lift of $\phi_{0,1}$.
  \item No statement here implies a denominator identity for
    $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$.
  \item No statement here implies the Gritsenko--Cl\'ery 8-row catalogue
    or the universal $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_N)=c_N(0)/2$ identity.
\end{itemize}
The local Hamiltonian theorem is one of two algebras (open and closed
trace algebras matched by Koszul duality on the formal local disk); the
Borcherds lift is one of automorphic forms on Siegel upper half plane
$\mathfrak H_2$. The repository-level role of this manuscript with respect
to Igusa is \emph{convention checking} ($d=2$ here, $d=3$ on the K3 side
of Vol III, $\dim\mathfrak H_2=3$ on the Igusa side) and not
theorem-grade transfer.

\paragraph{Audit residue.} The Igusa $K3\times E$ frontier explicitly
disclaims any physical identification used in the scalar theorem on the
modular side. Mirror discipline: this manuscript explicitly disclaims
any physical identification with the BKM denominator side of
$\Delta_5$.

\subsection{Status of every cross-volume claim}

\begin{enumerate}
  \item Local theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:main-local}): \emph{honest local
    statement; no transfer claimed}.
  \item LQT invocation in the Hamiltonian-sector discussion:
    \emph{transfer-compatible to Vol III Pillar $\alpha$ Stage~1,
    conventions verified on degreewise polynomial generators, not on
    chain-level framing data}.
  \item BCOV analogy (closed mixed Hamiltonian sector remark):
    \emph{transfer-incompatible to CY$_3$ BCOV; the local model is at
    $d=2$. Flagged}.
  \item Twisted M-theory motivation
    (Conjecture~\ref{conj:twisted-m-theory-universal}): \emph{conjecture
    with named hypotheses; deciding evidence is the BV-cohomology
    vanishing, the Costello locality theorem, and Hamiltonian-reduction
    regularity at $p$, as listed in the conjecture itself}.
  \item Moyal generating function (closed-open coupling section):
    \emph{honest local statement; no BKM transfer}.
  \item U(1) center anomaly (\S\ref{subsec:scalar-anomaly}):
    \emph{theorem on both sides, classical-to-quantum equivalence proved
    (Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-classical-anomaly}); cross-volume
    comparison with Mukai centre on Vol III is open}.
\end{enumerate}
